# ⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️

# Trigger Warning

# ⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️⚠️

**Author's Note & Trigger Warning:**

As I present this work, I must express the immense burden that comes with attempting to resolve the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, the most complex and deeply rooted issues in modern history. This conflict intertwines history, religion, identity, and trauma in ways that defy simple solutions or easy understanding.  
This document discusses themes of civilizational differences, ethnic cleansing, genocide, historical grievances, and religious disputes, which may be distressing to those impacted by the conflict. It also explores solutions that will challenge deeply held religious sensitivities and national narratives. The content presented here critically analyzes complex identities and narratives, inviting dialogue while acknowledging that such discussions may involve confronting uncomfortable and sensitive truths.  
**Viewer discretion is mandatory.**  
As historian Bernard Lewis suggests, those of us who enjoy the freedom to express and explore historical truths have a moral obligation to use that freedom responsibly, especially on behalf of those who cannot. **In times when history is often manipulated to serve propaganda, it is our duty to address these difficult subjects fairly, honestly, and competently—without apologetics or polemic.** This commitment to historical truth is crucial not only for understanding our present but also to preparing for our future.  
The cognitive load of holding and processing the multifaceted nature of this conflict, combined with the emotional challenge of addressing deeply conflicting narratives, has made this the most demanding period in my 30 years of life on this planet. Though this is not necessarily my formal specialty—I'm a Software Engineer by profession—I bring to this task a unique educational trajectory, a combination of hobbies, and a background as a marginalized person who empathizes with both persecuted peoples. I also recognize that, because I don't have a direct personal stake in the conflict, I am able to approach this issue with a level of impartiality that might not be possible for those directly involved. These experiences have equipped me to attempt this immense and complex endeavor.  
My motivation for tackling this issue is multifaceted. First and foremost, I wanted to solve the problem and believed that the Palestinian people need a realistic pathway towards a vision of security and self-determination that the Western world can support while also acknowledging the need for a safe national home for the Jewish people. Both nations suffer from the problem of “All Tactics, No Strategy” when addressing the conflict, and this plan aims to rectify that.  
As an African American, I feel a deep moral obligation to engage in the peace process, honoring the historic solidarity between Jews and African Americans in the struggle for civil rights. Just as Jews fought for our freedom, I believe it is now crucial to support Palestinian liberation while ensuring a secure national home for the Jewish people.  
While there is a strong taboo against outside solutions that might violate self-determination, I have come to believe that external mediation is necessary for the safety and security of both peoples. The perception of this being a foreign-provided solution is correct, but I believe that it is the only viable pathway forward for both nations.  
My intent is to illuminate these complexities in a way that is honest, fair, and aimed at fostering a deeper understanding and, ultimately, a pathway to peace. I carry this burden out of a commitment to truth, justice, and the hope that by confronting these difficult truths, we can contribute to a future where peace is possible.  
This peace plan is deeply indebted to the countless authors whose works have provided the essential historical, cultural, and political context necessary for its development, and I am profoundly grateful to ChatGPT for simultaneously educating me and assisting in transforming my thoughts into language, making the drafting of this document possible. The innovations by OpenAI and the Artificial Intelligence community in Large Language Models have been invaluable. I also want to acknowledge my family, friends, and coworkers for providing the support system crucial to this plan’s creation; their patience and understanding while I covertly dedicated myself to this task have been essential to its completion.  
I would like your understanding and invite you to approach these topics with the spirit of inquiry and commitment to resolution that has driven my efforts. The personal attacks I have endured as a peacemaker are undeniable evidence of the deep-seated malice that festers within the human heart, driven by those who would rather cling to division and hatred than pursue justice and peace.  
Creating this peace plan has become a quasi-messianic duty for me, if only rooted in superficial family history; My name is David Jr., my father’s name is David Sr., and his father is named Solomon—names that resonate powerfully with the lineage of King David. Throughout my life, I’ve been seen as a leader and have always taken on leadership roles whenever available.   
Above all, I challenge any opposing voice to prove your wisdom by presenting a more just solution.

To the best of the author's knowledge, it represents the most comprehensive plan available for addressing the long-standing disputes between Arabs and Jews over the Ancient Land of Canaan.

# Executive Summary {#executive-summary}

The Israeli-Palestinian Conflict, rooted in deep-seated nationalist ambitions and complex historical grievances, demands drastic solutions. This Interim Status Agreement introduces the Canaan Confederation and the Virtuous City of Gaza, a highly creative framework that fosters the conditions necessary for a secure Israel and a viable Palestinian State. Crafted with the strongest commitment to impartiality, this plan seeks to bridge centuries-old divides by suggesting comprehensive frameworks considering the perspectives and rights of all stakeholders involved, offering a holistic approach to resolving the world's most enduring frozen conflict.

**The Virtuous City of Gaza**: The Virtuous City of Gaza will rise from the rubble of conflict, inspired by the rich heritage of the Islamic Golden Age. This city aims to become a global center of learning and cultural exchange, embodying principles of peace, knowledge, and cooperation. Drawing from historical examples like Al-Andalus and the House of Wisdom in Baghdad, the Virtuous City will become the **Pluralistic Crown Jewel** of the Middle East, fostering a new era of Islamic revival and serving as a bridge between the Western and Islamic worlds.

**The Canaan Confederation**: The Canaan Confederation provides the substrate, a Judeo-Arab durable diplomatic vehicle that offers a flexible political framework for resolving the Israeli-Palestinian Conflict. Centered around Israel and the future Palestinian State, the Confederation will facilitate cooperation, economic integration, and regional stability, ensuring long-term peace and security.  This union, validated by David Ben-Gurion’s vision of an Arab federation inclusive of Israel (Teveth, 1985), seeks to spark a new Islamic Golden Age, serving as a bridge linking the prosperity of that era with contemporary modernity.

**A New Global Order for Peace and Security**: The Canaan Confederation introduces a new security architecture in the Middle East, which aims to foster regional stability and, by extension, enhance global security.

## The Strategic Objectives {#the-strategic-objectives}

1. **A Vision for Peace:** Establish a durable ceasefire in the Gaza Strip, setting the stage for re-establishing regional security throughout the Middle East.  
2. **Addressing The Acute Humanitarian Crisis:** Address immediate humanitarian needs in Gaza and set the stage for the region's reconstruction.  
3. **Formalizing a post-war Multinational Force:** Establish a security architecture that provides peacekeeping forces and security guarantees to support both nations and to counter regional threats.  
4. **Ensuring the Reconstruction of the Gaza Strip**: Establish the infrastructure to encourage international cooperation to rebuild the Gaza Strip through the creation of a dedicated Waqf and Modern House of Wisdom.  
5. **Balancing Separation and Reconciliation:** Tactical separation and marginalization of the extremist elements of both nations but counterbalanced by strategic reconciliation strategies through cultural innovation, economic, and educational integration with global partners.  
6. **Ensuring a Final Status Agreement for a Viable Palestinian State**: Creating a time-bounded Process for Establishing a Palestinian State.  
7. **Addressing Jewish-Muslim Relations Directly:** This is the thorniest issue in the conflict, which all previous political solutions have avoided due to diplomatic sensitivities.

## Critical Components {#critical-components}

* **Foundational Acknowledgements for Reconciliation**: Declarations that provide a baseline for reconciliation and address major historical grievances, informed by a thorough historical conflict analysis and deconstruction.  
* **Proposed Actions for Collective Peace and Security:**  
* Establish a renewable Confederation as a diplomatic vehicle for the Israeli-Palestinian Conflict.  
* Implement and maintain a generational Hudna (ceasefire) between major Palestinian factions and Israel.  
* Administer the Gaza Strip and the West Bank under Confederation oversight during reconstruction, leading to Palestinian Statehood.  
* Initiate phased disengagement in conflict zones with Confederation peacekeeping support.  
* A Compact of Free Association Between the Palestinian State and the United States  
* Limited Evacuation of the Gazan population to the West Bank to alleviate excess deaths from the Israel-Hamas War  
* Mandatory Land Lease for Land Occupied Beyond the 1947 Allocations  
* Various proposed Cultural and Religious Innovations to promote reconciliation in the Israeli-Palestinian Conflict, including formalizing the Judeo-Islamic and Abrahamic traditions.

## Challenges and Risks {#challenges-and-risks}

* **Ambition of the Plan**: The scope and novelty of this plan cannot be understated. It requires unprecedented cooperation and commitment between multiple parties with diverse interests.  
* **Security Concerns**: Peacekeeping, disengagement, and land-swap efforts must effectively address potential resistance and strategic depth concerns.  
* **Political opposition and skepticism:** Due to historical conflicts, cynicism and mistrust in both populations will pose significant barriers. Disruption of the current status quo will draw the ire of reactionaries.  
* **Diversity of religious and political interests:** The varied religious and political interests across the spectrum complicate diplomatic efforts.  
* **Overuse of Strategic Ambiguity:** The plan liberally uses strategic ambiguity to provide as broad a vision as possible, which the political process will fill in.  
* **Time:** The political process risks getting bogged down before enough progress can be made towards peace.

## Call to Action {#call-to-action}

The Canaan Confederation and the Virtuous City of Gaza represent a bold vision for peace that requires unprecedented cooperation. Despite numerous efforts, a bold post-war strategy for resolving the Israel-Hamas war remains elusive, highlighting the need for innovative solutions beyond the traditional approaches. This peace plan is designed to synthesize diverse perspectives and needs into a unified vision that respects the situation's complexity and is guided by a commitment to impartiality.  
The Confederation framework proposed here is flexible, allowing adjustments to accommodate all parties involved. However, the new order requires consideration in its ***entirety*** before addressing specific concerns, recognizing that this plan is a compromise in pursuit of peace.  
**Establishing a viable Palestinian State is essential for the *long-term* security and moral integrity of the Jewish People and crucial for regional and global stability.** This plan calls on global leaders, communities, and stakeholders to embrace a bold, comprehensive strategy to address the deep-rooted issues of extremism, ethnic and religious strife, and the existential crises affecting both nations.  
**The future of the Palestinian Nation hinges on the recognition of a *permanent* Israeli presence.** Anyone unable to support this new order should reflect on their reasons and consider the broader implications of continued conflict.  
By rebranding the Gaza Strip as the Virtuous City, we aim to inspire hope and highlight the potential for a new era of peace, learning, and cultural renaissance in the region. This initiative will ensure the Strip is rebuilt and transformed into a symbol of unity and progress for the entire world.  
The international community can advance the Confederation framework before the political elites of the Palestinian and Israeli Nations formally accept it. I urge nations worldwide to endorse this plan to foster a durable peace and ensure the security and prosperity of all involved.

# Confronting the Israeli-Palestinian Conflict {#confronting-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict}

The Israeli-Palestinian conflict demands that the international community undertake decisive actions — akin to ripping out metaphorical stitches — to address not only the conflict itself but also the broader human condition that underpins it. We stand at a critical juncture, with the potential for widespread conflict in the Middle East increasingly apparent.  
Numerous peace plans have attempted to address the core political issues at the heart of the conflict: the right of return for refugees, territorial disputes and settlements, security concerns, the status of Jerusalem, control of religious sites, and the mutual recognition of the Palestinian and Jewish states. However, these efforts have often been constrained by diplomatic sensitivities, lacking the scope necessary to bridge the deep divides of history, religion, language, culture, and ethnicity.  
The attack on October 7th by Hamas and the subsequent destruction of the Gaza Strip underscore the brutal realities of the conflict and highlight the need for radical changes to achieve a stable order of affairs. This plan proposes bold steps that deliberately cross known red lines because true resolution requires confronting the most uncomfortable aspects of our human condition. The differences between the Jewish nation and the largely Arab-Muslim Palestinian nation — religious, ethnic, cultural, and historical — are vast and volatile, and addressing these openly is essential for coexistence.  
The Canaan Confederation, the framework proposed herein, is designed around both the stated and unstated needs and narratives of the Arabs and Jews of the Historical Land of Canaan. It represents a comprehensive attempt to cut through the Gordian Knot of this conflict, aiming for a new era of peace and stability. This plan, including all its opinions, potential factual inaccuracies, and deficiencies, is a personal endeavor to present impartial solutions, and responsibility for them rests solely with the author.

# Disclaimer on the Use of Nations in Geopolitical Analysis: Addressing the Risk of Overgeneralization

# In this analysis, the concept of “nations” is employed as both an abstract model and a recognition of their tangible realities in geopolitical dynamics. While it is necessary to use these constructs to simplify the complex interactions and strategies on a global scale, it is also acknowledged that nations are very real entities with significant impacts on world affairs. The rise of nation-states and nationalism has made the distinctiveness and tangible consequences of national movements particularly evident. A prime example is the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, which clearly demonstrates the profound implications of national identity and sovereignty in shaping geopolitical outcomes. This analysis uses nations as theoretical tools to facilitate discussion, yet also respects their concrete presence and the diverse complexities within them.

# Foundational Acknowledgments for Reconciliation: {#foundational-acknowledgments-for-reconciliation:}

These are the most salient facts necessary for a baseline shared narrative between the two nations and to address the biggest elephants in the room. These cover consistent knowledge gaps I have identified in the national narratives of both nations.  
Some of these acknowledgments can be subject to negotiation and used as leverage as a part of the overall diplomatic process during the Hudna.

## The Israel-Hamas War Is the Result of a Profound Failure of Humanity {#the-israel-hamas-war-is-the-result-of-a-profound-failure-of-humanity}

### 	Humanity Has Failed The Israeli and Palestinian Nations {#humanity-has-failed-the-israeli-and-palestinian-nations}

The world must recognize the Israel-Hamas war as a stark reminder of the failure of humanity to prevent and resolve the Israeli-Palestinian conflict. This war, marked by over 51000 deaths, underscores the critical need for a comprehensive and enduring solution to the conflict.   
In this proposal, we acknowledge the collective trauma endured by both nations and affirm our commitment to a peace process that seeks to end the cycle of violence and address its root causes through dialogue, reconciliation, and mutual respect.  
The goal is to ensure that such tragedies are not repeated and to pave the way for a future where peace and justice prevail for all parties involved.

### The Need for External Meditation {#the-need-for-external-meditation}

**The unchecked self-determination of both nations will inevitably perpetuate internecine conflict, as each pursues its vision of sovereignty at the expense of the other's existence. The severe moral decline of these nations, stemming from the absence of a viable path to peace, necessitates external mediation to restore humanity and prevent further degradation.**  
The Israeli and Palestinian nations, deeply entrenched in a conflict marked by historical grievances, religious animosities, and existential fears, are unlikely to solve the conflict themselves. Both sides have been shaped by narratives that portray the other as an implacable adversary, leading to a deep mistrust that undermines any attempt at genuine reconciliation. The mutual suspicion and the zero-sum nature of their respective nationalisms make it nearly impossible for either side to propose a solution that the other would accept. In this context, any resolution emerging from within these two communities is likely to be viewed with skepticism and hostility, further perpetuating the cycle of violence and despair. As such, an external framework or intervention, untainted by the biases of either side, is necessary to pave the way for a sustainable peace.

## The Israeli-Palestinian Conflict Is a Manifestation of the Limitations of Modern Statecraft and the Nation-State Concept {#the-israeli-palestinian-conflict-is-a-manifestation-of-the-limitations-of-modern-statecraft-and-the-nation-state-concept}

The Israeli-Palestinian conflict is emblematic of the broader challenges associated with the relatively recent concept of the nation-state, which emerged from the Treaty of Westphalia in 1648 following Europe's devastating Thirty Years' War. This treaty marked a turning point by establishing the principles of sovereign statehood that have since guided international relations and territorial integrity.  
The Thirty Years' War itself was largely fueled by the religious tensions between Catholics and Protestants, illustrating how religious identity can become entangled with questions of governance and territorial control. This conflict fundamentally reshaped European political landscapes and introduced the concept of state sovereignty that influenced global diplomacy.  
The birth of modern nation-states has often been accompanied by significant turmoil and violence, a pattern replicated in various regions around the world as empires disintegrated and new national identities were forged:

* **Yugoslavia's breakup** led to ethnic wars in the 1990s.  
* **Rwanda's genocide** in 1994 followed heightened ethnic tensions.  
* **The Partition of British India** in 1947 caused massive displacement and violence.  
* **Sudan and South Sudan** have been engulfed by conflicts post-partition.  
* **Balkans**: Post-Ottoman ethnic conflicts, notably the Kosovo War.  
* **Israel's creation** in 1948 triggered ongoing conflict and displacement.  
* **African decolonization** led to conflicts like the Nigerian Civil War.

Specific to the Israeli-Palestinian Conflict, the collapse of the Ottoman Empire and the dissolution of the millet system, which had allowed religious communities to govern themselves, led to significant upheaval. The loss of this system contributed to tensions and conflicts in the Balkans and the Middle East, including the Armenian and Assyrian genocides, as new nation-states struggled to define citizenship and belonging in newly homogeneous terms.  
These historical events underscore the inherent challenges and often violent nature of creating and maintaining nation-states within rigidly defined borders, especially in regions characterized by diverse populations with complex historical and cultural backgrounds. The Israeli-Palestinian conflict, therefore, is not merely a regional issue but a part of a broader history of nation-state formation and the struggle for self-determination in the post-imperial world.

## Hamas Has Destroyed Israel's Sense of Security {#hamas-has-destroyed-israel's-sense-of-security}

### Israel's Strategic Vulnerability {#israel's-strategic-vulnerability}

Despite being the most powerful nation in the Middle East with unrivaled technological, economic, and military strengths—a testament to the intellectual capital and resilience of the Jewish people—the catastrophic events of October 7th have underscored a profound failure.  
**Israel has not been able to ensure a safe national home or protect its Jewish population from antisemitism effectively. These events have shattered the perceived security within the State of Israel, making it currently the most dangerous place for Jews to reside.** This sense of vulnerability extends to the Jewish people worldwide.

### A Symbolic Interpretation of October 7th {#a-symbolic-interpretation-of-october-7th}

The events of October 7th, and the subsequent destruction of Gaza, can be interpreted, at least metaphorically and symbolically, as Hamas executing on the hadith prophesying a final confrontation with the Jews, which is outlined in Article 7 of their charter. This hadith, found in Sahih Muslim, Book 41, Hadith 6985, speaks of a time when rocks and trees will call out to Muslims to come and kill Jews hiding behind them. While it is a matter of interpretation whether this specific prophecy has been fulfilled, the attack and its aftermath have undeniably contributed to a heightened sense of impending crisis and a potential shift in the broader eschatological landscape.

### A Call for Fundamental Change {#a-call-for-fundamental-change}

This situation is a disaster not only for Israel but for the entire Middle East, exemplified by the significant destruction and humanitarian crisis suffered by the Palestinians of the Gaza Strip and the regional spill over in Lebanon, Syria, Yemen, Iraq, and Iran. The Israeli-Palestinian Conflict has re-emerged as mankind’s most pressing geopolitical crisis, destabilizing the region and demanding a reassessment of the status quo.  
A fundamental change in the Middle East and the broader human condition is necessary. Drastic actions must be taken. National consciousness must evolve, with all parties striving to abandon the mentalities that have led to prolonged conflict in the Holy Land.

## Palestinians Have Historically Been Dehumanized, With Their Security Needs Systematically Deprioritized {#palestinians-have-historically-been-dehumanized,-with-their-security-needs-systematically-deprioritized}

### Historical Roots of Insecurity and the Balfour Declaration {#historical-roots-of-insecurity-and-the-balfour-declaration}

The historical insecurity of the Palestinian people stretches back well before the pivotal events of 1948\. Beginning in the late 19th century, the rise of the Zionist movement and the onset of Jewish immigration under the weakening Ottoman Empire introduced significant changes to the demographic and cultural landscape of Palestine. This period marked the initial seeds of conflict, as the land began to witness the establishment of new communities that would eventually challenge the existing social and political order.  
The Balfour Declaration of 1917, which supported the establishment of a 'national home for the Jewish people' in Palestine, significantly heightened these tensions. The subsequent British Mandate period saw accelerated Jewish immigration and land purchases, facilitated at times by British policies. This influx was perceived as a direct threat to the Arab way of life and their ancestral lands, leading to increased friction and several violent confrontations, including the major Arab revolts from 1921 to the extensive uprising between 1936 and 1939\.

### Consequences of Demographic Shifts {#consequences-of-demographic-shifts}

By the time of the UN's partition plan in 1947, the demographic shifts and the continued establishment of Jewish settlements had deeply entrenched a sense of insecurity among the Palestinian Arabs, culminating in the mass displacements and conflicts of 1948, known as the Nakba. The enduring legacy of these early tensions and the subsequent conflicts underpin the complex and persistent insecurity that affects the Palestinian community to this day.

### Colonial Narratives and Dehumanization {#colonial-narratives-and-dehumanization}

**The pattern of rhetoric and behavior observed in early Zionist statements and policies reflects a broader process of dehumanization that has been critically impactful in the Israeli-Palestinian conflict.**   
This dehumanization is evident in the denial of Palestinian identity and existence, as exemplified by statements like Golda Meir’s assertion that '*there were no such thing as Palestinians.*' Such rhetoric served to justify the displacement, dispossession, and marginalization of Palestinians, framing them as obstacles rather than as rightful inhabitants with legitimate claims to the land.  
While the Palestinian national consciousness was formally articulated by the PLO, the sense of a distinct Palestinian identity had been developing over decades. This identity evolved particularly in response to the political and social changes during the Ottoman and British Mandate periods, manifesting strongly in opposition to Zionist settlement and British colonial policies, even before the PLO's formal declaration.  
Furthermore, in *The Jewish State*, Theodor Herzl's depiction of the Jewish state as an '*outpost against barbarism*' reflects colonial attitudes that portrayed the indigenous population as backward and in need of civilization. This dehumanization was further reinforced by the pervasive rhetoric that Palestine was '*a land without a people for a people without a land*,' which ignored the existing Arab population and their historical connection to the land.  
By depicting the land as empty or uncultivated, Zionist rhetoric implied that the incoming Jewish settlers were reclaiming and revitalizing a supposedly deserted land, further marginalizing the indigenous population. This portrayal has been instrumental in shaping international perceptions and policy approaches to the region, often at the expense of Palestinian rights and visibility. This has had profound effects on the conflict, perpetuating cycles of violence and making reconciliation more difficult. Addressing this legacy of dehumanization is essential for understanding the roots of the conflict and for moving towards a future where the rights and humanity of all parties are recognized and respected.

## Israeli and Palestinian Security Needs Are Intrinsically Linked {#israeli-and-palestinian-security-needs-are-intrinsically-linked}

The security and well-being of both nations are intrinsically linked—two sides of the same coin. Without addressing Palestinian grievances and security concerns, Israel's security remains precarious, particularly given the unstable geopolitical environment in the region, including the influence of external actors like Iran in neighboring states.

## Israelis and Palestinians are Loose Descendants of Canaanites {#israelis-and-palestinians-are-loose-descendants-of-canaanites}

### 	This is a Civil War Between Nations of Quasi-Canaanite Ancestry {#this-is-a-civil-war-between-nations-of-quasi-canaanite-ancestry}

Both Israelis and Palestinians have deep historical connections to the Land of Canaan and can be considered to have quasi-Canaanite ancestry (Gassel, 2022).   
The Israelites, originally part of the Canaanite peoples, formed their own distinct civilization over time. The Jewish people, emerging from Israelite origins, have historically maintained a strong sense of community characterized by endogamous practices and limited proselytization. Genetic studies indicate that Jewish populations share common paternal ancestry, reflected in Y-chromosome haplotypes, while the maternal lines, as indicated by mitochondrial DNA, are more diverse. This diversity largely stems from Jewish men marrying and converting non-Jewish women, which contributed to the genetic mixture within the Jewish community . This has preserved a unique genetic and cultural identity linked to both their Israelite ancestry and the diverse lands they have inhabited. Over centuries, widespread anti-Semitism and systemic persecution culminated in the Holocaust, providing overwhelming push factors that drove the need for a secure homeland, which Zionism aimed to establish in their ancestral land.  
Similarly, the Palestinians have evolved from what can be considered Arabized Canaanites, integrating various cultural and genetic influences over the centuries. Today, both groups maintain a profound and fundamental attachment to this shared land, underscoring their long-standing ties to it.  
Despite the differences that have shaped their respective histories and identities, Israelis and Palestinians are, in many ways, distant cousins linked by a common, distant Canaanite heritage. Acknowledging this shared past can serve as a foundation for dialogue, helping both communities explore their complex relationship and the possibilities for future cooperation based on mutual respect and shared historical ties.

## The Acknowledgment of Genocidal Realities and the Necessity of Hostile Population Disengagement and Repartitioning with International Assistance {#the-acknowledgment-of-genocidal-realities-and-the-necessity-of-hostile-population-disengagement-and-repartitioning-with-international-assistance}

### 	Acknowledgment of the Imprecision of the word Genocide {#acknowledgment-of-the-imprecision-of-the-word-genocide}

The term 'genocide' carries a weighty and specific legal definition, rooted in the intent to destroy, in whole or in part, a particular group. However, in the context of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, the line between intent and outcome is often blurred by the overwhelming historical, political, and social complexities at play. While I use the term 'genocidal' in this discussion to describe the severe and devastating impacts of actions taken by either nation, it is important to acknowledge the imprecision inherent in this usage, as well as the asymmetry of power between the Israeli and Palestinian nations, which risks accusations of false equivalence. The conflict's deeply entrenched nature, characterized by mutual existential threats and profound historical grievances, makes it difficult to neatly categorize actions under strict legal definitions. Instead, this discussion aims to highlight the devastating human cost and the cyclical violence that has come to define this conflict, recognizing that while the term 'genocidal' may be imprecise, it captures the extreme levels of violence and destruction that have shaped the lives of Israelis and Palestinians alike.  
The following discussion presents a personal perspective on the question of genocide in the Israeli-Palestinian conflict. It does not seek to place blame solely on any party but recognizes the complex realities that have driven the violence. The actions of both Israelis and Palestinians have been shaped by fear, survival, and the pursuit of security, often leading to severe consequences for civilians.  
The discussions and assertions within this document regarding accusations of genocide are provided as a personal interpretation by the author to shed light on the underlying biases responsible for these proposed actions. Comprehensive analyses and determinations on such matters are currently being litigated by experienced experts in International Humanitarian Law and are out of the scope of this peace plan.	  
In discussing the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, particularly the Israeli military tactics, it is crucial to address the complex issue of intent. While genocide is legally defined by the intent to destroy, in whole or in part, a particular group, this intent is often challenging to prove conclusively in such a politically charged context. However, the outcomes of certain actions, such as the high civilian death tolls and extensive destruction, can mirror the effects of genocide. In this context, the term 'de facto genocidal' is used to describe actions that, while possibly lacking clear genocidal intent, result in consequences that are effectively genocidal by their outcomes. This perspective acknowledges the murkiness of causality while emphasizing the undeniable human cost and destruction that occurs, which is apparent to all observers.

### The Israeli and Palestinian Nations Are Genocidal Towards Each Other {#the-israeli-and-palestinian-nations-are-genocidal-towards-each-other}

The Israeli-Palestinian conflict represents a profound existential struggle, where both nations perceive the stakes as nothing less than their survival and right to self-determination. This 100+ year-old ethno-religious and nationalist conflict leaves little room for compromise, with the lines between combatants and civilians blurred due to the pervasive impact on everyday life. Despite its relatively lower intensity compared to other global conflicts, the totality of this conflict is immense, affecting all aspects of Israeli and Palestinian societies.  
The genocidal massacre of October 7th and the subsequent planetary devastation of the Gaza Strip serve as stark evidence of the genocidal nature of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, highlighting the extreme levels of violence and destruction that underscore the existential stakes perceived by both sides.  
**The self-determination efforts of both Israelis and Palestinians are fundamentally opposed and zero sum, leading to a cycle of genocidal violence.** Each nation’s drive for sovereignty and identity is perceived as inherently incompatible with the other’s existence, fueling a conflict where both sides view the eradication or suppression of the other as necessary for their own survival.  
**The situation is further complicated by the diminishing support for a two-state solution, which has historically been seen as a viable pathway to peace.** With decreasing faith in the feasibility of coexistence, the conflict increasingly appears as a zero-sum game, exacerbating the potential for extreme violence and making the prospects for peace ever more elusive.

### Israeli Military Tactics Are At Least De Facto Genocidal in Context {#israeli-military-tactics-are-at-least-de-facto-genocidal-in-context}

The high civilian death toll in the Israeli-Hamas war is at least partly due to the tactics employed by Hamas, which involve embedding military operations within civilian areas. However, Israel’s response to this challenge, characterized by the overwhelming use of force and targeting of infrastructure, also results in extensive civilian casualties.  
**This dynamic places the Israeli state in a position where its efforts to combat Palestinian militants, which many government’s in the Western world have justified under the nation’s right to self-defense, have led to actions that are at least de facto genocidal, especially given the history of persistent dehumanization of the Palestinian people by the Zionist movement and the persistent policies of occupation by the State of Israel.**  
**An unjust government cannot wage a just war; members of the ultranationalist coalition led by Bibi Netanyahu, including Kahanist figures like Itamar Ben-Gvir and Bezalel Smotrich, have consistently and openly displayed unrepentant genocidal intent towards the Palestinian people. These members exemplify the moral decline of the Israeli state, and their influence on setting the overall war strategy is undeniable, given their repeated threats to collapse the government during a time of war.**  
**The Israel-Hamas war and the destruction of the Gaza Strip exemplify the final conclusion of th e Dahiya Doctrine, a military strategy employed by the Israeli Defense Forces (IDF) that advocates for the use of overwhelming and disproportionate force to deter and punish hostile entities like Hamas.**  
This doctrine, which involves targeting civilian infrastructure to create a powerful deterrent and inflict psychological damage, is evident in the extensive destruction seen in Gaza during the conflict. The scale of destruction, tolerance for a high civilian death toll, and deliberate targeting of essential infrastructure can easily be interpreted as genocidal, raising serious questions about the potential for these actions to constitute genocide.  
The extensive deployment of the Mark 84 bomb, an extremely heavy ordnance, in densely populated areas of the Gaza Strip can be viewed as indicative of genocidal force, demonstrating a disregard for the disproportionate impact on civilian populations. (Ismay, 2024\)  
The use of AI-driven targeting systems like "Hasbora" and "Gospel" by the Israeli military, especially following the October 7th genocidal massacre, underscores an intensification of the Israeli state's approach towards the Palestinians. These systems, designed to rapidly identify and propose military targets, were deployed early on in the war with very loose rules of engagement, leading to a significant escalation in the scale and intensity of attacks. This heightened use of technology in warfare, particularly when coupled with the state's high tolerance for the civilian casualties resulting from such operations, can be seen as further evidence of the Israeli state's genocidal actions towards the Palestinian population.  
The term "mowing the lawn" starkly illustrates the disturbing mindset behind recurring military tactics employed by the Israeli Defense Forces (IDF) in Gaza. This phrase, ostensibly trivializing and routine, suggests a cyclical, systematic approach to the suppression of perceived threats, implying that elements of the Palestinian population, like overgrown grass, must periodically be cut down. While it is acknowledged that the IDF is combating militants who are intent on the destruction of Israel, the casual use of such language in military and political discourse not only dehumanizes the Palestinians but also suggests a normalization of continuous violence as a maintenance strategy. This dehumanization is instrumental in justifying extreme measures, which can be interpreted as aligning with genocidal tactics by reducing the gravity and humanity of the actions taken.  
The practice of home demolitions by the Israeli Defense Forces (IDF) stands as a continuation of tactics employed since the Nakba, aimed at forcibly displacing Palestinian communities. This policy, often justified by Israel as a means of deterrence or security measures, systematically targets Palestinian structures under various pretexts such as lack of building permits in areas where such permits are notoriously difficult to obtain or as retaliation for attacks. These actions not only lead to immediate and tangible suffering but also serve to erode the foundation of Palestinian societal and cultural continuity. By perpetuating instability and transience among Palestinian populations, these demolitions can be interpreted as part of a genocidal strategy, aiming to undermine the viability of the Palestinian nation itself.  
**Finally, the destruction of Hamas as the governing backbone of the Gaza Strip is inevitably genocidal due to the deep embedding of Hamas in the fabric of Gazan society.** As an organic Palestinian resistance movement that emerged in response to the Zionist project, Hamas is not only a militant organization but also a crucial part of the social, political, and economic structures within Gaza. This integration means that efforts to dismantle Hamas necessarily involve widespread devastation across the civilian population, as the lines between combatants and non-combatants are blurred. **The destruction of Hamas, therefore, implied the destruction of the very community it governs, leading to consequences that can be interpreted as genocidal in nature.**  
The perception of existential threats has historically been a precursor to genocide, as seen in various global instances where states or groups, fearing for their survival, have resorted to extreme measures against those they perceive as threats. In the context of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, Israel views itself as being in an existential battle, particularly given the threats from groups like Hamas, which is a manifestation of Islamic Antisemitism within the broader Palestinian National Movement. Hamas’s founding charter not only seeks the elimination of Israel but also contains deeply antisemitic rhetoric, framing Jews as inherent adversaries of Islam. This dangerous interplay of existential fear and ideological extremism has driven Israel to adopt actions thatv   are genocidal in nature, as they aim to neutralize what is perceived as a mortal threat.  
History has shown that such mixtures of perceived existential threats and dehumanizing beliefs have led to catastrophic outcomes, as evidenced by the Holocaust, where Nazi Germany, perceiving Jews as an existential threat, orchestrated the systematic extermination of six million Jews; the Armenian Genocide, where the Ottoman Empire, fearing Armenian collaboration with enemies, led to the mass killing and forced deportation of Armenians; and the Rwandan Genocide, where Hutu extremists, perceiving Tutsis as a threat to their power, committed mass atrocities. The fear of annihilation, when coupled with dehumanizing ideologies, has historically set the stage for genocidal actions, and similar dynamics are at play in the Israeli-Palestinian conflict today.

### Hamas as the Spiritual Successor To Amin al-Husseini: A legacy of Genocidal Intent {#hamas-as-the-spiritual-successor-to-amin-al-husseini:-a-legacy-of-genocidal-intent}

The attacks carried out by Hamas and its allied militias on October 7th were strategically designed to achieve multiple goals: drawing international attention to the Palestinian cause, inciting severe Israeli retaliation, and perpetuating a state of endless conflict. These actions reveal a deeply ingrained genocidal intent within Hamas, aimed not solely at resisting Israeli occupation but at fostering a cycle of violence that continuously escalates suffering for both communities.  
Hamas’s history of suicide bombings and rocket attacks targeting Israeli civilians underscores a tactical approach that seeks to instill fear and provoke retaliatory measures that further justify their ongoing resistance. This cycle of violence, often indiscriminate and aimed at causing maximum civilian casualties, can be interpreted as having genocidal overtones as it perpetuates an environment of perpetual conflict and suffering, undermining efforts towards peaceful coexistence.  
Moreover, the psychological impact of this terror on Israeli society is profound, contributing to the dehumanization of Palestinians in Israeli public perception, which in turn fuels the conflict. The inevitable Israeli military responses to these attacks have led to high civilian casualties, significant infrastructural damage, and deepening humanitarian crises in Gaza. These outcomes serve Hamas’s narrative by depicting the Palestinian population as under siege, thereby galvanizing support for their cause both locally and internationally.  
Furthermore, Hamas’s use of human shields and civilian infrastructure—schools, mosques, and hospitals—as operational bases exploits the legal and ethical dilemmas faced by the Israeli military. This “lawfare” strategy is ineffective in deterring Israeli actions but successful in increasing Palestinian civilian casualties, which Hamas uses to garner international sympathy and intensify global anti-Israel sentiment. This approach not only perpetuates the conflict but also intensifies the cycle of dehumanization and heightens the genocidal atmosphere of the conflict.  
Organizationally a descendant of the Egyptian Muslim Brotherhood and ideologically a spiritual successor to Grand Mufti Amin al-Husseini, Hamas epitomizes the core of Palestinian nationalism. This ideological lineage, grounded in the use of Islamic rhetoric to frame their opposition to Zionism, poses significant existential threats to Jewish self-determination in historic Palestine.  
By continuing the legacy of Amin al-Husseini, Hamas merges deep-seated religious and nationalist fervor into a unified stance against the existence of Israel, reinforcing its position at the heart of Palestinian nationalism.

### The Land of Canaan Must Be Repartitioned, The Populations Disengaged, With Buffer Zones Established {#the-land-of-canaan-must-be-repartitioned,-the-populations-disengaged,-with-buffer-zones-established}

Militancy and moral decline has become embedded within both populations, shaping the socio-political landscape and daily life in profound ways. **This plan explicitly recognizes the tragic and genocidal nature of this relationship and the necessity for a radical, yet deeply unpopular, remedy: the disengagement of these populations from one another, along with the necessity of repartitioning the Land of Canaan.**  
International assistance will be necessary to disengage the most hostile elements of the population from each other, ensuring they fulfill their role in stabilizing the region and preventing further conflict. The historical precedence of establishing demilitarized zones (DMZs), buffer zones, safe zones, and safe evacuation corridors in conflicts such as the Korean Peninsula, Cyprus, Bosnia, the Sinai Peninsula, the Golan Heights, and during the breakup of Yugoslavia highlights their effectiveness in reducing direct confrontations and facilitating peace processes.  
Similar measures will be crucial in the Canaan Confederation implementation. The Canaan Confederation members will negotiate the establishment and maintenance of these zones, ensuring they serve as neutral areas that prevent violence and allow for humanitarian assistance to reach those in need.  
This measure, while fraught with challenges and further displacement, is a necessary step to mitigate the ongoing cycle of violence and ethnic conflict. **The separation of these communities may create new problems for future generations, but it is essential to prevent further bloodshed and to lay the groundwork for eventual reconciliation.** We acknowledge the pain and hardship this decision will cause, yet believe it is a crucial step toward a future where both peoples can coexist in peace, even if initially apart.

### Israeli Minority Citizenship Must Not be Stripped {#israeli-minority-citizenship-must-not-be-stripped}

**This peace plan unequivocally advocates that no individual’s citizenship will be stripped during the process of population disengagement or land swaps. The protection of citizenship rights is paramount, as the presence and inclusion of minorities within Israel will be crucial for future reconciliation efforts.**   
**These minority communities serve as bridges between the Israeli and Palestinian populations, embodying the possibility of coexistence and mutual respect. Their role in fostering dialogue and understanding is indispensable, and their citizenship must remain intact to pave the way for a peaceful and integrated future. While Israel may inevitably attempt to challenge this principle, the plan allows for compromises in other aspects to ensure that citizenship rights are upheld and remain non-negotiable.**

### Bilateral Trade Must be Maintained to the greatest extent possible {#bilateral-trade-must-be-maintained-to-the-greatest-extent-possible}

The disruption of bilateral trade and the movement of workers between Israeli and Palestinian territories must be minimized for security purposes during the redrawing of borders and disengagement under the Canaan Confederation, especially given that the two economies are still deeply intertwined. To ensure continuity and stability, the Paris Protocol must be maintained to the greatest extent possible until the Canaan Confederation can develop a suitable replacement. Maintaining stable economic relations is essential to prevent economic hardship that could exacerbate tensions and undermine the peace process. Ensuring the continued flow of goods, services, and labor across the new borders will help sustain livelihoods, reduce the potential for unrest, and support the broader goals of stability and reconciliation within the region.

## The Collective Shitlist Is Countably Infinite[^2] {#the-collective-shitlist-is-countably-infinite}

In times of crisis, the quest for moral clarity is both natural and necessary. Yet, this conflict exists on a fundamental fault line of human civilization, complicating any straightforward attribution of blame. Participants in this conflict perpetually exchange a vast array of grievances, forming a complex web of accusations that seems virtually endless. Recognizing that the combined grievances of every party involved form an 'infinite list' can help us understand why placing the blame solely on one side is challenging and unproductive. Such recognition calls for a more nuanced approach that seeks understanding and reconciliation rather than perpetuating blame.  
In addition, the creation of this plan is partial evidence of the combination of educational and technological resources needed to create an innovative political framework for the Israeli-Palestinian conflict only recently. It is crucial to recognize the difficulty of this frozen conflict when considering new approaches to the conflict.

## The Western World Must Fully Recognize the Palestinian Catastrophe {#the-western-world-must-fully-recognize-the-palestinian-catastrophe}

### Historical Context and Colonial Influence {#historical-context-and-colonial-influence}

In the shadow of a deeply persecuted Jewish diaspora, the establishment of a Jewish National Home was seen as a necessity, albeit at a devastating and continuous cost to the Arab inhabitants and descendants of Historic Palestine. This process, heavily influenced by the colonial and imperialist attitudes of Western powers, is widely understood as an extension of Western geopolitical strategies in Muslim-majority lands. The Palestinian narrative of settler-colonialism encapsulates the vast injustices experienced before, during, and after the establishment of Israel. This project is often acknowledged as the last Western-sponsored colonial endeavor, emerging at a time when the international legal principle of self-determination had already gained broad recognition.  
The creation of Israel, though seen as necessary by many, occurred over the vehement objections of the Arab population in Palestine, leading to catastrophic suffering. The 1947 UN Partition Plan, which aimed to establish both Jewish and Arab states, was fraught with contention and reflects the moral dilemmas faced by the international community in creating an ethnically homogeneous Jewish Nation-State on land predominantly inhabited by Arabs.

### Economic and Cultural Fears of Arab Populations {#economic-and-cultural-fears-of-arab-populations}

The Arab fear of Jewish immigration and eventual domination in Palestine was driven by a combination of economic, cultural, and political anxieties. The discrepancy in wealth between the largely agrarian Arab population and the more economically advanced Jewish immigrants created a sense of economic displacement. Jewish immigrants, supported by wealthy Zionist organizations and great power influence, acquired land through legal transfers, often displacing Arab tenant farmers and altering the social and economic landscape. The creation of a Jewish national home, endorsed by the Balfour Declaration and backed by British colonial authorities, intensified these fears, as it was seen as an imposition by foreign powers that threatened Arab sovereignty and identity.  
Beyond economic concerns, Arabs feared cultural and religious erosion, particularly the potential loss of Islamic and Arab identity in Palestine, and the perceived threat to the sacredness of Jerusalem and other holy sites. There was also a profound fear of political marginalization, with the growing Jewish population potentially leading to the Arabs' loss of political power and influence. The rapid demographic changes sparked concerns about becoming a minority in their own homeland, exacerbating the sense of impending domination.   
Additionally, the social changes brought by Jewish immigration, including new economic practices, social structures, and modernist ideas, were seen as a threat to the traditional Arab social order. Many Arabs viewed the Zionist project as part of a broader pattern of colonial exploitation, akin to other Western imperial endeavors in the Middle East and North Africa, which added to the sense of injustice and fueled resistance. These intertwined fears collectively contributed to the deep-seated animosity and opposition that would shape Arab attitudes towards the Zionist movement and the eventual establishment of the State of Israel.

### Disillusionment with Political Processes {#disillusionment-with-political-processes}

The loss of faith among the Arabs of Palestine in the political process is a trend that dates back to the original British Mandate (*Peel Commission Report*, 1937). The failure of the Mandate to protect Arab interests and its perceived favoritism towards the Zionist project sowed deep mistrust in the political mechanisms that were supposed to safeguard their rights. This disillusionment was compounded by broken promises, unfulfilled commitments, and the inability of international institutions to address Arab concerns adequately. Over time, this erosion of trust in the political process contributed to a growing sense of helplessness and fueled resistance, as many Palestinians felt that peaceful and diplomatic avenues were increasingly ineffective in securing their rights and future. This loss of faith also explains the deep-seated resistance to any externally imposed solution, such as the two-state solution often touted by the West, which is viewed by many Palestinians as another attempt to dictate their fate without genuine consideration of their needs and aspirations.

### Recognition of Historical Grievances {#recognition-of-historical-grievances}

Acknowledging the tragedy of creating a new diaspora while settling another is vital. To deny the ethnic cleansing and continuous suffering of the Palestinians is to overlook the original sin of this conflict’s history. Recognizing these historical grievances is essential, not only as a matter of justice but as a foundation for future peace efforts. Any diplomatic resolution should involve a forthright recognition of the events of 1948, addressing Palestinian historical grievances as part of confidence-building measures that also critique current policies perpetuating further conflicts.

## Acknowledgments of the History of Jewish-Muslim Relations within the broader context of the Abrahamic Tradition[^3]: {#acknowledgments-of-the-history-of-jewish-muslim-relations-within-the-broader-context-of-the-abrahamic-tradition:}

The establishment of a Palestinian State requires the acknowledgment of historical conflicts between Jews, Christendom, and the Islamic World, with a clear understanding of their implications for all communities.

### We Must Acknowledge The Theological and Political Conflicts Starting From Medina {#we-must-acknowledge-the-theological-and-political-conflicts-starting-from-medina}

A significant factor in the Western indifference to the Palestinian question can be attributed to perceived antisemitism in the Muslim world, which its leaders have not addressed. This observation is not meant to blame the Palestinians for their plight but to highlight a critical barrier to broader empathy and support.  
A straightforward reading of conservative translations of the Quran, along with key Hadith, Tafsir, and Sira, reveals motifs that could be interpreted as anti-Jewish (Bostom, 2013). These interpretations often focus on the historical conflicts between the Prophet Muhammad and the Jewish tribes of Medina and Khaybar, reflecting tensions that influenced early Islamic teachings. While these texts are central to the Islamic faith, it is crucial to recognize that they do not inherently dictate antisemitic beliefs among Muslims today. Many Islamic scholars advocate for contextually driven interpretations that align with principles of peace and respect for all people.  
Hamas's utilization of certain verses in its charter and their presence in Palestinian educational materials[^4] highlights the challenges of historical religious tensions between Jews and Muslims. Although the updated Hamas charter attempts to distance the organization from outright antisemitism, it still denies the historical persecution of Jews as linked to Arab and Muslim heritage[^5], a stance that is factually questionable and hinders reconciliation efforts.  
It is impossible to understate the potential intractability of this problem. The responsibility falls on the leaders of the Arab and Islamic world to confront and speak to these theological tensions.   
By recognizing these challenges openly and striving for new approaches that encourage peaceful coexistence, there is potential for significant progress. Organizations such as the Arab League and the Organisation of Islamic Cooperation could lead this transformative dialogue, using platforms like the Saudi Arabia-Israel normalization processes or the United Nations Alliance of Civilizations as starting points.  
This approach to religious rapprochement aligns with recent movements towards moderation in the Muslim world, demonstrated by initiatives such as the Marrakesh Declaration and the Amman Message, which advocate for interfaith harmony and understanding.

### The Arab/Islamic World Must Acknowledge the Tolerance, Discrimination, and Persecution of the Jews Living in Arab/Islamic Lands {#the-arab/islamic-world-must-acknowledge-the-tolerance,-discrimination,-and-persecution-of-the-jews-living-in-arab/islamic-lands}

#### 	The Context of the Dhimmi Status on self-determination for People of the Book {#the-context-of-the-dhimmi-status-on-self-determination-for-people-of-the-book}

The historical dhimmi status of Jews in Muslim lands should logically cast doubt on the feasibility of the secular one-state solution of Palestine proposed by the Arab League during discussions over the future of Mandatory Palestine. While this status was not explicitly discussed in the partitioning of historical Palestine, it should lend credence to the belief that it would be unsafe to subject large Jewish populations to the rule of a majority Arab Muslim population, implying that a separate nation-state is needed to address the concerns about the Jewish nation's security in historical Palestine, especially against the backdrop of the ethnic violence following the Ottoman Empire’s dissolution.  
It is important to recognize that dhimmi status, while offering protection and certain rights, also designated Jews and other non-Muslims as second-class citizens within the Islamic world. As ‘People of the Book’ (Ahl al-Kitab), Jews were granted certain protections under Islamic law, but the degree of protection and the conditions of life under dhimmi status varied significantly depending on a range of factors, including the time period, geographic location, the attitudes of the ruling authorities, and the broader political, economic, and social context. In some periods and regions, Jewish communities thrived under Muslim rule, contributing to society in meaningful ways and enjoying a degree of autonomy in their religious and communal affairs. In other instances, they faced restrictions, discrimination, and persecution.

#### The Old Yishuv {#the-old-yishuv}

We must also recognize that the Old Yishuv, the Jewish communities that had resided in Palestine for centuries before the advent of Zionism, were relatively tolerated by the Arab population. Deeply rooted in the religious and cultural life of cities like Jerusalem, Hebron, Safed, and Tiberias, these communities were seen as part of the region’s historical fabric and did not pose a significant threat to Arab political or demographic interests. Unlike the newer Zionist immigrants associated with the nationalist movement and the push for a Jewish state, the Old Yishuv focused on religious scholarship and lived a largely apolitical existence.   
As part of the millet system during the Ottoman period, the Old Yishuv was granted a degree of religious and communal autonomy, which allowed them to manage their own affairs and maintain their religious practices. However, their status as dhimmis under this system also reinforced their position as second-class subjects, requiring them to pay the jizya tax and abide by various legal and social restrictions that marked them as non-Muslims. While there were instances of violence during periods of heightened tension, the Old Yishuv generally maintained peaceful, albeit sometimes uneasy, relations with their Arab neighbors. They were not the primary target of Arab resistance efforts during the British Mandate period, but the legacy of their dhimmi status continued to influence their experience of social and political inequality in Palestine.

#### The Context of Secularism in the Islamic World {#the-context-of-secularism-in-the-islamic-world}

In considering the feasibility of a secular one-state solution in Palestine, it's crucial to recognize that secularism in the Islamic world often differs from Western secularism. In many Islamic societies, even where secularism is officially embraced, religious principles and laws can still exert significant influence over governance. This stems from the belief that God's law, or Sharia, supersedes human-made laws. As a result, the ability to maintain true secularism within such a state is questionable, raising legitimate concerns about whether Jewish populations could trust that their rights and security would be adequately protected. This potential for religious influence in governance underscores the argument for the necessity of a separate Jewish nation-state to ensure these protections.  
We must recognize that beyond religious concerns, the Arab population in Palestine harbored other significant grievances against Jewish immigration, including economic displacement, cultural erosion, political marginalization, changes in social structures, and modernist ideas that threatened the traditional Arab social order.

#### Acknowledgement of Jewish Experiences in the Islamic World {#acknowledgement-of-jewish-experiences-in-the-islamic-world}

Nevertheless, leaders in the Arab and Islamic world need to acknowledge the full spectrum of experiences—positive, negative, and at times, oppressive—that Jewish communities have endured in their lands. While these persecutions were not the primary catalyst for Zionist settlement in Palestine nor the direct cause of the nationalist conflict between Jews and Arabs in the region, they have undeniably contributed to the deep-seated mistrust complicating the peace process in the Israeli-Palestinian conflict and broader Arab-Jewish relations. This shared history is known among both Arabs and Jews, and there is a pressing need for leaders to engage in frank and comprehensive dialogues about this past. Acknowledging these historical dynamics openly could pave the way toward breaking the cycle of violence.

#### The Christians Kill the Jews, So They Take Muslim Land?\! {#the-christians-kill-the-jews,-so-they-take-muslim-land?!}

While I recognize the Muslim perspective that views its relationship with Jews as superior to that with Christians—partly due to the protected status of Jews as People of the Book—and acknowledges the Christian world's role in making Muslims bear the consequences of Christian persecution of Jews, it is equally critical to address the historical treatment of Jews in the Muslim world. Such an acknowledgment is essential for fostering a balanced understanding and advancing the cause of reconciliation.

### The Israeli Nation Consists of the Jews of Islamic Lands {#the-israeli-nation-consists-of-the-jews-of-islamic-lands}

The Nation of Israel, situated at the crossroads of the Arab World, fundamentally includes a significant population of Jews from Arab lands—commonly known as Mizrahi Jews. These communities, having migrated to Israel primarily due to persecution and seeking safety, reflect a broader historical pattern of Jewish immigration in Muslim-majority lands. While the establishment of Israel involved violent conflicts and the displacement of Palestinian Arabs, it also marked another significant episode in the long history of Jews seeking refuge in the region, including the Jews of Christendom fleeing to Palestine to escape Christian persecution.  
This reality, although potentially uncomfortable for both Jews and Muslims, underscores a shared historical narrative that might serve as a foundation for mutual understanding and tolerance. Recognizing Israel as a diverse nation, including deep roots in the Middle East through its Mizrahi population, is crucial for regional acceptance and peace. Despite the contentious nature of their coexistence, both communities share a history of displacement and adaptation that could foster a common ground.  
Acknowledging this intertwined history is essential, not only for healing but also for the practical realities of cohabitation and mutual security. The journey towards peace requires accepting these complex identities and histories and working towards a future where both Jewish and Arab populations can coexist with mutual respect and security.

### We Must Acknowledge The Greater Christendom-Islamic World Fault Line in the Israeli-Palestinian Conflict {#we-must-acknowledge-the-greater-christendom-islamic-world-fault-line-in-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict}

The Israeli-Palestinian conflict, while fundamentally a nationalist and territorial dispute, is also deeply influenced by broader Christian-Muslim dynamics. Historically, the Western Christian world, led by the United States, has predominantly supported Israel, providing substantial political, military, and economic backing. This support is partly motivated by value alignment, strong political alliances and the theological beliefs of Christian Zionism, which sees the establishment of Israel as fulfilling biblical prophecy.

#### Western Christendom Is Responsible for Palestinian Disillusionment with the Political Process {#western-christendom-is-responsible-for-palestinian-disillusionment-with-the-political-process}

**Western Christendom's bias toward the Zionist cause is arguably the primary reason for the deep-seated disillusionment among Arabs towards the political process.** **Western political processes and interventions in the Arab world have largely resulted in negative outcomes, marked by a legacy of colonialism, support for authoritarian regimes, and destabilizing military interventions.**  
From the Balfour Declaration to the Peel Commission's partition proposal, Arab populations have witnessed the Western powers consistently favoring the establishment of a Jewish national home at the expense of Palestinian Self-Determination. This favoritism has fueled a profound sense of betrayal and injustice, leading many Palestinians to accurately view the political process as inherently biased and skewed against their interests. As a result, there is widespread skepticism and resistance to externally imposed solutions, such as the two-state solution, which are often seen as perpetuating Western dominance and neglecting the legitimate grievances and rights of the Palestinian people.  
Conversely, the Muslim-majority countries universally support the Palestinian cause, driven by a combination of religious solidarity, regional politics, and historical grievances. The centrality of Jerusalem and its Islamic holy sites further intensifies Muslim support for Palestinian rights.

#### The Legacy of The Crusades {#the-legacy-of-the-crusades}

Religious zeal, often manifested as a divine mandate for conquest, has been a core historical element in both Christianity and Islam, profoundly shaping their interactions through crusades, jihads, and the expansion of caliphates and kingdoms. The legacy of the Crusades has left lasting impressions on Christian-Muslim relations, with historical memories of conflict and conquest shaping contemporary attitudes. The interactions between Islamic Caliphates and the Western world, marked by periods of conflict and cooperation, have also played a significant role in shaping these dynamics. The colonial period, during which Christian European nations dominated and often exploited Muslim-majority lands, has further contributed to long-standing grievances and perceptions of injustice.  
These geopolitical alignments have added layers of complexity to the conflict, often exacerbating regional tensions and influencing international diplomacy. While there are significant efforts towards peace and reconciliation, including various peace processes and interfaith dialogue initiatives, challenges remain due to deep-seated mistrust and divergent objectives.  
**Amid these historical and ongoing dynamics, Western Christendom has a moral obligation to act as a stabilizer rather than an agitator.** Recognizing the role it has played in shaping the current landscape, it is imperative for Western nations to explicitly foster a stable social order for both the Palestinian and Israeli Nations.   
Christendom must leverage its considerable influence to encourage policies that acknowledge the rights and aspirations of all parties, actively supporting efforts that aim to heal divides rather than widen them. This balanced approach is not only a reflection of the ethical teachings central to Christian doctrine but also a practical strategy for lasting peace and stability in the region.  
This peace plan, while embracing certain Western values associated with human rights, democracy, and the rule of law, does so with a profound respect for the rich cultural and religious heritage of the Middle East. We are mindful that the imposition of values can be sensitive; hence, the approach is not about supplanting local traditions but enhancing governance and societal structures to ensure that all individuals within the region can enjoy peace, security, and prosperity.

## The Israeli State Cannot Resolve the Palestinian Question Unilaterally, by Devastating Force, Disenfranchisement, Humiliation, or Forced Displacement {#the-israeli-state-cannot-resolve-the-palestinian-question-unilaterally,-by-devastating-force,-disenfranchisement,-humiliation,-or-forced-displacement}

### 	The Iron Wall of Revisionist Zionism Crumbled on October 7th {#the-iron-wall-of-revisionist-zionism-crumbled-on-october-7th}

The Israeli-Palestinian conflict transcends the capacity of Israel alone to resolve, mainly through unilateral measures such as occupation and overwhelming disproportionate military force. Historical efforts, such as Ariel Sharon's unilateral disengagement plan or the periodic genocidal “mowing the lawn” operations, have failed to enhance security or bring peace to the region. The internal dynamics of Israel, marked by its collective trauma and the militancy of its population, compound the intractability of the conflict. Significant international assistance is necessary, as the conflict's resolution involves factors beyond Israel's control.  
The concept of relying on international (Gentile) intervention conflicts with the post-Holocaust consciousness of Jewish national security. Yet, the relentless nature of the conflict, exemplified by the October 7th attacks, demands a reevaluation of long-held security strategies, including the occupation of Palestinian territories.  
Furthermore, the perpetuation of images depicting the suffering of Palestinians has eroded international support, sparking a rise in antisemitism, particularly among Western youth, which will have long-term implications for Israel's global relationships and the security of Jewish communities worldwide.

### The Status Quo Implies Permanent Ethnic Conflict {#the-status-quo-implies-permanent-ethnic-conflict}

The ongoing occupation and the demographic reality of a significant Arab Muslim population under Israeli control challenge the strategic viability of maintaining a Jewish democratic majority, which implies a permanent infringement of Palestinian rights. This status quo implies ethnic conflict and extremism, contributing to the degradation of Israel’s long-term security and stability.  
However, it is critical to recognize that not tempering the maximalist claims of the state of Israel is leading to severe consequences. The pursuit of these goals, particularly through excessive military force and disenfranchisement, is causing atrocities against Palestinian Arabs and contributing to the overall degradation of Israel’s safety, security, and society. This approach not only undermines Israel's moral standing in the world but also erodes the internal fabric of the nation, fostering a cycle of violence and retribution that weakens its long-term viability as a secure and democratic state.  
Ultimately, the enduring solution requires rethinking Israel's future configuration, potentially moving towards a binational Judeo-Arab state that aligns with demographic realities (unlikely) or establishing a Palestinian state to ensure peace and security for both peoples. Only by tempering maximalist ambitions and embracing a pragmatic approach to coexistence can Israel hope to achieve a sustainable and peaceful future.

## The Palestinian Nation Must Advance Through Pragmatism, State-Building, Civil Resistance, and a Broader Use of Islamic Tradition {#the-palestinian-nation-must-advance-through-pragmatism,-state-building,-civil-resistance,-and-a-broader-use-of-islamic-tradition}

### 	This Peace Plan is Meant to Stop the Bleeding {#this-peace-plan-is-meant-to-stop-the-bleeding}

The disengagement strategy outlined in this peace plan is designed to stop the killing and provide the Palestinian people with the necessary breathing room by halting the ongoing cycle of violence, displacement, and destruction. By creating a separation from Israeli forces, this plan allows the Palestinian nation to focus on mourning its losses and beginning the critical process of rebuilding.  
The objective is to create a stable environment where the immediate threat of Israeli aggression is removed, giving Palestinians the space to heal and restore their communities without the constant pressure of conflict. This period of disengagement is crucial for the long-term viability of a Palestinian state, offering the time needed to lay the foundations for a peaceful and prosperous future.

### The Palestinian Vision For Self-Determination Must Be Acceptable to the Western World to End the Occupation {#the-palestinian-vision-for-self-determination-must-be-acceptable-to-the-western-world-to-end-the-occupation}

This peace plan is predicated on the Palestinian nation adopting a more pragmatic vision of self-determination—one that aligns with principles the Western world can support. It calls for a shift from maximalist goals toward a more achievable and sustainable pathway to statehood, recognizing the realities of the geopolitical landscape and the need for international cooperation.   
By embracing a pragmatic approach, the Palestinian National Movement can garner broader global support, particularly from Western nations, which is essential for securing the economic, political, and humanitarian aid necessary for nation-building and long-term stability. This approach ensures that the pursuit of self-determination is not only about reclaiming land but also about building a viable and stable state that can thrive in the modern world.

### The Limits of Martyrdom {#the-limits-of-martyrdom}

Recognizing the culture of martyrdom within the Palestinian community is essential; this culture, shaped by decades of conflict, displacement, and occupation, is not merely a symbol of despair but an expression of profound resistance and a means of asserting their struggle for national identity and statehood.   
The extremely harsh realities of life under occupation, including economic hardships, restricted freedoms, and genocidal violence, contribute to the valorization of sacrifice as a component of national identity. The valorization of sacrifice, reinforced by a collective narrative of resistance against perceived injustice and the fight for self-determination, is crucial for understanding the motivations behind martyrdom and addressing it in ways that lead to a more peaceful and constructive pathway forward.  
Despite the very practical power of religious zeal, the Palestinian nation must consciously reframe its culture of martyrdom to gain both international support for state creation and foster internal stability, especially with the introduction of the Confederation Peacekeepers.  
The disproportionate military asymmetry with Israel, combined with the Jewish people's 2000 years of experience in resilience and resistance, highlights the limitations of direct confrontation. Acknowledging this imbalance is essential for focusing national efforts on sustainable development and institution building within the political framework of the Canaan Confederation.

### The Theological Animosity Between Muslims and Jews Must Be Ameliorated {#the-theological-animosity-between-muslims-and-jews-must-be-ameliorated}

A respectful engagement with Islamic beliefs, which deeply influence the relationships between Jews and Muslims and encode early interactions between the two groups, is necessary given Islam’s pivotal role in Palestinian nationalism.
