The resolution of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict is contingent upon pragmatic adaptations—deliberately limited and deeply rooted in Islamic tradition—to foster coexistence.   
Hamas, the militant Islamist organization that has become the most dominant force in Palestinian politics, traces a spiritual and rhetorical lineage back to Amin al-Husseini, the original leader of the Palestinian national movement.   
Al-Husseini, as the Grand Mufti of Jerusalem, was the most prominent figure in early Palestinian resistance against both British rule and the Zionist movement, advocating for a Palestine that was exclusively Arab and Islamic. **His rhetoric, steeped in anti-Zionism and Islamic antisemitism, laid the groundwork for the uncompromising stance that Hamas adopted in its own charter and public declarations.**  
Like al-Husseini, Hamas rejects the legitimacy of the State of Israel and calls for the establishment of an Islamic state in all of historical Palestine, maintaining the same ideological framework that has driven much of the Palestinian national movement since its inception.

### Flexible Use of the Islamic tradition is necessary  {#flexible-use-of-the-islamic-tradition-is-necessary}

A significant grievance fueling the conflict from the Israeli perspective is the portrayal of Jewish people in Islamic education, which often perpetuates narratives contributing to mistrust and hostility. Addressing this educational aspect is crucial for altering perceptions and building a foundation for eventual reconciliation and mutual respect.  
Today, as the Muslim world confronts a range of existential threats, addressing these challenges demands a flexible, adaptive approach to using the rich history of the Islamic civilization as an example of coexistence. Instances of harmonious coexistence, such as those during the Islamic Golden Age—a period marked by a flourishing of science, culture, and religious tolerance—show that peaceful cohabitation is achievable within the broader context of the Islamic faith.  
**This peace plan emphasizes drawing on the broader tradition of the Islamic faith, rather than promoting specific interpretations, to minimize the natural imposition that often accompanies a peace plan.**  
Moral support for the Palestinian cause should simultaneously validate their experiences of oppression while advocating for a path that leads to actual progress—one that balances resistance with the necessity of pragmatism, state-building, and long-term peace and stability, within the Canaan Confederation framework.

## A Significant Amount of the Gazan Population Must be At Least Temporarily Resettled {#a-significant-amount-of-the-gazan-population-must-be-at-least-temporarily-resettled}

### 	The Destruction of Gaza is the ultimate realization of the Dahiya Doctrine {#the-destruction-of-gaza-is-the-ultimate-realization-of-the-dahiya-doctrine}

The Planetary Devastation of Gaza, under the Dahiya doctrine, has led to a situation where billions of dollars and years will be required merely for demolition, let alone reconstruction. Given these daunting financial and logistical challenges, no nation will likely commit the necessary funds without substantial guarantees. The international community, while posturing, may ultimately force many in Gaza to live in untenable conditions.   
Moreover, the entrenchment of extremism threatens the long-term viability of a rebuilt Gaza, continuing to pose an existential threat to Israel. Additionally, ongoing uncertainties in Israeli-Palestinian negotiations complicate any commitments from Arab nations regarding Gaza’s future. Given the staggering estimated costs of $20 to $90 billion required for rebuilding—sums that starkly contrast with the region's current economic capacity and population size—an evacuation strategy is regretfully humane to further minimize the Palestinian death toll.  
This step, while induced by the dire state of the region rather than chosen freely by its residents, must still be managed with the utmost respect for the rights and dignity of those affected. The international community must ensure that any such evacuation is conducted under adherence to international humanitarian law, including the recognition of an instance of forced population transfer as defined by legal standards.

## The Discontinuity of the Palestinian Territories Implies that Full Palestinian Sovereignty Over the Gaza Strip is Impossible {#the-discontinuity-of-the-palestinian-territories-implies-that-full-palestinian-sovereignty-over-the-gaza-strip-is-impossible}

Due to its isolation and compact size, the Gaza Strip is inherently dependent on external control over its borders, primarily by Israel and Egypt. This reality subjects Gaza to de facto Israeli-Egyptian security and humanitarian oversight. Any negotiated solutions, like a land corridor or tunnel connecting Gaza with the West Bank remain vulnerable to closures by Israel on security grounds. Therefore, any final status agreement must acknowledge these realities, proposing a distinct geopolitical status for Gaza that differs from that of the West Bank, reflecting its unique challenges and dependencies.

## A Future Palestinian Nation-State within the 1967 Borders Will Likely Resist for More Land {#a-future-palestinian-nation-state-within-the-1967-borders-will-likely-resist-for-more-land}

### 	The 1967 Border’s Are Likely A Temporary Solution {#the-1967-border’s-are-likely-a-temporary-solution}

The pursuit of a Palestinian nation-state within the 1967 borders faces inherent challenges due to the deep-rooted and mutually incompatible territorial claims rooted in the historical narratives of both Arabs and Jews. The Palestinian national consciousness, which has evolved under conditions of conflict and displacement, is unlikely to find satisfaction with just 22% of what is considered their historical homeland. This sentiment is exemplified by the ongoing activities in Gaza, which historically served as a significant base for Palestinian resistance since the 1948 conflict and continues to do so.  
The original 1947 UN Partition Plan, which sought to divide the land roughly equitably, has obviously failed to quell the underlying territorial dispute between the two nations. The idea of significant land swaps between Israeli and Palestinian states remains sensitive and fraught with the potential for further displacement and upheaval. Israeli concerns about strategic depth, along with the broad Palestinian desire for the entirety of historic Palestine, suggest that strategically redrawing borders might be a necessary discussion for long-term stability.

### Repartition Is Likely Necessary for a Stable Social Order {#repartition-is-likely-necessary-for-a-stable-social-order}

However, the feasibility of re-partition or significant border adjustments is limited by the current geopolitical context and the lack of military parity. Despite this, the conversation about potentially redrawing borders should remain on the table as the current configurations may not suffice to resolve the conflict sustainably.  
While a typical Zionist argument posits that Palestinians should have accepted a Partition Plan, the geometry of the 1947 Partition map, along with the national, demographic, and geographic realities of that time made such a partition untenable for Arab leaders, especially given the implied displacement of existing populations and the allocation of fertile lands like the Coastal Plain to the Jewish state—a decision that would be unacceptable to any nation.

# Proposed Actions for Collective Peace and Security: {#proposed-actions-for-collective-peace-and-security:}

## Establish a Multi-National Canaan Confederation as a Durable Diplomatic Vehicle {#establish-a-multi-national-canaan-confederation-as-a-durable-diplomatic-vehicle}

### 	Confederation Oveview and Membership {#confederation-oveview-and-membership}

The Canaan Confederation is envisioned as a robust multinational agency/force consisting of Arab, Muslim, and Western states, aimed at fostering stability across the Middle East through continuous diplomatic engagement. As a dedicated diplomatic vehicle, the Confederation will include the State of Israel and the State of Palestine as permanent members, thus reflecting the Judeo-Arab entanglement that is the Israeli-Palestinian Conflict. This union will also extend invitations to neighboring countries such as Egypt, Jordan, and Lebanon, as well as other influential global players, including the United States, Saudi Arabia, Iran, the UAE, the United Kingdom, France, Russia, Qatar, and others to join as observer members. These countries will contribute to and benefit from the Confederation's diplomatic infrastructure.  
Informally, the Confederation will simply be the name of the set of states involved in solving the tragedy of the Israeli-Palestinian Conflict. Israel's allies, the current Arab States lending diplomatic and humanitarian support, as well as countries currently funding UNRWA and supporting the Palestinians, are already members of this set.  
The Confederation's overarching principle is to provide hope and promote stability by delegating international arbitration, assistance, or observation to this collective, while minimizing the infringement on the sovereignty of the Israeli and Palestinian States. **It aims to serve as the vehicle for the Final Status Agreement for the State of Palestine. It will also facilitate a peace table and diplomatic vehicle between all member states to parley during conflict when truces are inevitably broken.**

### Governance and Security Dynamics {#governance-and-security-dynamics}

Regarding governance, the Palestinian State would be placed under the auspices of the Confederation, tasked with administering and revitalizing governance through either the Palestinian Authority or a new Arab governing entity. Additionally, a joint Arab-European-American force could rebuild the internal security of Palestinian territories, alleviating Israel's burden of policing these areas.  
	**However, recognizing the complex geopolitical dynamics, Israel would need to transfer its Security Sovereignty over the Occupied Territories to the Confederation for this initiative to succeed**.  
Given its history of extreme tactics, Hamas's status necessitates a reconstitution of its role if the Gaza Strip is to be rebuilt, requiring the exile of its military leadership to a Confederation observer state, the conditional surrender of its fighters in the Gaza Strip, and the integration of its governance structures into the broader framework of the Confederation after revising its charter to support the strategic goals of the Confederation.  
The Confederation, while not having a strong centralized voting system, would see countries voting with their contributions—financial, logistical, and personnel. The aim is to create a flexible yet robust framework for cooperation that adapts to the evolving geopolitical landscape, ensuring peace and stability through joint efforts and shared responsibilities.

## At Least a 30-Year Hudna Between All Signatories of this Plan {#at-least-a-30-year-hudna-between-all-signatories-of-this-plan}

### Purpose and Overview of the Hudna {#purpose-and-overview-of-the-hudna}

In an effort to establish a durable peace and lay the groundwork for comprehensive and lasting agreements, the plan proposes at least a 30-year Hudna among all parties involved in this ambitious peace architecture.   
This extended ceasefire is designed to provide the vital breathing room necessary for the complex task of implementing the nuances of such a transformative agreement. It represents a collective acknowledgment of war fatigue and signifies a commitment from all signatories to pivot towards a global campaign for peace, reconciliation, and the dawn of a new era reminiscent of an Abrahamic Golden Age.

### Challenges and Enforcement {#challenges-and-enforcement}

To encompass all aspects of the region’s dynamics, the Hudna will include infrastructure to monitor and report non-compliance and extremism. Recognizing that some Palestinian militant factions might opt out of the peace agreement, it is understood that these groups would then potentially face conflicts with the peacekeeping forces of the Canaan Confederation member states. Importantly, the raison d'être of this plan is to prevent these confrontations from replacing the current Israeli-Palestinian military engagements.  
Furthermore, we must remain vigilant about the potential risks from extremist elements within the Jewish community, recalling the historical activities of groups like Irgun, Lehi, and the Jewish Defense League and their subsequent effects on Israeli politics, as well as the rampant extremist settler violence occurring in the West Bank.   
While the Hudna aims to significantly reduce the frequency and intensity of conflicts for at least 30 years, it pragmatically acknowledges the inevitable breaches given the volatile history of the region. Nevertheless, the aim is to reduce the overall totality of conflict in the Middle East by at least one generation.

### Amnesty and Reconstruction {#amnesty-and-reconstruction}

As part of the ceasefire, detailed discussions will be needed to negotiate terms of amnesty, allowing both Israel and Palestine to focus on rebuilding their societies without the burden of past conflicts hanging over them. This amnesty is crucial for facilitating a forward-looking approach that focuses on reconstruction and state-building.  
The Hudna is envisioned not just as a temporary ceasefire but as a strategic pause that sets the stage for a comprehensive peace process, supported by mechanisms for monitoring, rapid conflict resolution, and continuous dialogue to adapt to evolving circumstances. By establishing this framework, we aim to create an environment conducive to peace and long-term stability in the region.

## Reclassify the Gaza Strip as Corpus Separatum Under Disputed/Confederation Sovereignty {#reclassify-the-gaza-strip-as-corpus-separatum-under-disputed/confederation-sovereignty}

The proposed reclassification of the Gaza Strip as 'Corpus Separatum' under disputed/Confederation sovereignty acknowledges the current high-intensity military disputes and the extensive reconstruction needed due to destruction from the Israeli-Hamas War. This on-paper action signifies the transitional status of Gaza’s sovereignty, necessitating substantial international assistance for governance rebuilding.

## Unified Acceptance of All Religious Traditions Necessary to Promote Peace in the Israeli-Palestinian Conflict {#unified-acceptance-of-all-religious-traditions-necessary-to-promote-peace-in-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict}

### We Must Respect Palestinian Self-Determination {#we-must-respect-palestinian-self-determination}

In seeking lasting peace in the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, it is crucial to respect the perspectives and rights of Palestinian Arabs, allowing them to lead their own journey toward coexistence with the Jewish people. The international community’s role should be to supportively facilitate these efforts, fostering an environment conducive to peace.

### However, Flexibility Is Needed vis-à-vis Islamic Teachings For This Order to Work {#however,-flexibility-is-needed-vis-à-vis-islamic-teachings-for-this-order-to-work}

The Islamic philosophical and intellectual tradition, celebrated for its depth and richness, provides the primary framework for addressing contemporary challenges. By tapping into this tradition, we encourage open dialogues within the Muslim community centered on principles of mercy, peace, and tolerance. These discussions, steered by the community's scholars and leaders, aim to draw on Islam’s rich historical legacies while exploring new pathways for peace.  
**This plan's approach is to avoid prescribing specific solutions as much as possible but to advocate for the widening of the Islamic intellectual and philosophical traditions to utilize the full breadth of the civilization’s history to enhance peace and coexistence.**  
By supporting this approach, we uphold the principle of self-determination and contribute to a more effective and respectful resolution of this enduring conflict.  
As we call upon our Muslim friends to explore their traditions to foster peace and understanding, we recognize that this is not a journey they should undertake alone. The Jewish community, too, holds a critical role in this endeavor. Just as Islamic scholars can look to the rich traditions of early thinkers for inspiration, so too can Jewish scholars draw upon the profound ethical teachings of our own tradition.

### Tikkun Olam Must Become the Motto For the Israeli State {#tikkun-olam-must-become-the-motto-for-the-israeli-state}

Judaism has evolved with time, reflecting the deep thinking of scholars who interpret the Torah and Talmud to meet contemporary needs. Today, we find ourselves at a crossroads where these interpretations can significantly impact our shared future. For instance, the Jewish concept of 'Tikkun Olam,' or repairing the world, encourages us to pursue justice and healing, which can serve as a foundational principle for peace.  
Moreover, initiatives like interfaith education programs, which bring Jewish and Muslim youth together, will be vital to the foundation of the Confederation. These programs not only educate but rebuild lost trust between communities.  
Our commitment to peace must be demonstrated in words and actions. We urge leaders and scholars within the Jewish community to join their Muslim counterparts in this crucial dialogue. By promoting teachings emphasizing respect, tolerance, and understanding and actively engaging in community outreach and educational reform, we can create a fertile ground for peace and mutual respect.  
Together, let us build a bridge of dialogue and understanding supported by the pillars of our rich, respective traditions. Let this be our joint contribution to a world where future generations can thrive in peace and harmony.

## The Formal Establishment of the Judeo-Islamic and the Abrahamic Traditions {#the-formal-establishment-of-the-judeo-islamic-and-the-abrahamic-traditions}

In an era marked by conflict, there lies an opportunity to revisit and revitalize the historically rich relationships that Jews, Christians, and Muslims once enjoyed. The proposed initiative to formally recognize and develop the Judeo-Islamic and Abrahamic traditions is not merely symbolic; it is a call to action for deep, meaningful reconciliation as we concurrently seek to resolve the Israeli-Palestinian conflict.

### A New Covenant for Al-Aqsa Mosque and Temple Mount: A Practical Détente {#a-new-covenant-for-al-aqsa-mosque-and-temple-mount:-a-practical-détente}

Central to our peace initiative is the establishment of a new Covenant for Al-Aqsa Mosque and Temple Mount. This covenant marks a critical juncture—a symbolic détente in Jewish-Muslim relations. Rather than aspiring to a utopian harmony, it acknowledges the complex realities and seeks to establish a framework for peaceful coexistence. This covenant is not about erasing differences but about managing them with mutual respect and shared objectives.  
The covenant aims to move beyond historical conflicts, fostering dialogue grounded in pragmatic cooperation. By formally establishing this détente, both communities signal their commitment to a more stable and constructive relationship, creating a foundation for future generations to build upon.  
Within the Canaan Confederation, educational materials will be tailored to reflect this pragmatic approach, framing historical interactions as lessons in negotiation and conflict resolution. These narratives will serve as essential tools for understanding the past's complexities while promoting a culture that values strategic dialogue and collaboration.  
The covenant will also function as a living document, continuously guiding interfaith relations to ensure that Al-Aqsa Mosque/Temple Mount remains a respected symbol of coexistence. Under this new framework, initiatives such as joint cultural festivals, Abrahamic dialogues, and collaborative community projects will be developed. These efforts will emphasize the site's role as a crucial bridge between communities, fostering shared experiences without demanding complete assimilation.  
By embracing this narrative of détente, we recognize the historical intricacies and the potential for a future where peaceful coexistence is the norm. The Al-Aqsa Mosque/Temple Mount will become a cornerstone of strategic interfaith cooperation within the Canaan Confederation, symbolizing a commitment to navigating the challenges of coexistence with wisdom and respect.

### The Revival of Judeo-Arabic, and Interfaith Diplomacy {#the-revival-of-judeo-arabic,-and-interfaith-diplomacy}

Language and cultural exchange are also vital. **We encourage the intentional revival of Judeo-Arabic as a bridge between Israeli and Palestinian communities.** By fostering this shared language for artistic and political dialogue, we highlight the interconnected narratives of Jews and Arabs. This linguistic revival will support mutual understanding and respect, which are critical components of lasting peace.  
Recognizing Medina's strategic significance, we propose its use as a venue for interfaith diplomatic events, symbolizing our commitment to these dialogues. Medina's historical openness to non-Muslim diplomatic presence makes it an ideal location for significant ceremonies, like signing peace agreements such as the Final Status Agreement for the State of Palestine, demonstrating our dedication to these principles in action.  
Finally, the involvement of key global and regional stakeholders—Israel, Saudi Arabia, Egypt, Jordan, and the Vatican—is crucial. Their support can ensure the success of these initiatives, leveraging their unique positions to foster dialogue, promote reforms, and implement the ambitious goals of this peace plan.  
By formally establishing the Judeo-Islamic and Abrahamic traditions, we do more than acknowledge our past; we build a foundation for a more harmonious future. This effort is a testament to our shared commitment to dialogue, understanding, and peace.

## Multilateral Disengagement: Deployment of Confederation Peacekeepers {#multilateral-disengagement:-deployment-of-confederation-peacekeepers}

### Israel Is Overextended In Its Ability To Protect Itself {#israel-is-overextended-in-its-ability-to-protect-itself}

**Israel is drastically overextended, facing an array of challenges that threaten its security, international standing, and long-term viability.** The combination of military strain, international isolation, and a growing list of adversaries has left Israel struggling to maintain control over the occupied territories and protect its borders. The complex network of threats, both external and internal, underscores the need for a reassessment of Israel's strategic direction, as the current trajectory is proving increasingly unsustainable.

### **Top Reasons Why Israel is Overextended:**

1. **Military Strain Due to the Israel-Hamas War**: The ongoing conflict with Hamas in Gaza, coupled with military challenges from Hezbollah in the north and the new front in the West Bank, has pushed the Israeli Defense Forces (IDF) to their limits. Sustaining operations on multiple fronts is depleting Israel’s military resources and eroding its readiness.  
2. **Massive Humanitarian Crisis in Gaza**: The Israel-Hamas war has led to a catastrophic humanitarian crisis in Gaza. The destruction of infrastructure, combined with severe restrictions on movement and access to necessities, has created dire conditions for civilians. This crisis further isolates Israel internationally and places additional moral and logistical burdens on its ability to sustain the occupation.  
3. **Pariah State Status**: In the aftermath of the Israel-Hamas war, Israel has increasingly become viewed as a pariah state by much of the international community, even though it retains significant support from Western allies. This shift has led to deeper international isolation, potential economic sanctions, and diplomatic challenges, making it more difficult for Israel to pursue its geopolitical goals and maintain the occupation.  
4. **Lost Support Among Democratic Voters**: Within the United States, Israel is losing support among younger and more progressive voters, particularly within the Democratic Party. This shift could weaken the traditionally strong U.S.-Israel relationship, reducing diplomatic and military support that Israel has relied on for decades.  
5. **Lack of Clear Strategic Vision for Dealing with Iran and Its Proxies**: Israel's focus on the occupation and regional security concerns has led to a lack of a coherent and clear strategic vision for dealing with the growing threat posed by Iran and its network of proxies. These proxies, including Hezbollah, Hamas, The Houthi’s, and various militias in Iraq and Syria, represent a multi-front threat that complicates Israel's defense strategy. Additionally, Iran's smuggling operations in the West Bank are creating another crisis, further destabilizing the region and adding to Israel's security challenges.  
6. **Erosion of Democratic Values**: The internal political landscape in Israel is increasingly contentious, with democratic values being eroded by morally bankrupt governments. Initiatives like the judicial overhaul have led to widespread protests and internal divisions, weakening the social fabric and democratic institutions that are crucial for Israel's stability and long-term governance.  
7. **Credible Accusations of Genocide**: Israel faces credible accusations of genocide related to its treatment of Palestinians, particularly in the context of military operations in Gaza and the West Bank. These accusations not only further isolate Israel internationally but also fuel resistance and deepen the moral and ethical dilemmas associated with maintaining the occupation.  
8. **Increasing Sophistication of Its Adversaries**: Israel's adversaries, including Hamas, Hezbollah, and Iran-backed groups, are becoming increasingly sophisticated in their tactics, technology, and strategic capabilities. This growing sophistication makes it more challenging for Israel to maintain military superiority and control over the region, further stretching its resources and complicating its security landscape.  
9. **No Credible Path to Peace**: The lack of a credible path to peace is a significant factor that exacerbates Israel's overextension. Without a viable plan or process for resolving the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, the occupation is likely to continue indefinitely, perpetuating cycles of violence, resistance, and international criticism. The absence of a peace process further complicates Israel's ability to achieve long-term stability and security.  
10. **Demographic Realities**: The demographic reality of a relatively small nation like Israel trying to control a large and growing Palestinian population is fundamentally unsustainable. The increasing Palestinian population threatens Israel's ability to maintain a Jewish majority while controlling a disenfranchised population, leading to long-term instability and resistance.  
11. **Political Desire for Lebensraum vs. Reality**: Israel's political desire for territorial expansion (Lebensraum) is increasingly disconnected from its ability to effectively and safely control these territories. The desire for more land does not align with the practical realities of governance, security, and international legitimacy, leading to strategic overreach.  
12. **Failure of War Goals in the Israel-Hamas War**: The stated goals of the Israel-Hamas war, including the destruction of Hamas and the return of hostages, have not been achieved. This failure, combined with the heavy costs of the war, has exposed the limits of Israel's military strategy and further strained its resources and international standing.  
13. **Hubris Leading to the October 7th Attack**: The October 7th attack by Hamas revealed a clear hubris within Israeli leadership, which underestimated the capabilities and resolve of its adversaries. This miscalculation not only led to significant casualties and the capture of hostages but also exposed vulnerabilities in Israel's security apparatus, shaking public confidence and international perceptions of Israel's strength.  
14. **Lack of a Credible Path to Military Independence**: Israel's military prowess is heavily reliant on its alliances, particularly with the United States. Despite its advanced defense industry, Israel lacks the economies of scale necessary to fully sustain its military needs through domestic manufacturing alone. The sheer size and technological reach of the U.S. military apparatus provide Israel with capabilities that it cannot replicate independently. Without a credible path to decoupling its military dependency on these allies, Israel remains vulnerable to shifts in international politics and the policies of its benefactors, further complicating its ability to maintain long-term security and strategic autonomy.  
15. **Loss of the Monopoly on the Use of Force**: Israel is increasingly losing its monopoly on the legitimate use of force, as armed settlers act with impunity, often with the complacency or tacit approval of members of the IDF. This erosion of state control is further exacerbated by the influence of ultranationalist figures like Itamar Ben-Gvir, who subvert the political will of the state and embolden these violent actors. The rise of rogue Jewish terror militias, driven by extremist ideologies, threatens to undermine the very foundation of the Israeli state. This internal fragmentation risks creating a scenario where state authority is challenged from within, further destabilizing Israel and complicating its ability to maintain order and security. v  
16. **U.S. Fatigue with Middle East Conflicts**: The United States, after decades of involvement in Middle Eastern wars, is increasingly fatigued with ongoing conflicts in the region. This war-weariness is leading to a shift in U.S. foreign policy priorities, with a growing reluctance to engage in or support new military entanglements. As a result, Israel will find it more challenging to secure the same level of U.S. military support in defending against Iranian aggression. This fatigue complicates Israel's strategic calculus, as it can no longer assume that the U.S. will automatically and robustly intervene on its behalf in future regional conflicts.  
17. **Threat to Jewish People Worldwide**: Israel's actions, particularly during the Israel-Hamas war, have heightened anti-Semitic sentiments globally, leading to increased threats against Jewish communities around the world. This backlash not only endangers the safety of Jews abroad but also complicates Israel's efforts to maintain international support and solidarity within the global Jewish community.

### Israel Must Have An Exit Plan For The Occupation

Israel is at a critical crossroads, facing severe overextension due to its current military, political, and diplomatic strategies. The ongoing conflicts, demographic pressures, and international isolation underscore the urgent need for a shift towards a more just and equitable order. To restore its sense of security and stability, Israel must reconsider its approach and move towards a resolution that acknowledges and addresses the rights and grievances of all parties involved. This necessitates a bold and transformative step: the multilateral disengagement of the Israeli military from the occupied territories.  
This disengagement, facilitated by international cooperation, should be supported by the deployment of peacekeepers from the proposed Canaan Confederation—a framework designed to promote stability, security, and reconciliation in the region. These peacekeepers would ensure a smooth transition, maintaining order and security as Israeli forces withdraw, while also providing a neutral buffer to prevent further escalations. Such a move would not only alleviate the military strain on Israel but also pave the way for a sustainable and just peace, creating the conditions necessary for a lasting resolution to the Israeli-Palestinian conflict and a more secure future for all.

### Strategy 1: Deployment in Lower-Risk Zones {#strategy-1:-deployment-in-lower-risk-zones}

**Minimizing Confrontations:** This approach focuses on deploying peacekeepers in areas where the likelihood of direct confrontation is lower, such as the Jordanian Valley and less volatile parts of the West Bank. The gradual deployment in these zones allows for more extensive community engagement, confidence-building measures, and the establishment of a stable presence without the immediate threat of violence. This strategy minimizes risks to peacekeepers and allows for a more controlled and sustained peacekeeping effort.

### Strategy 2: Deployment in High-Conflict Zones {#strategy-2:-deployment-in-high-conflict-zones}

**Prioritizing Urgent Needs:** The alternative strategy involves deploying peacekeepers in high-conflict areas where their presence is most urgently needed. These include regions like Jenin, Tulkarem, and Gaza, where confrontations between the State of Israel and Palestinian groups occur most frequently. This approach is more aggressive and aims to stabilize the most volatile areas rapidly, providing immediate protection to civilians and preventing further escalations. However, it carries a higher risk of direct confrontations with militant groups and requires a robust, well-prepared peacekeeping force. To further reduce friction and enhance cooperation, the Confederation will explore the possibility of negotiating militia-specific treaties with Palestinian resistance factions. These treaties would aim to ameliorate tensions and facilitate a more collaborative environment between peacekeepers and local armed groups. This approach aims not only to alleviate the immediate security concerns but also to restore a sense of humanity and justice to the governance of these territories, aligning with international law and moral expectations.

### Balancing the Strategies {#balancing-the-strategies}

The choice between these strategies will depend on the evolving political and security landscape. A phased or hybrid approach could also be considered, starting with lower-risk zones to establish a foothold and then gradually moving into higher-conflict areas as conditions permit. This adaptive strategy would allow the Confederation to respond to the most pressing needs while minimizing unnecessary risks to peacekeeping forces.

### Peacekeepers Must Maintain A Monopoly of the Use of Force {#peacekeepers-must-maintain-a-monopoly-of-the-use-of-force}

The peacekeeping forces must maintain a monopoly on the legal use of force in their deployed sectors. **This is essential not only for dealing with potential insurgencies and ensuring the safety of both peacekeepers and civilian populations but also for providing the Palestinian nation with much-needed relief from Israeli aggression**. By controlling the use of force, peacekeepers can prevent escalations and protect vulnerable communities from violence, thereby creating a more stable environment. This approach is crucial for mitigating threats posed by all forms of extremism, which jeopardize the objectives of peace and stability in the region. Ultimately, maintaining this monopoly on force aims to pave the way for a more peaceful coexistence and a comprehensive resolution of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict.

## Temporary Resettlement of A Significant Amount of the Gazan Population to the West Bank, With a Binding Right of Return Guaranteed by The Canaan Confederation {#temporary-resettlement-of-a-significant-amount-of-the-gazan-population-to-the-west-bank,-with-a-binding-right-of-return-guaranteed-by-the-canaan-confederation}

### 	It Is Not Sustainable To Keep The Palestinian’s in Gaza Indefinitely {#it-is-not-sustainable-to-keep-the-palestinian’s-in-gaza-indefinitely}

The Gaza Strip, enduring planetary devastation, presents a humanitarian crisis where the conditions continue to deteriorate, ensuring the exacerbation of the suffering among its population. The mental and physical toll on the Gazans under such dire circumstances makes it inhumane to compel them to remain in what is arguably the most devastated region on earth.  
Given this, the regretful evacuation of a significant portion of Gaza's population emerges as a critical, albeit reluctant, necessity. While this step arises from necessity rather than choice, it must be conducted with the highest respect for the rights and dignity of those affected. The international community, particularly the Canaan Confederation, must ensure that any such resettlement adheres to international humanitarian law to the greatest extent possible.   
An alternative scenario where Gazans are forced to live among the ruins of their former homes for an indefinite period is untenable and inhumane. Survival in such conditions is possible, but it does not contribute to a viable long-term solution to the conflict or the well-being of the people.

### This Plan Acknowledges This Is Forced Displacement {#this-plan-acknowledges-this-is-forced-displacement}

To facilitate this, Israel will have to create evacuation corridors to the West Bank, with international peacekeeping assistance. Moreover, a ***Binding*** UN Security Council Resolution must guarantee the Right to Return for all displaced Gazans guaranteed by The Canaan Confederation, properly enshrining this right under international law and record.  
This plan pragmatically acknowledges that many displaced Gazans will not return, and must accept that this is likely at least a generational trip for the families displaced, and that this represents another Nakba for the Palestinian people.  
Additionally, members of the Canaan Confederation should commit to accepting Palestinian refugees. This global approach not only shares the burden but also underscores the international community's role in bearing the burden of the sins of this unresolved conflict.

## Reserved Minority Representation in the Israeli Governing Cabinet {#reserved-minority-representation-in-the-israeli-governing-cabinet}

### Israel is an Ultranationalist State {#israel-is-an-ultranationalist-state}

In Israel, the balance between maintaining a democratic state and preserving its Jewish identity presents unique challenges. Ensuring that Israel’s minority citizens have a formal, reserved representation in the governing cabinet will be crucial for the moral fiber of the Israeli State.  
**Recent political developments in Israel have shown a trend where figures associated with ultranationalist ideologies have gained significant influence, as evidenced by individuals such as Itamar Ben-Gvir and Bezalel Smotrich rising to prominent positions.** This shift towards more extreme stances underscores the need for a governance structure that actively includes diverse perspectives, especially those from minority communities who are deeply impacted by these policies.  
**The historical experiences of the Jewish people with racism, ultranationalism, and occupation highlight the critical importance of preventing similar injustices within their own state.** Ensuring minority representation in government could serve as a counterbalance to potential ethnic supremacy and promote a more equitable society. This is not only a moral imperative but also a practical necessity to draw on all available human capital to address ongoing and future challenges in the region.  
Given the unlikely scenario of Jewish settlements in at least the early Palestinian state, the proposal for reciprocal commitments may not be necessary. However, for Israel, implementing reserved minority representation could be a significant step toward ensuring that its democratic institutions reflect and benefit all its citizens, thereby strengthening the state’s democratic and inclusive character.

## Reserved Female Representation in the Palestinian Liberation Organization {#reserved-female-representation-in-the-palestinian-liberation-organization}

	Ensuring reserved female representation within the Palestinian Liberation Organization (PLO) will significantly impact peace efforts and the overall stability of the region. Women in political leadership roles bring a wealth of benefits that extend beyond mere inclusivity. Their involvement will likely lead to more sustainable peace by incorporating a broader range of perspectives and priorities. Women leaders are known for their strong community ties, which can be instrumental in building grassroots support for reconciliation and peace initiatives.   
They tend to prioritize social welfare issues such as health, education, and economic development, which are critical for long-term stability and growth. Moreover, women often advocate for non-violent solutions, contributing to a decrease in overall violence. The inclusion of women in leadership also helps to legitimize peace efforts both locally and internationally, showing a commitment to balanced representation and inclusivity. Thus, promoting female leadership within the PLO is not only a step towards gender equity but also a strategic enhancement of the effectiveness and sustainability of peacebuilding efforts.

## Expand the Definition of Weapons of Mass Destruction to Include Advanced Artificial Intelligence Systems {#expand-the-definition-of-weapons-of-mass-destruction-to-include-advanced-artificial-intelligence-systems}

The development and deployment of advanced AI systems in military operations, as evidenced by Israel's use of systems like the Habsora and Lavender Targeting Recommendation Systems, underscore the potential for new technologies to impact modern warfare significantly. These systems, which leverage machine learning to enhance targeting and operational decisions, represent a technological leap that could pose risks comparable to traditional WMDs in terms of their impact on civilian populations and global stability.  
Given these concerns, there is a pressing need for international recognition and regulation of such technologies. This would help mitigate the risks associated with their development and deployment and slow our progression toward scenarios that could lead to the obliteration of the human race.

### Transparency is Needed To Adjudicate Genocidal Intent {#transparency-is-needed-to-adjudicate-genocidal-intent}

Transparency in how these AI systems are trained, validated, and deployed must be mandated. The Israelis, who are at the forefront of this technology, should disclose the methodologies involved in training and validating their systems. This transparency is crucial not only for fostering international trust but also for ensuring that the deployment of these systems complies with international humanitarian laws or are dismantled accordingly.	  
**Moreover, the use of such advanced AI in conflict zones must be scrutinized to determine if their deployment meets the legal definitions of warfare conduct, including the evaluation of whether such actions could be de jure legal but de facto genocidal**. This scrutiny should be part of an international framework to ensure that all nations employing similar technologies adhere to the same standards of accountability.

## Mandatory Land Lease: Sanctions Imposed for Expansion Beyond 1947 Allocations {#mandatory-land-lease:-sanctions-imposed-for-expansion-beyond-1947-allocations}

To address the ongoing expansion of Israeli settlements beyond the territories initially allocated to Israel by the 1947 UN Partition Plan, a system of economic sanctions is proposed. This plan would impose a financial penalty per dunam on the total area exceeding the 55% land allocation, excluding the Golan Heights, and any buffer zones and DMZ’s created for population disengagement.

### Israel Is Overextended in Its Ability to Secure Itself Due to Bad Politics and a Lack of Strategic Vision {#israel-is-overextended-in-its-ability-to-secure-itself-due-to-bad-politics-and-a-lack-of-strategic-vision}

**This financial repercussion aims to freeze settlement activity and curtail the settler movement, which is at the forefront of the territorial occupation and radicalization present in Israeli society.** The ongoing expansion is part of an ***overextension*** that not only threatens peace and stability in the region but also hampers Israel’s long-term security and international relations.  
**Appropriating Holy Land from the Palestinian nation to build houses is not an effective anti-terror strategy; instead, it is a tactic driven by political ideology rather than long-term strategic vision, focusing more on short-term gains and the appearance of control rather than on addressing the underlying causes of conflict and working towards a sustainable peace.**  
**The pursuit of a Greater Israel, driven by tactical decisions without a coherent strategic vision, has compromised Israel’s long-term security and stability.** While short-term actions such as settlement expansion and territorial control may offer immediate gains, they fail to address the demographic realities and geopolitical challenges that threaten the viability of a Jewish and democratic state. **The politically driven expansion of Israel’s borders disregards the fact on the ground that there are not enough Jews to sustain such a vision, leading to policies that undermine both Israel’s security, morality, and its international standing.**

### Land Lease, Either Adopted or Imposed {#land-lease,-either-adopted-or-imposed}

**To enforce these sanctions, a Land Lease scheme must be implemented or imposed.** This scheme would require the cooperation of all of Israel's diplomatic and trading partners, ensuring a concerted international effort to support the enforcement of these penalties in the case of non-compliance.   
Implementing this scheme would compel Israel to make critical decisions regarding what land it wishes to claim based on its financial and strategic viability. This approach does not only seek to penalize but also to provide a structured pathway for Israel to align its settlement policies with secure borders, thereby contributing to a more sustainable and peaceful resolution of the conflict.  
**This peace plan unequivocally advocates that no individual’s citizenship will be stripped during the process of land reallocation.** The protection of citizenship rights is paramount, as the presence and inclusion of minorities within Israel will be crucial for future reconciliation efforts.   
These minority communities serve as bridges between the Israeli and Palestinian populations, embodying the possibility of coexistence and mutual respect. Their role in fostering dialogue and understanding is indispensable, and their citizenship must remain intact to pave the way for a peaceful and integrated future.   
While Israel may inevitably attempt to challenge this principle, the plan is designed with enough strategic ambiguity to ensure that citizenship rights are upheld and remain non-negotiable.

## Explicitly Condition U.S. Military Aid to Israel Based upon Compliance with the Canaan Confederation Framework {#explicitly-condition-u.s.-military-aid-to-israel-based-upon-compliance-with-the-canaan-confederation-framework}

### Heeding George Washington's Warning Against Permanent Entangling Alliances {#heeding-george-washington's-warning-against-permanent-entangling-alliances}

In line with the principles advocated by George Washington in his farewell address to the young American nation, which cautioned against forming permanent, unconditional military alliances that might not align with American interests and risk entangling the nation in ongoing foreign conflicts, the U.S. must develop a conditional framework for its military aid to Israel. This framework is intended to support a strategy that prioritizes a sustainable peace process over an overreliance on military deterrence, often leading to the overextension of military efforts and the exacerbation of conflicts for political gain.

### Congressional Oversight on Israel's Adherence to the Canaan Confederation Framework {#congressional-oversight-on-israel's-adherence-to-the-canaan-confederation-framework}

Central to this proposal is a periodic review process, synchronized with Congressional debates on foreign aid bills, to ensure that assessments of Israel's compliance with the Canaan Confederation agreements directly influence Congressional decisions regarding the continuation, modification, or cessation of military aid. These reviews would evaluate Israel's commitment to cooperative security arrangements, the protection of civilian rights, and overall cooperation within the confederation framework.  
The findings from these reviews would be compiled and presented to Congress. This procedure is designed to enhance legislative oversight and ensure that U.S. military aid promotes long-term stability and peace consistent with American values and strategic goals. By linking aid to general compliance with the framework and embedding the review process within the political process, this policy aims to enhance accountability and ensure that military support serves as a constructive tool in international relations, adapting to evolving dynamics and aligning with U.S. strategic interests in maintaining Pax Americana in a multipolar world.

## Offer the State of Palestine a Compact of Free Association with the United States, conditioned upon their adherence to the Canaan Confederation framework {#offer-the-state-of-palestine-a-compact-of-free-association-with-the-united-states,-conditioned-upon-their-adherence-to-the-canaan-confederation-framework}

### 	A Compact of Free Association as Partial Restitution {#a-compact-of-free-association-as-partial-restitution}

The proposal emphasizes a strategic partnership primarily with the United States, focusing on the integration of the State of Palestine into the global community through a Compact of Free Association. This compact, contingent upon Palestinian acceptance of the Canaan Confederation framework, represents a profound commitment to rectifying historical injustices while facilitating Palestine's economic and educational advancement. It draws upon the model historically used to support Israel, acknowledging that while the creation of Israel addressed a critical need for the Jewish people, it also resulted in severe repercussions for the Palestinian Arabs, including displacement and ongoing conflict.

### Bridging the Geopolitical Fault line Through Western Integration {#bridging-the-geopolitical-fault-line-through-western-integration}

The strategy of shifting the geopolitical fault-line to integrate the Palestinian nation into the Western world represents a bold and transformative approach to resolving the Israeli-Palestinian conflict. By aligning Palestine more closely with Western economic systems, educational exchanges, and political alliances, this plan seeks to bridge the historical divide that has marginalized the Palestinians. Offering a Compact of Free Association with the United States could serve as a cornerstone of this strategy, providing economic support, security guarantees, and a stronger connection to the international community. This approach not only aims to stabilize and empower the Palestinian state but also repositions it as a dynamic and integral part of the global order, fostering peace and prosperity in a region long defined by conflict.  
Offering a Compact of Free Association to Palestine by the United States would provide not only economic support and security guarantees but also crucial international recognition. This gesture of justice and restitution recognizes the enduring grievances of the Palestinian people, establishing a foundation for a more equitable path towards regional peace and stability. It also proposes making Palestine a vibrant center for tourism and pilgrimage, leveraging its historical and spiritual significance to enhance economic stability.

### Gaza As An Educational Nexus: Building the New House of Wisdom {#gaza-as-an-educational-nexus:-building-the-new-house-of-wisdom}

The integration initiative could further extend to forging cultural and educational ties, such as transforming the Gaza Strip into a nexus of culture and learning. Plans would include establishing a center reminiscent of the historic House of Wisdom along with a Museum of Islamic Civilization. This would not only highlight the rich intellectual heritage of the Islamic world but also attract global scholarly attention and tourism, creating sustainable sources of income and fostering international goodwill.  
Emphasizing human rights and universal values of justice and equality is crucial, serving as prerequisites for continued international support. This approach positions economic empowerment, educational advancement, and cultural revival at the heart of a comprehensive blueprint for addressing the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, promoting long-term peace and prosperity in the region.

## A US-Led Enforcement Action Against Iran and its Proxies If They Refuse/Violate The Hudna {#a-us-led-enforcement-action-against-iran-and-its-proxies-if-they-refuse/violate-the-hudna}

### Containing the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps {#containing-the-islamic-revolutionary-guard-corps}

Given the persistent regional threats posed by Iran and its proxies, including the IRGC (Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps) and Quds Force, a contingency plan for a US-led enforcement action becomes necessary to meet the stringent security guarantees needed by Israel for this plan to succeed. This action would be considered if Iran refuses to participate in a peace treaty or substantially violates an established Hudna, thereby risking further escalation that could potentially lead to a broader conflict.  
The proposal recognizes these groups' existential threats to regional stability for decades. It suggests that the existing regional cooperation pact, which has previously defended Israel from Iranian aggression, could be formalized to strengthen deterrence mechanisms.  
While acknowledging the legitimate grievances Iran may hold against Western and American influences, the proposal critically views the Islamic Revolution's regressive ideologies and their impacts, including religious-based oppression and its broader social consequences. The historical context of Iran's technological and cultural contributions, particularly before the isolation of the Iranian civilization, underscores the potential benefits of Iran improving its relationships with the Western and Arab worlds.  
Furthermore, the trauma of the Iran-Iraq war and its enduring impact on Iran's national psyche, including the development of a martyrdom culture, highlight the deep-seated complexities at play. The proposal argues that the UK and the US, having historical roles in shaping modern Iranian attitudes, should lead efforts to achieve détente with Iran. This approach aims for a resolution that respects Iran’s rich cultural and historical contributions while pragmatically addressing current geopolitical realities.

### Iran's Contribution to the Canaan Confederation Waqf: A Path for Rebuilding Gaza and International Reintegration {#iran's-contribution-to-the-canaan-confederation-waqf:-a-path-for-rebuilding-gaza-and-international-reintegration}

**Iran is invited to contribute its frozen assets to the Canaan Confederation Waqf as a step toward international reintegration, symbolizing its commitment to peace and regional stability.**  
This initiative draws inspiration from Cyrus the Great, who supported the rebuilding of the Jewish Temple in Jerusalem, during a period when Zoroastrianism likely influenced the development of Jewish thought and, by extension, the broader Abrahamic tradition. By following this precedent, Iran can rekindle this ancient connection, playing a constructive role in the Middle East's future and reaffirming its commitment to peace, cooperation, and shared values.

## Confidence Building Actions for Nations Supporting The Canaan Confederation {#confidence-building-actions-for-nations-supporting-the-canaan-confederation}

As the post-World War II liberal international order shows signs of cracking, it is critical to renew our collective commitment to it, addressing emerging multipolarity to maintain global stability. This renewal requires addressing critical issues that divide nations, especially along civilization fault lines.  
To foster peace and stability in the Middle East, the Canaan Confederation seeks to promote confidence-building measures that address historical grievances and contemporary challenges. These measures are designed to soothe existing tensions and lay a foundation for enduring cooperation across the region.

### Asylum for Members of the Old Order {#asylum-for-members-of-the-old-order}

**Members of the Confederation can offer asylum to leaders of the old order as a confidence-building measure, facilitating a peaceful transition and stabilization within the region.**

### Funding the Confederation Waqf

The involvement of the Western world in guaranteeing the support and security of the Canaan Confederation through the strategic use of frozen Iranian assets to fund the Confederation Waqf will be pivotal.

### Addressing Historical Grievances due to Colonialism {#addressing-historical-grievances-due-to-colonialism}

Historically, colonial actions by major powers have left deep scars that contribute to ongoing mistrust and conflict. Recognizing this, we propose that key nations undertake gestures of reconciliation. France and the UK, for instance, should formally apologize for their roles in the Sykes-Picot Agreement, which arbitrarily divided the Middle East in ways that have fueled conflict for over a century. Similarly, the United States and the UK need to acknowledge their involvement in the 1953 Iranian coup, which has long soured Iran's relations with the West. Additionally, the United States should address its missteps leading to and during the Second Gulf War, particularly the intelligence failures and policies that precipitated widespread chaos and contributed to the rise of ISIL.

### The Arab World Must Improve Its Respect for Human Rights {#the-arab-world-must-improve-its-respect-for-human-rights}

These historical reflections should be complemented by proactive steps to improve human rights and freedom of expression in the Arab and Islamic world to increase the Ummah’s soft power, which has very real implications for the humanization of the Palestinian people.

### Americas Geopolitical Rivals Must Assist For World Stability {#americas-geopolitical-rivals-must-assist-for-world-stability}

Finally, stabilizing international relations between the United States, China, and Russia is crucial for providing a stable backdrop for the Confederation's activities. We can ensure a cooperative approach to resolving the Middle East's complex issues through a concerted effort to mend these international rifts.  
These confidence-building actions represent a sampling of the comprehensive approach required to address the roots of conflict and lay the groundwork for a peaceful and prosperous region, aligning historical grievances with contemporary needs for justice, reconciliation, and mutual respect.

### US-Turkey-Palestine Joint Effort for Gaza Reconstruction

In a strategic move to enhance the reconstruction of the Gaza Strip, the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers, in collaboration with Turkish contractors and the Palestinian Authority, will deploy a workforce comprising both Turkish and Palestinian labor. This approach aims to utilize the extensive construction experience of Turkish professionals alongside the local knowledge and skills of Palestinian workers. By integrating these diverse capabilities, the partnership seeks to streamline the rubble clearance and rebuilding processes efficiently. This method is not just about physical reconstruction; it aims to foster a cooperative and respectful work environment, promoting intercultural understanding and strengthening economic recovery efforts. This collaborative workforce strategy will contribute significantly to regional stability, peace, and prosperity by rebuilding trust and cooperation among the communities involved.

# Potential Pathways for the Evolution of the Canaan Confederation: Addressing the Right of Return and the Status of East Jerusalem {#potential-pathways-for-the-evolution-of-the-canaan-confederation:-addressing-the-right-of-return-and-the-status-of-east-jerusalem}

The Confederal Framework is designed to evolve, offering pathways to address key issues such as the Right of Return and the status of East Jerusalem. Its flexibility is based on unprecedented pragmatism and reconciliation between the two nations, allowing for phased solutions and mutual concessions tailored to their evolving needs, thereby fostering cooperation and aiming for a sustainable resolution.  
Recognizing that the demographic balance of the State of Israel is a hard constraint, any right of return will naturally be limited. Addressing historical grievances from the Nakba realistically involves acknowledging this event and providing more equitable territorial concessions and exploring other forms of reparations that can further the reconciliation process. These may include financial compensation, restoration of property rights, or cultural acknowledgments, all contributing to honoring the past while laying the foundation for a more just and sustainable peace process. This approach offers a path forward that respects the needs and identities of all parties involved.

## Two Semi-Separate States with the Expiration of the Confederation {#two-semi-separate-states-with-the-expiration-of-the-confederation}

This is not preferred, but the Confederation could serve as a temporary framework that facilitates the peaceful coexistence and development of Israel and Palestine until both entities are ready to function semi-independently. In this phase, the right of return would be limited, with a focus on resettlement within the Palestinian state rather than Israel proper. East Jerusalem could potentially be designated as the capital of the Palestinian state, though sovereignty might remain fully with the State of Israel, with Ramallah remaining the Capital of the Palestinian State. The Confederation would play a crucial role in facilitating negotiations over the status of East Jerusalem during this period.   
After a set period or upon achieving certain milestones, the Confederation could dissolve, leaving behind a sovereign state of Israel and a semi-sovereign state of Palestine with clearly defined borders and semi-independent governance. **Due to the power imbalance between the State of Israel and Palestine, the Palestinian State will not have all the rights of a fully sovereign State but will exist in a stabler manner than today.** This pathway attempts to meet the aspirations for statehood on both sides while recognizing geopolitical reality.  
**A Compact of Free Association between the State of Palestine and the United States of America can ameliorate the loss of full self-determination of the Palestinian State and to rebalance the relationship between the State of Israel and the State of Palestine.** This forms the core of the backup plan for the Canaan Confederation and can go far in stabilizing the social order in the Middle East.

## Permanent Existence of the Confederation {#permanent-existence-of-the-confederation}

This is the minimally viable solution. The Canaan Confederation could become a permanent fixture in the region, providing a continuous framework for cooperation and shared governance. With the Confederation becoming permanent, there is greater potential for more flexible solutions to both the right of return and East Jerusalem. The Confederation could oversee a limited and managed return of Palestinian refugees, primarily within the Palestinian Territories but possibly with a limited number into Israel proper, while perhaps allowing for East Jerusalem to become the capital of the Palestinian State. The Confederation would act as a stabilizing force, ensuring that both Israel and Palestine can coexist peacefully while addressing shared challenges such as security, economic development, and resource management. The Confederation’s permanence would symbolize a long-term commitment to peace and regional stability, potentially serving as a model for conflict resolution in other parts of the world.

## A Canaan Federation {#a-canaan-federation}

The most stable end-game that respects the needs of two states for two peoples. The Canaan Confederation could evolve into a more robust Canaan Federation where both Israel and Palestine retain significant autonomy but operate under a centralized federal authority for certain critical functions, like foreign policy. In this model, there is the possibility of a full right of return to Israel proper, with Palestinians being granted permanent residency status. However, Palestinian enfranchisement would be reserved for the Palestinian state, allowing Palestinians to maintain their cultural and political identity within the Federation. Jerusalem would serve as a shared capital, reflecting the deepened cooperation between the two entities. This federal model would focus on shared governance in areas such as security, foreign policy, and infrastructure, while allowing each entity to maintain its cultural and political identity. Over time, as trust and cooperation deepen, this model could strengthen, leading to more integrated governance structures and potentially a shared national identity.

## Single Binational Judeo-Arab State of Canaan {#single-binational-judeo-arab-state-of-canaan}

This is a highly romantic endgame of the Confederation. This would involve the integration of Israeli and Palestinian territories into a unified political entity where both Jewish and Arab populations share equal rights and responsibilities.   
In this scenario, the right of return could be more broadly implemented within a unified state, allowing for full citizenship rights and resettlement throughout the state, including in Israel proper and Jerusalem. Jerusalem would be a unified city, serving as the capital of the unified state and symbolizing the shared heritage and new national identity that blends Jewish and Arab elements. **This pathway would require significant reconciliation efforts, the conclusive resolution of long-standing grievances, a shared commitment to fostering new moral and cultural values aimed at coexistence, and a commitment to the principles of natural law. If successful, it could lead to a state representing a neo-Canaanite national identity, drawing from Jewish and Arab heritages.**

## Conclusion {#conclusion}

The Confederal substrate is a dynamic framework designed to adapt to the needs and aspirations of the Israeli and Palestinian peoples. As the Confederation evolves, the prospects for addressing the right of return and the status of East Jerusalem increase, with more integrated models offering greater potential for meaningful solutions. Whether it evolves into a stronger federal model, a single binational state, two separate states, or remains a permanent entity, the Confederation provides the necessary flexibility to respond to the complex realities of the region. Its ultimate form will depend on the progress made in reconciliation, governance, and mutual respect between the two nations.

# The Rebirth of the Virtuous City of Gaza {#the-rebirth-of-the-virtuous-city-of-gaza}

### Al-Farabi's Vision For the Perfect City-State

Our commitment to rebuilding the Gaza Strip stands central as we envision the region's future. **The rebuilding of the Gaza Strip into a vision inspired by Abu Nasr Al-Farabi’s “Al-Madina Al-Fadila,” or the 'Virtuous City[^6]' is essential not only for the well-being of its residents but also for Israel's acceptance in the Middle East**. This reconstruction can commence only after the exit of the military leadership of Hamas and Palestinian Islamic Jihad and their organized battalions conditionally surrender and pledge to work within the new political framework.

### Rebuilding The Gaza Strip and The Palestinian Nation Movement

Addressing Palestinian factionalism is crucial. The Palestinian National Movement must strive for unity, drawing upon the Arab Nation’s pool of skilled technocrats. These leaders can drive the nation-building efforts essential for a modern Palestinian state.  
A technocratic government should be tasked with first crafting a 30-year Virtuous City plan, laying the foundations for economic development, social cohesion, and political stability for the rebuilt Gaza Strip. Setting an expiration and renewal date for the Confederation, initially aligned with the 30-year Hudna, will provide a structured timeline for assessing progress and making necessary adjustments.

### A More Stable Order For Both Israeli’s and Palestinians

My vision is a future where the Palestinian and Israeli states coexist—uneasily, perhaps, but in a significantly more stable relationship than today. Conflict may persist, but its intensity must be dramatically reduced to avoid tragedies like those witnessed on October 7th or the subsequent obliteration of the Gaza Strip.  The Confederal substrate is flexible enough to evolve with the self-determination goals of the Israeli and Palestinian Nations toward a more unified and just union. **The ultimate goal is clear: such acts of violence must never be repeated, and the immense suffering experienced must not recur. From the river to the sea, only peace will set us free.**

## 

# Appendix A: Draft Articles of Confederation for the Canaan Confederation Multinational Force {#appendix-a:-draft-articles-of-confederation-for-the-canaan-confederation-multinational-force}

**Preamble**  
Recognizing the complexities and historical sensitivities of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, these Articles of Confederation establish a multinational force dedicated to maintaining peace, security, and fostering conditions for long-term stability and cooperation in the region.

**Article 1: Purpose and Principles**  
	1\.	The primary purpose of this Confederation is to maintain peace and security in the region, and to facilitate a conducive environment for dialogue and cooperation between Israel, Palestine, and the greater Middle East.  
	2\.	The Confederation shall operate with full respect for the sovereignty and legal frameworks of both Israel and Palestine and adhere to international law and human rights standards.

**Article 2: Structure and Composition**  
	1\.	The Confederation will consist of a multinational force, with contributions from various nations, subject to approval by both Israel and Palestine.  
	2\.	A permanent negotiating council, with representatives from Israel, Palestine, and contributing nations, will haggle the operations of the Confederation and operate by strategic consensus. 

**Article 3: Security Operations**  
	1\.	The multinational force will engage in peacekeeping operations, border security, and monitoring to prevent hostilities and ensure the safety of both nations.  
	2\.	Rules of engagement for the force will be clearly defined and agreed upon by the governing council.

**Article 4: Conflict Resolution and Mediation**  
	1\.	The Confederation will provide mechanisms for conflict resolution between member states, including mediation and arbitration services.  
	2\.	A dedicated peace table will be formed within the Confederation to address and resolve emerging conflicts.

**Article 5: Governance and Cooperation**  
	1\.	While the primary focus is on security, the Confederation will also facilitate cooperation in areas like infrastructure development, environmental protection, and cultural exchange.  
	2\.	Joint committees may be established for specific cooperative projects or initiatives as needed.

**Article 6: Establishment of a Special Tribunal of Last Resort** 

1. A Tribunal of Last Resort shall oversee legal disputes within the Confederation. The scope of this tribunal will be negotiated and agreed upon by all member states of the Confederation.

**Article 7: Funding and Resources**  
	1\.	The Confederation will be funded through contributions from member nations, as well as potential funding from international organizations.  
	2\.	A transparent financial system will be established to manage and allocate these funds.

**Article 8: Communication and Transparency**  
	1\.	The Confederation will maintain open and transparent communication channels both internally and with the public.  
	2\.	Regular reports on the Confederation’s activities and progress will be made available to ensure accountability and public trust.

**Article 9: Training and Capacity Building**  
	1\.	The Confederation will implement comprehensive training programs for its personnel, focusing on areas such as peacekeeping operations, cultural sensitivity, and conflict resolution.  
	2\.	Joint training exercises with local authorities will be conducted to foster mutual understanding and effective collaboration.

**Article 10: Duration, Review, and Renewal**  
	1\.	The Confederation is established for an initial period of 30 years, starting from the date of ratification by both Israel, Palestine and the founding core states.  
	2\.	A comprehensive review of the Confederation’s effectiveness will be conducted at the end of the 10th year, with a special review subcommittee appointed for this purpose.  
	3\.	Decisions on the renewal, amendment, or termination of the Confederation will be made based on the outcome of the 30-year review, with the option for renewal if agreed upon by both parties.  
	4\.	In case of non-renewal, a structured plan for the orderly withdrawal of the multinational force and transfer of responsibilities will be implemented.

**Article 11: Amendments and Ratification**  
	1\.	Amendments to these articles can be proposed by any member of the governing council and require a consensus or supermajority for adoption, depending on their nature and impact.  
	2\.	The Articles of Confederation will be ratified according to the legal procedures of both Israel and Palestine and will come into effect upon mutual ratification.

**Article 12: Exit Strategy and Contingency Planning**  
	1\.	An exit strategy will be developed for scenarios where the Confederation may need to be dissolved or its mission significantly altered.  
	2\.	Contingency plans will be in place to address potential emergency situations, including escalation of hostilities or humanitarian crises.

**Article 13: Special Provisions for the West Bank and Gaza**  
	1\.	Security and Stability:  
	•	The Confederation will prioritize the establishment and maintenance of security and stability in both the West Bank and Gaza, with the Gaza Strip designated as Corpus Separatum under the collective Confederation’s sovereignty.  
	•	Specific security protocols will be developed in consultation with Confederation members to address the unique security challenges in these regions.  
	2\.	Economic Development and Humanitarian Aid:  
	•	The Confederation will facilitate and oversee economic development initiatives in the West Bank and Gaza to improve living conditions and economic opportunities.  
	•	Special attention will be given to humanitarian aid in Gaza, particularly for rebuilding infrastructure, healthcare, and education.  
	3\.	Border Management:  
	•	The Confederation will assist in managing and monitoring border crossings to ensure the safe and regulated movement of people and goods, while respecting security concerns.  
	4\.	Cultural and Social Cohesion:  
	•	Efforts will be made to promote cultural and social cohesion within these regions, including initiatives to bridge divides between different communities.  
	5\.	Environmental and Resource Management:  
	•	The Confederation will support projects aimed at environmental sustainability and efficient resource management, particularly water resources and agricultural development.  
	6\.	Local Governance and Civil Society Engagement:  
	•	The Confederation will work with local governance structures in both regions to ensure that their needs and concerns are adequately represented and addressed.  
	•	Civil society organizations in the West Bank and Gaza will be encouraged and supported to participate in peacebuilding and community development activities.  
	7\.	Education and Employment Initiatives:  
	•	Special programs will be launched focusing on education and employment, especially targeting youth in the West Bank and Gaza, to foster a sense of hope and opportunity.  
	8\.	Monitoring and Reporting:  
	•	Regular monitoring and reporting mechanisms will be established to assess the situation in the West Bank and Gaza, ensuring timely responses to any emerging challenges.

**Article 14: Commitment to a Final Status Agreement for the Palestinian State**  
	1\.	Objective:  
	•	The Confederation reaffirms the commitment to achieving a final status agreement that recognizes the establishment of a sovereign Palestinian state, living in peace alongside Israel.  
	2\.	Negotiation Framework:  
	•	The Confederation will facilitate and support negotiations between Israel and Palestine aimed at reaching a final status agreement. This will include identifying and addressing key issues such as borders, security arrangements, the status of Jerusalem, refugees, and settlements.  
	3\.	International Involvement:  
	•	The Confederation will seek the involvement and support of the international community, including the United Nations, to assist in the negotiation process and to ensure that the final status agreement aligns with international law and resolutions.  
	4\.	Timelines and Milestones:  
	•	The Confederation will work with both parties to establish realistic timelines and milestones for the negotiation process, ensuring steady progress towards the final agreement.  
	5\.	Transparency and Inclusivity:  
	•	All negotiations will be conducted with a high degree of transparency and inclusivity, ensuring that a wide range of voices and perspectives from both Israeli and Palestinian societies are heard and considered.  
	6\.	Confidence-Building Measures:  
	•	The Confederation will encourage and facilitate confidence-building measures between the two parties to foster trust and create a conducive environment for productive negotiations.  
	7\.	Public Engagement and Support:  
	•	The Confederation will engage in public diplomacy efforts to build support for the final status agreement within both Israeli and Palestinian societies, highlighting the benefits of peace and the importance of a two-state solution.  
	8\.	Monitoring and Evaluation:  
	•	Regular monitoring and evaluation mechanisms will be established to assess the progress of negotiations and to make adjustments as necessary to ensure the successful conclusion of a final status agreement.

**Article 15: Promotion of Judeo-Islamic Tradition through Religious Consultation and New Practices**  
	1\.	Consultation with Religious Authorities:  
	•	The Confederation will facilitate regular consultations with leading Jewish and Islamic religious authorities to explore avenues for mutual understanding and respect based on shared traditions and values.
