	•	These consultations will aim to identify common ground and shared historical narratives that can foster a sense of kinship between the two faiths.  
	2\.	Development of New Religious Practices:  
	•	Based on the outcomes of these consultations, the Confederation will support the development of new religious practices or the revitalization of historical ones that embody the principles of the Judeo-Islamic tradition.  
	•	Special emphasis will be placed on practices that can be incorporated into communal and individual religious life, promoting peace and coexistence.  
	3\.	Educational Programs:  
	•	The Confederation will collaborate with religious and educational institutions to introduce programs that educate about the shared heritage and values of Judaism and Islam.  
	•	These educational initiatives will target all age groups, with a focus on young people, to build a foundation of mutual respect from an early age.  
	4\.	Cultural and Interfaith Events:  
	•	The Confederation will sponsor cultural events, workshops, and interfaith dialogues that highlight the Judeo-Islamic tradition.  
	•	These events will serve as platforms for deeper engagement and understanding between Jewish and Muslim communities.  
	5\.	Public Awareness Campaigns:  
	•	Launch public awareness campaigns to promote the values and teachings of the Judeo-Islamic tradition, emphasizing themes of peace, tolerance, and coexistence.  
	6\.	Support for Religious Leaders:  
	•	Provide support and resources to religious leaders who are actively working to bridge communities and promote the Judeo-Islamic tradition.  
	7\.	Monitoring and Evaluation:  
	•	Regularly assess the impact of these initiatives on community relations and adjust strategies as needed to enhance their effectiveness.

**Article 16: Promotion of the Abrahamic Tradition**  
	1\.	Interfaith Harmony: The Confederation commits to fostering an environment of interfaith harmony and mutual respect among the Abrahamic traditions, recognizing their shared values and historical connections.  
	2\.	Educational Initiatives: Implement educational programs and curricula that highlight the commonalities and respect the differences between the Abrahamic traditions, aiming to reduce misconceptions and promote understanding.  
	3\.	Cultural and Religious Dialogue: Encourage and support dialogue among religious leaders, scholars, and community members from the Jewish, Christian, and Islamic communities to discuss shared concerns and promote peace.  
	4\.	Interfaith Celebrations and Observances: Promote and support the observance of interfaith celebrations and events that recognize the significance of each tradition and foster a sense of community and mutual appreciation.  
	5\.	Preservation of Religious Heritage: Work towards the preservation and appreciation of religious sites, artifacts, and traditions that are significant to the Abrahamic traditions, ensuring access and respect for all.  
	6\.	Collaborative Community Service Projects: Encourage and facilitate collaborative service projects that bring together individuals from the Jewish, Christian, and Islamic communities to work on common goals and serve the wider community.  
	7\.	Promotion of Peaceful Coexistence: Advocate for and implement policies that promote peaceful coexistence and mutual respect among followers of the Abrahamic traditions within the Confederation.

**Article 17: Involuntary Displacement Provision under War Duress**  
1\. Recognition of the Circumstances of Displacement:  
	•	The Confederation recognizes that the current displacement of individuals and communities is a direct consequence of the ongoing conflict and war conditions. This recognition underscores the extraordinary nature of the decision to leave one’s home, emphasizing that such decisions are made under extreme duress and uncertainty.

2\. Prioritization of Safety and Human Rights:  
	•	In implementing displacement policies, the foremost priority shall be the safety and well-being of affected individuals. All actions will strictly adhere to international humanitarian and human rights laws, ensuring that the dignity and rights of displaced persons are respected and protected under these trying circumstances.

3\. Involuntary Decision-Making in Context:  
	•	It is acknowledged that decisions made by individuals to leave the Gaza Strip are fundamentally involuntary and represent a form of Forced Population Transfer.

4\. Support and Assistance for the Displaced:  
	•	Comprehensive support will be provided to individuals who decide to leave, including but not limited to financial assistance, legal aid, psychological support, and assistance with relocation logistics. This support aims to mitigate the hardships faced during displacement and facilitate a dignified transition to new circumstances.

5\. Protection of Property and Legal Rights:  
	•	The legal and property rights of displaced individuals will be rigorously protected. Measures will be implemented to allow them to manage their property from afar, including options to sell, lease, or retain ownership as appropriate.

6\. Monitoring and Transparency:  
	•	An independent monitoring body will oversee the displacement process to ensure its transparency and fairness. This body will also be responsible for safeguarding the rights of displaced individuals, addressing grievances, and ensuring adherence to international standards.

7\. Provision for Resettlement and International Cooperation:  
	•	The Confederation will collaborate with international partners to secure humane and viable resettlement options. This includes potential relocation to other countries, where necessary, with an emphasis on ensuring the social, cultural, and economic integration of displaced individuals.

8\. Defined Timeframe and Review:  
	•	The involuntary displacement policy will have a clearly defined timeframe, with regular reviews to assess its impact and effectiveness. These reviews will consider the evolving situation, the well-being of displaced persons, and compliance with legal and ethical standards.

9\. Reintegration and Support for Return:  
	•	For individuals who choose to return once conditions stabilize, the Confederation will facilitate and support their reintegration. This includes logistical support for return, rebuilding efforts, and programs designed to foster communal harmony and reconciliation.

10\. Emphasis on Restoration and Future Stability:  
	•	While recognizing the necessity of displacement under war duress, the Confederation is committed to the future restoration of communities and the establishment of conditions conducive to long-term stability. Efforts will be made to address the root causes of displacement and to create an environment where displaced persons can voluntarily and safely return to their homes, should they choose to do so.

**Article 18: Acknowledgment of the Injustices of the 1947 UN Partition Plan**  
	  
1\.	Recognition of Historical Context:  
	•	The Confederation acknowledges the historical context surrounding the 1947 UN Partition Plan for Palestine, recognizing that while it was imperative to settle the highly persecuted Jewish Diaspora, fundamental injustices exist towards the Palestinian people, which have contributed to ongoing conflicts and disputes.

	2\.	Inadequacies of the Plan:  
	•	Identifies that the 1947 Partition Plan could never address the complexities of demographic distributions, cultural and religious connections to the land, and naturally ensured the conflicts that would arise from its implementation.  
	

3\.	Impact on Subsequent Developments:  
	•	Notes that the imposition of the plan have had lasting impacts, contributing to the displacement of populations, the emergence of conflict, and the enduring struggle for peace in the region.  
	  
4\.	Learning from the Past:  
	•	Emphasizes the importance of learning from the shortcomings of the 1947 Partition Plan in any current and future efforts to resolve the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, ensuring that all parties’ concerns are more comprehensively and empathetically validated.  
	  
5\.	Commitment to a Just and Sustainable Solution:  
	•	Reaffirms the Confederation’s commitment to seeking a just and sustainable solution to the Israeli-Palestinian conflict that acknowledges past errors and is based on mutual respect, recognition, and the rights of all people in the region.

**Article 19: Establishment of the Confederation Waqf**

**Section 1: Purpose and Scope**

1.1 The Canaan Confederation Waqf (hereafter referred to as "the Waqf") shall be established as a perpetual endowment to support the religious, educational, cultural, and humanitarian activities within the Canaan Confederation.

1.2 The Waqf shall serve as a vehicle for fostering interfaith harmony, preserving heritage sites, and promoting sustainable development in accordance with the principles of the Confederation.

**Section 2: Governance**

2.1 The Waqf shall be governed by a Board of Trustees composed of representatives from the core member states of the Confederation.

2.2 The Board of Trustees shall include scholars, religious leaders, and experts in various fields to ensure diverse and comprehensive oversight.

2.3 The Board shall be responsible for the management, investment, and distribution of the Waqf’s resources, ensuring they are used in alignment with its founding principles.

**Section 3: Funding and Contributions**

3.1 Initial funding for the Waqf shall come from member state contributions, international donations, and grants from global organizations committed to peace and development.

3.2 The Waqf shall be open to voluntary contributions from individuals, corporations, and other entities supportive of its mission.

**Section 4: Activities and Projects**

4.1 The Waqf shall fund projects that promote rebuilding the Gaza Strip, interfaith dialogue, cultural preservation, educational initiatives, and humanitarian aid within the Confederation’s jurisdiction.

4.2 Specific projects may include the restoration of religious and cultural sites, scholarships for students, community development programs, and emergency relief efforts.

**Section 5: Transparency and Accountability**

5.1 The Waqf shall operate with full transparency, providing regular reports on its activities, finances, and impact to the Confederation Council and the public.

5.2 Independent audits shall be conducted annually to ensure accountability and proper use of funds.

**Section 6: Legal Status**

6.1 The Waqf shall be recognized as a legal entity within the Confederation, with the ability to enter into contracts, hold assets, and undertake legal actions as necessary to fulfill its mission.

**Section 7: Amendments**

7.1 Amendments to this Article may be proposed by the Board of Trustees and must be approved by a two-thirds majority of the Confederation Council.

**Article 20: Land Lease Scheme as a Bridging Mechanism for Land Disputes**

1. **Purpose and Objectives:**  
   * The Land Lease Scheme aims to provide a temporary and pragmatic solution to the underlying land disputes between the Israeli and Palestinian Nations of the land of Canaan, enhancing security, combating extremism, and establishing defensible borders while longer-term agreements are negotiated.  
2. **Framework and Negotiation:**  
   * The governing nations of the Confederation will negotiate the terms and conditions of the land lease scheme.  
   * The negotiations will focus on identifying specific areas suitable for leasing, the duration of leases, compensation mechanisms, and usage rights.  
   * Both parties will agree on transparent and equitable criteria for selecting and managing leased lands based on the 1947 UN Partition Plan allocations.  
3. **Historical Allocations:**  
   * According to the 1947 UN Partition Plan, approximately 56% of the land was allocated to the Jewish state (Israel) and about 42% to the Arab state (Palestine).   
   * The land lease scheme will take these historical allocations into account, rounding the land distribution to approximately 55%-45%, ensuring that leasing agreements approximately reflect the original intent of the partition.  
4. **Implementation and Management:**  
   * A joint Land Lease Management Authority (LLMA) will be established to oversee the implementation and management of the land lease scheme.  
   * The LLMA will be composed of equal representation from Israeli and Palestinian authorities, along with neutral international experts to ensure impartiality.  
   * The LLMA will be responsible for administering leases, resolving disputes, and ensuring compliance with the agreed terms.  
5. **Security and Defensible Borders:**  
   * Leases will be strategically designed to enhance the security of both Israel and Palestine, creating defensible borders that reduce the risk of conflict.  
   * The LLMA will work closely with security experts to ensure that leased lands contribute to the overall stability and safety of the region.  
   * Security arrangements will include monitoring and patrols to prevent unauthorized activities and ensure compliance with lease terms.  
6. **Lease Terms and Conditions:**  
   * Leases will be granted for a fixed term, with provisions for renewal based on mutual agreement and evaluation of the lease’s impact.  
   * The terms will include specific guidelines on the permissible use of leased lands, ensuring that activities align with the agreed purposes such as residential development, agriculture, or commercial enterprises.  
   * Compensation for leased lands will be fair and transparent, with payment structures benefiting the rightful landowners and supporting community development.  
7. **Economic and Social Benefits:**  
   * The land lease scheme aims to stimulate economic growth by providing opportunities for investment, development, and job creation in leased areas.  
   * Revenue generated from leases will be invested in local infrastructure, education, and social services, benefiting communities on both sides.  
   * The scheme will promote cross-border cooperation and interaction, fostering better relations and understanding between Israelis and Palestinians.  
8. **Legal and Regulatory Framework:**  
   * The LLMA will develop a comprehensive legal and regulatory framework to govern the land lease scheme, ensuring compliance with both Israeli and Palestinian laws, as well as international standards.  
   * The framework will include dispute resolution mechanisms to address conflicts arising from lease agreements and land use.  
9. **Monitoring and Evaluation:**  
   * The effectiveness of the land lease scheme will be regularly monitored and evaluated by the LLMA, with periodic reports submitted to the governing council and made available to the public.  
   * Independent reviews will be conducted to assess the scheme’s impact on resolving land disputes, economic development, and social cohesion.  
10. **Public Participation and Transparency:**  
    * The LLMA will ensure transparency in its operations, providing regular updates and maintaining open communication channels with the public.  
    * Public consultations will be held to gather input from affected communities, ensuring that their concerns and suggestions are considered in the decision-making process.  
11. **Commitment to Long-Term Resolution:**  
    * The land lease scheme is intended as a bridging mechanism while permanent solutions to land disputes are pursued.  
    * Both parties reaffirm their commitment to continue negotiations for a comprehensive and lasting resolution to the land disputes, using the lessons learned and foundations built through the land lease scheme.

**Article 21: U.S.-Sponsored Canaan Confederation Peacekeeping Force**

1. **Purpose and Objectives:**  
   * The U.S.-Sponsored Canaan Confederation Peacekeeping Force (CCPF) is established to maintain peace and security within the Confederation, prevent hostilities, and support the enforcement of Confederation agreements.  
2. **Composition and Structure:**  
   * The CCPF will be composed of military and security personnel contributed by member states of the Confederation, initially formed by the Palestinian Authority and other participating nations, with significant support and oversight from the United States.  
   * The force will be organized into units specializing in various aspects of peacekeeping, including monitoring, patrols, conflict resolution, and emergency response.  
3. **Command and Control:**  
   * The CCPF will operate under the command of a Joint Command Council (JCC), which includes representatives from Israel, Palestine, the United States, and other member states.  
   * The United States will play a leading role in strategic planning, operational oversight, and coordination with local authorities and international bodies.  
4. **Rules of Engagement:**  
   * The rules of engagement for the CCPF will be clearly defined and approved by the governing council of the Confederation, in consultation with the United States.  
   * These rules will prioritize the protection of civilians, respect for human rights, and the use of force only when necessary to maintain peace and security.  
5. **Operational Mandate:**  
   * The CCPF will conduct peacekeeping operations, including border security, monitoring ceasefires, and preventing unauthorized activities.  
   * The force will also provide rapid response to emerging threats, support humanitarian missions, and assist in the implementation of Confederation policies.  
6. **Training and Capacity Building:**  
   * Comprehensive training programs will be established for CCPF personnel, focusing on peacekeeping operations, conflict resolution, cultural sensitivity, and human rights, with significant involvement from U.S. military and security experts.  
   * Joint training exercises with local security forces, U.S. forces, and international peacekeeping bodies will be conducted to ensure interoperability and effectiveness.  
7. **Funding and Resources:**  
   * The CCPF will be primarily funded through contributions from the United States, supplemented by member states and international organizations committed to supporting peace and security in the region.  
   * Adequate resources will be allocated to ensure the force's operational readiness, including equipment, logistics, and support services, with substantial U.S. assistance.  
8. **Legal and Regulatory Framework:**  
   * The CCPF will operate within a legal framework established by the governing council, ensuring compliance with international law, human rights standards, and the legal frameworks of Israel and Palestine, with oversight from U.S. legal experts.  
   * Mechanisms for accountability and oversight will be in place to address misconduct and ensure adherence to the rules of engagement.  
9. **Monitoring and Reporting:**  
   * Regular monitoring and reporting mechanisms will be established to assess the performance and impact of the CCPF.  
   * Reports on CCPF activities, challenges, and successes will be submitted to the governing council and the United States, and made available to the public to ensure transparency and accountability.  
10. **Community Engagement:**  
    * The CCPF will engage with local communities to build trust, gather intelligence, and address concerns related to security and peacekeeping operations.  
    * Community outreach programs will be developed to foster cooperation and support for CCPF initiatives.  
11. **Commitment to Peace and Stability:**  
    * The CCPF is committed to upholding the principles of the Confederation, promoting peace, stability, and cooperation among member states.  
    * The force, with strong U.S. support, will work diligently to create a secure environment conducive to dialogue, development, and long-term peace in the region.

**Article 22: Constitution of Haram al-Sharif/Temple Mount**

1. **Purpose and Objectives:**  
   * This article establishes the framework for developing a constitution for the Al-Aqsa Mosque and Temple Mount, inspired by the principles of the Constitution of Medina.  
   * The primary goal is to formalize the Judeo-Islamic tradition and enshrine the current status quo, while striving towards the eventual realization of Isaiah 56:7, which envisions the complex as a house of prayer for all nations.  
2. **Historical and Religious Significance:**  
   * Recognizing the profound historical and religious significance of Al-Aqsa Mosque and Temple Mount to both Muslims and Jews, this constitution aims to promote mutual respect and coexistence.  
   * The Constitution of Medina serves as a historical precedent for creating a framework that respects the rights and practices of diverse religious communities.  
3. **Development Process:**  
   * A Constitutional Committee will be established, composed of representatives from Islamic and Jewish religious authorities, local and international legal experts, community leaders, and the Jordanian Waqf.  
   * The committee will draft the constitution through a collaborative and inclusive process, ensuring input from all stakeholders.  
4. **Guiding Principles:**  
   * The constitution will be guided by the principles of the Constitution of Medina, emphasizing coexistence, mutual respect, and the protection of religious practices.  
   * It will also incorporate the vision of Isaiah 56:7, which aspires to make the complex a shared space for worship for all people.  
5. **Current Status Quo:**  
   * The constitution will enshrine the current status quo regarding religious practices and access to Al-Aqsa Mosque and Temple Mount.  
   * It will ensure that the rights and responsibilities of both Islamic and Jewish communities are clearly defined and respected.  
6. **Governance and Administration:**  
   * A Joint Religious Council (JRC) will be established to oversee the administration of Al-Aqsa Mosque and Temple Mount, led by the Jordanian Waqf.  
   * The JRC will include representatives from the Jordanian Waqf, Islamic and Jewish religious authorities, and neutral international observers.  
   * The council will be responsible for managing daily operations, resolving disputes, and ensuring compliance with the constitution.  
7. **Security and Preservation:**  
   * The constitution will include provisions for the security and preservation of the complex, ensuring that it remains a safe and accessible place for worship for all.  
   * Security measures will be implemented in coordination with local and international authorities to protect the site and its visitors.  
8. **Promotion of Judeo-Islamic Tradition:**  
   * The constitution will mark the formal establishment of the Judeo-Islamic tradition, promoting shared values and mutual understanding between the two faiths.  
   * Educational and cultural programs will be developed to highlight the shared heritage and foster respect and cooperation.  
9. **Implementation of Isaiah 56:7:**  
   * While enshrining the current status quo, the constitution will outline a gradual and respectful approach towards the eventual implementation of Isaiah 56:7.  
   * Steps will be taken to create an inclusive environment where people of all faiths can pray and worship, in line with the vision of a house of prayer for all nations.  
10. **Legal and Regulatory Framework:**  
    * The constitution will be developed within the legal frameworks of Israel and Palestine, ensuring compliance with international law and human rights standards.  
    * Mechanisms for accountability and oversight will be established to address any violations and ensure the integrity of the constitution.  
11. **Monitoring and Evaluation:**  
    * The implementation and impact of the constitution will be regularly monitored and evaluated by the Joint Religious Council.  
    * Reports on the progress and challenges will be submitted to the governing bodies of the Confederation and made available to the public.  
12. **Commitment to Peace and Coexistence:**  
    * The constitution will reaffirm the commitment of all parties to peace, coexistence, and mutual respect.  
    * It will serve as a symbol of hope and a practical step towards resolving one of the most sensitive aspects of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict.

**Article 23: Commitment to the Reconstruction of Gaza as the Virtuous City**

1. **Islamic Golden Age Inspiration**: The Canaan Confederation envisions the Virtuous City of Gaza as a beacon of hope, renewal, and intellectual flourishing. Inspired by the principles of Al-Farabi and the illustrious history of cities like Al-Andalus and Baghdad during the Islamic Golden Age, Gaza will be transformed into a global city where leaders and scholars from around the world come to learn, collaborate, and innovate.  
2. **Purpose**: The Virtuous City of Gaza aims to foster virtue among its residents and visitors, promoting values of peace, knowledge, and cooperation. It will serve as the crown jewel of the Middle East, representing the broader Arab and Islamic world, and the entire Global South.  
3. **Global Significance:** This city will be a symbol of the continuation of the Islamic revival, bridging the gap between the Western and Islamic worlds. It will host international leaders, scholars, and innovators, becoming a hub for dialogue, learning, and cultural exchange.  
4. **Al-Farabi’s Principles**:  
   * **Rational Governance**: Establish governance led by individuals who embody reason and wisdom, ensuring that policies are rational and just.  
   * **Moral and Ethical Development**: Encourage citizens to cultivate moral and ethical virtues, contributing to the overall harmony and well-being of society.  
   * **Education and Knowledge**: Prioritize education and intellectual development, ensuring a well-educated populace that can sustain a virtuous society.  
   * **Social Harmony and Cooperation**: Promote social cohesion and cooperation, where individuals support each other in their pursuit of virtue.  
   * **Justice and Equity**: Ensure that laws are fair and just, providing equal opportunities for all citizens to thrive.  
   * **Spiritual and Material Well-being**: Address both the spiritual and material needs of citizens, ensuring a balanced approach to well-being.  
5. **Commitment to Virtue**: The Virtuous City of Gaza will promote the principles of virtue as articulated by Al-Farabi, focusing on ethical governance, the pursuit of knowledge, and the well-being of its inhabitants. Residents and visitors will be encouraged to engage in activities that foster moral and intellectual growth, contributing to the city’s reputation as a center of excellence.  
6. **Quality Infrastructure and Services**: Develop safe, affordable housing, modern urban infrastructure, healthcare facilities, educational institutions, and cultural centers to foster a vibrant, harmonious, and prosperous community.  
7. **Legacy and Impact**: The Virtuous City of Gaza will stand as a symbol of hope and renewal, proving that from the greatest trials can come the most profound transformations. It will not only be a place of refuge and learning but also a testament to the human spirit’s resilience. By drawing on the rich history of the Islamic Golden Age and the vision of philosophers like Al-Farabi, the Virtuous City of Gaza will stand as a testament to the enduring values of the Islamic civilization.

**Article 24: Establishment of the New House of Wisdom**

1. **Purpose**: The Canaan Confederation hereby establishes the New House of Wisdom, signifying a beacon of learning, dialogue, and innovation. This institution will be dedicated to fostering academic and cultural exchanges among the diverse populations of the Confederation, enhancing mutual understanding, and contributing to the global body of knowledge.  
2. **Location**: The New House of Wisdom will be located in the Virtuous City of Gaza, symbolizing the renewal and hope of the region. It will serve as a central hub for scholars, researchers, and thought leaders from around the world.  
3. **Objectives**:  
   * **Cultural Integration**: To promote the integration of diverse cultural heritages, emphasizing the shared histories and values within the Canaan Confederation.  
   * **Educational Excellence**: To provide world-class facilities and resources for research in the sciences, humanities, and arts, inviting collaboration across geopolitical and disciplinary boundaries.  
   * **Peacebuilding**: To contribute to the peace process through education and the free exchange of ideas, fostering a culture of peace and understanding among the future leaders of the region.  
4. **Governance**:  
   * The House of Wisdom will be governed by a council composed of representatives from each member state of the Canaan Confederation, ensuring equitable management and operation.  
   * The council will oversee the creation of curricula, the invitation of scholars, and the establishment of research priorities in alignment with the goals of the Confederation.  
5. **Funding**:  
   * The construction and operational costs of the House of Wisdom will be funded by contributions from member states of the Canaan Confederation and supported by international donors who wish to invest in the future stability and prosperity of the region.  
   * A special fund will be established to support scholarships and research grants for students and scholars from economically disadvantaged backgrounds within the Confederation.  
6. **Programs and Activities**:  
   * The House of Wisdom will host annual conferences, workshops, and symposiums that address key issues facing the region and the world, including peace and security, sustainable development, and intercultural dialogue.  
   * It will also house permanent and temporary exhibitions that showcase the cultural and scientific contributions of the Middle East and broader Islamic and Jewish civilizations, drawing parallels and building on historical successes such as those seen in Al-Andalus and other centers of learning during the Islamic Golden Age.  
7. **Commitment to Accessibility**:  
   * The New House of Wisdom will be accessible to all individuals, regardless of nationality or religion, and will strive to remove barriers to entry for all participants, ensuring it acts as a true house of knowledge and bridge-building.  
8. **Legacy and Vision**:  
   * By reviving the spirit of the original House of Wisdom in Baghdad, this new institution will stand as a testament to the region's commitment to scholarship and peace. It will aim to replicate and surpass the achievements of historical intellectual centers, propelling the region into a new era of enlightenmen

**Article 25: The Role of the Benevolent Advisor for Life (BAL)[^7]**

* **Purpose**: The BAL is established to provide visionary guidance and strategic advice to the Canaan Confederation, ensuring the long-term alignment of its policies with the founding principles of the peace plan. This role prioritizes autonomy and minimal oversight to foster innovative and independent decision-making.  
* **Appointment**: The author of the peace plan will assume the role of BAL, acknowledging their unique understanding and commitment to the Confederation’s success. This direct appointment highlights the *burden* of consistent and visionary leadership.  
* **Responsibilities and Scope**: The BAL will advise on key strategic decisions, including policy directions, conflict resolution, and long-term planning. The advice will be based on a deep understanding of the region’s complexities and strategic needs of the Confederation.  
* **Immunity from Prosecution**: The BAL is granted complete immunity from prosecution by nations of the Confederation for any actions performed in good faith while executing duties within the scope of their official role as advisor. This comprehensive immunity is designed to protect the BAL from any legal liability arising from their efforts to guide and influence the Confederation's strategies and policies.  
* **Scope of Immunity**: This immunity extends to all decisions and actions undertaken in good faith that relate to the BAL's official functions. Additionally, it includes actions taken to maintain the BAL's physical, mental, and emotional wellbeing, acknowledging that the BAL’s ability to perform their role effectively is directly tied to their overall health.  
* **Exclusions**: While the BAL enjoys broad immunity, it does not extend to actions that constitute gross criminal misconduct, or are undertaken in bad faith.  
* **Privacy and Autonomy**: The BAL retains the right to privacy and substantial autonomy in their advisory role. Regular, detailed reporting is not required; instead, the BAL will provide high-level summaries at their discretion, focusing on major strategic advice and decisions.  
* **Review and Oversight**: Oversight will be minimal, with an independent review scheduled every five years. This review will be non-intrusive and limited to ensuring that the BAL's guidance aligns with the Confederation's overarching goals and principles. The review process will respect the autonomy and unique position of the BAL.  
* **Term and Succession**: The role of the BAL is held for life, emphasizing the enduring commitment required. Succession to the role will be based on merit and demonstrated commitment to the Confederation’s principles, particularly a lifelong dedication to peace and stability.  
* **Part-Time Compensation**: In recognition of the part-time engagement of the BAL, a modest salary will be provided. This salary is to be funded through contributions from the member nations of the Canaan Confederation, reflecting their collective investment in the stability and success of the peace initiatives.   
* **Adjustment and Review**: The specifics regarding the amount and distribution of the salary will remain flexible and subject to periodic review based on the evolving needs of the Confederation and the duties expected from the BAL. The salary shall be pegged to the inflation of the U.S. dollar to ensure that the compensation retains its value over time and remains fair and adequate in relation to global economic conditions.

# Appendix B: Draft Proposal for the Vision of the Virtuous City of Gaza {#appendix-b:-draft-proposal-for-the-vision-of-the-virtuous-city-of-gaza}

**Preamble**

Inspired by the illustrious heritage of the Islamic Golden Age, where the Judeo-Islamic tradition reached its zenith, we envision the Virtuous City of Gaza as a global center of learning and cultural exchange. This city, rising from the rubble of the Israel-Hamas War, aims to be a new crown jewel of the Middle East, symbolizing the unity and intellectual resurgence of the broader Arab and Islamic world, as well as the entire Global South. The Virtuous City of Gaza will serve as a continuation of the Islamic revival, bridging the Western and Islamic worlds and embodying the principles of virtue and enlightenment envisioned by the great philosopher Al-Farabi.

**Article 1: Vision and Mission**

In Al-Farabi's conception of the virtuous city, key values such as Hikmah (wisdom), ‘Adl (justice), and Fadila (virtue) are foundational. The city is governed by a leader who embodies philosophical depth and practical wisdom, steering the community toward a harmonious existence where each individual’s well-being is intricately linked to the collective good. Justice ensures equity and order, while the cultivation of moral and intellectual virtues allows individuals to attain true Sa‘adah (happiness). Education is crucial, nurturing Ilm (knowledge) and moral integrity among the citizens. Unity and harmony are central, ensuring that the community's interests supersede personal desires. These core values, supported by religious and ethical teachings, foster a society aimed at the perfection of the soul and communal prosperity.

The Virtuous City of Gaza will be established as a global city dedicated to fostering virtue, knowledge, and cultural exchange. It will be a place where world leaders, scholars, and citizens from diverse backgrounds come together to learn, collaborate, and innovate. Drawing inspiration from Al-Farabi’s vision of integration of Greco-Roman values, the city will prioritize the cultivation of virtuous citizens who contribute to the common good.

**Article 2: Educational and Cultural Hub**

1. **House of Wisdom**: A modern House of Wisdom will be constructed, mirroring the spirit of Baghdad’s renowned Bayt al-Hikma. This institution will be a center for advanced learning and research, attracting scholars from around the world to study and teach various disciplines, including science, technology, humanities, and the arts.  
2. **Global Leadership Institute**: Establish an institute where future leaders from the Islamic world and beyond can receive training in governance, diplomacy, and ethics, ensuring that they are equipped to lead with wisdom and integrity.  
3. **Cultural Heritage Center**: A center dedicated to celebrating and preserving the rich cultural heritage of the Islamic Golden Age, featuring exhibitions on Al-Andalus, the libraries of Timbuktu, the Timurid Renaissance, and more.

**Article 3: Sustainable Development and Technological Innovation**

1. **Tech and Innovation Park**: Develop a state-of-the-art technology park to attract global tech companies and startups, fostering innovation and economic growth. This park will promote collaboration between local and international enterprises, driving advancements in various fields.  
2. **Sustainable Development Initiatives**: Implement sustainable urban development projects, including green energy solutions, eco-friendly infrastructure, and waste management systems, setting a benchmark for environmental stewardship.  
3. **Infrastructure**: Rebuild Gaza with cutting-edge infrastructure that supports both local needs and global interactions, making it a hub for international conferences and collaborations.

**Article 4: Interfaith and International Relations**

1. **Interfaith Dialogue Center**: Establish a center for interfaith dialogue, promoting understanding and cooperation between different religious communities. This center will host regular conferences, workshops, and events aimed at fostering peace and mutual respect.  
2. **International Collaborations**: Forge partnerships with leading universities, research institutions, and cultural organizations worldwide, creating a network of collaborators committed to the vision of the Virtuous City.

**Article 5: Governance and Administration**

1. **Inclusive Governance**: Ensure that the governance of the Virtuous City is inclusive, transparent, and participatory, involving representatives from various sectors of society, including academia, business, and civil society.  
2. **Security and Stability**: Work closely with international peacekeeping forces and local security agencies to ensure the safety and stability of the city, creating an environment where residents and visitors can thrive.  
3. **International Guarantees**: Secure international guarantees to protect the Virtuous City from future destruction, ensuring that it remains a safe haven for its residents and visitors.  
4. **Peacekeepers**: Deploy peacekeeping forces from the Canaan Confederation to maintain security and stability, preventing conflicts and ensuring the city's development continues unimpeded.

**Article 6: Funding and Resources**

1. **International Fund for Gaza’s Reconstruction**: Leverage the Canaan Confederation Waqf to support the reconstruction and development of Gaza, encouraging contributions from governments, philanthropic organizations, and private sector entities.  
2. **Resource Allocation**: Prioritize the allocation of resources towards education, healthcare, and infrastructure, ensuring that the needs of the population are met and the city can flourish.

**Conclusion**

The Virtuous City of Gaza represents a bold vision for the future, drawing on the rich heritage of Islamic civilization and aiming to create a beacon of hope and progress in the Middle East. It will stand as a testament to the enduring values of knowledge, virtue, and collaboration, inspiring generations to come. By building this city, we honor the past, address the present challenges, and pave the way for a brighter, more harmonious future.

# Appendix C: Draft Proposal for the Modern House of Wisdom in The Virtuous City of Gaza {#appendix-c:-draft-proposal-for-the-modern-house-of-wisdom-in-the-virtuous-city-of-gaza}

**Introduction:**

The Modern House of Wisdom, strategically planned in the newly envisioned Virtuous City of Gaza, represents a cornerstone in the comprehensive rebuilding of Gaza City. This institution is not merely an educational facility but a vital response to the historical trajectory that has shaped the current state of the Islamic world, particularly in the context of Palestine. The decline in intellectualism within the Islamic world—a decline that contributed to the vulnerability and eventual loss of Palestine—serves as a critical reminder of the importance of fostering knowledge and innovation. The Modern House of Wisdom is designed to transform Gaza into a global hub of enlightenment and innovation, rekindling the spirit of the Islamic Golden Age to foster regional stability and prosperity.

**Context and Historical Necessity:**

During the Islamic Golden Age, spanning from the 8th to the 14th century, Muslim scholars made remarkable contributions to science, philosophy, medicine, and the arts, positioning the Islamic world at the forefront of global intellectual leadership. However, over time, a shift away from this intellectual openness occurred. Influential figures like Al-Ghazali harshly critiqued the integration of Greek philosophy into Islamic thought, emphasizing faith over reason. This shift, coupled with the banning of the printing press in much of the Islamic world, led to a narrowing of intellectual pursuits and a decline in scientific, philosophical, and technological advancements.

This intellectual retreat had far-reaching consequences, weakening the Islamic world and making it more vulnerable to external pressures. By the 19th and early 20th centuries, the decline was evident in the Ottoman Empire, which controlled Palestine. The empire's inability to modernize and its internal decay made it susceptible to European intervention, culminating in the loss of Palestine. The creation of the state of Israel in 1948 was the result of a broader narrative of decline within the Islamic world, underscoring the critical importance of liberal education in preserving a civilization's influence and territorial integrity.

The vision for the Modern House of Wisdom in the rebuilt Gaza Strip is a direct response to these lessons from history. It aims to revive the spirit of the Islamic Golden Age by providing a liberal education that balances faith and reason, fosters intellectual curiosity, and embraces technological advancements.

**Mission Statement:**

To establish a world-class secular center of learning that promotes critical thinking, creativity, pluralism, and freedom of thought and expression, serving as an essential pillar in the socio-economic regeneration of Gaza and beyond.

Objectives:

* **Educational Excellence:** Deliver a broad spectrum of cutting-edge academic programs focusing on sustainable development, peace studies, and technological innovation, tailored to empower the next generation of leaders.  
* **Cultural Renaissance:** Act as a dynamic forum for cultural revival and intellectual exchange, preserving and promoting the rich heritage of the region while embracing global cultural diversity.  
* **Strategic Rebuilding:** Position the institution as a central player in the broader strategy to reconstruct Gaza as the Virtuous City, symbolizing hope and renewal for the Palestinian people and the international community.

**Architectural Vision:**

Reflecting the fusion of historical inspiration and sustainable innovation, the architectural design of the Modern House of Wisdom will serve as a landmark in the Virtuous City of Gaza. The facility will be constructed using eco-friendly materials and technologies, exemplifying a commitment to environmental stewardship and resilience.

**Impact:**

* **Educational and Economic Catalyst:** Propel economic revitalization in Gaza through education-led development, job creation, and international investments.  
* **Cultural and Social Harmony:** Foster social cohesion and intercultural understanding, positioning Gaza as a model of multicultural coexistence and peace.  
* **Symbol of Resilience and Innovation:** Showcase Gaza’s transformation from a conflict zone to a flourishing center of academic and cultural excellence.

**Conclusion:**

The Modern House of Wisdom is more than an educational institution; it is a vital foundation in the ambitious project to rebuild Gaza into the Virtuous City. This initiative invites global participation from governments, academia, and international donors to invest in a future marked by peace, prosperity, and intellectual achievement. By rekindling the spirit of the Islamic Golden Age and addressing the historical intellectual decline that contributed to the loss of Palestine, the Modern House of Wisdom will stand as a beacon of hope and a catalyst for a new era of enlightenment and stability in the Middle East.

# Appendix D: The Narrowing of the Islamic Intellectual and Philosophical Traditions and the Loss of Palestine {#appendix-d:-the-narrowing-of-the-islamic-intellectual-and-philosophical-traditions-and-the-loss-of-palestine}

## ⚠️⚠️Disclaimer⚠️⚠️ {#⚠️⚠️disclaimer⚠️⚠️}

This discussion is based on interpretations of historical events and intellectual trends within the Islamic world and their potential impact on the geopolitical landscape, particularly concerning the loss of Palestine. It aims to provide insight into how shifts in intellectual focus and priorities may have influenced broader historical outcomes. However, readers should be aware that historical analysis often involves simplification of complex events and may incorporate perspectives that are subject to debate among scholars.  
The views presented here do not claim to capture the entirety of the factors at play but seek to highlight certain intellectual and technological trends that may have contributed to geopolitical shifts. The interpretation follows one perspective within the broad spectrum of historical scholarship and is not intended to diminish the role of external forces such as colonialism, global politics, and other internal dynamics that significantly shaped the region’s history.   
This appendix is part of a larger peace plan that includes both historical analysis and forward-looking proposals aimed at fostering stability and intellectual revival in the region. The inclusion of this discussion is intended to enrich our understanding of the past as a means of informing future initiatives, not to provide a definitive explanation of historical events.

## Intellectual Transitions and Their Geopolitical Impacts: A Historical Interpretation on the Loss of Palestine {#intellectual-transitions-and-their-geopolitical-impacts:-a-historical-interpretation-on-the-loss-of-palestine}

This historical interpretation delves into the profound impact of intellectual shifts within the Islamic world, changes that this author believes contributed to the eventual loss of Palestine. During the Islamic Golden Age, spanning from the 8th to the 14th century, Muslim scholars made remarkable contributions to science, philosophy, medicine, and the arts. This era was characterized by a flourishing of knowledge, with figures like Avicenna, Al-Farabi, and Averroes (Ibn Rushd) building upon and expanding Greek philosophical traditions, positioning the Islamic world at the forefront of global intellectual leadership.  
Over time, a significant shift in intellectual focus emerged. Prominent thinkers such as Al-Ghazali, with his influential work *The Incoherence of the Philosophers*, and later Ibn Taymiyyah, began to critique the integration of Greek philosophy into Islamic thought. Both were leaders in the arguement that certain philosophical ideas were incompatible with Islamic teachings, emphasizing the orthodox view of the supremacy of faith over reason. The popularity of this class of critique marked a turning point, leading to a gradual de-emphasis on the rational and empirical sciences that had thrived during the Golden Age. The focus shifted towards theology and religious jurisprudence, which, while vital, contributed to a *narrowing* of intellectual and philosophical pursuits.  
Al-Ghazali’s metaphysical arguments, particularly his critique of causality and advocacy of occasionalism, posited that the apparent cause-and-effect relationships observed in nature are not the result of inherent natural laws but rather the direct will of God. By asserting that God is the only true cause and that natural events merely occur according to divine custom, Al-Ghazali undermined the notion of consistent, discoverable natural laws that form the foundation of scientific reasoning.   
This theological determinism shifted the focus away from empirical investigation and the search for natural causes, leading to a more conservative approach to science in the Islamic world. The implications of this shift were significant: while it preserved a theological worldview, it also contributed to a relative decline in scientific innovation by diminishing the emphasis on rational inquiry and the exploration of the natural world as governed by consistent principles.  
Ibn Taymiyyah's critique of Aristotelian philosophy had a profound and dual impact on both theology and the sciences within the Islamic world. Theologically, his emphasis on the primacy of revelation over human reason reinforced a more conservative and scripturalist approach, which sought to purify Islamic thought from what he viewed as foreign philosophical influences. This shift helped solidify orthodox religious practices and doctrines, but it also contributed to a growing skepticism towards philosophical inquiry, including the natural sciences that were deeply intertwined with Aristotelian thought. As a result, while his critiques invigorated theological rigor and adherence to traditional Islamic teachings, they also played a role in the gradual decline of scientific innovation, as the intellectual focus increasingly prioritized religious scholarship over the rationalist and empirical methods that had previously driven scientific exploration in the Islamic world.  
Islam originally had a strongly rationalist sect known as the Mu’tazilites, who emphasized the compatibility of faith with reason and critical thinking. The Mu’tazilites strongly favored the use of reason in theological matters, placing it at the forefront of their interpretation of Islamic doctrine. However, over time, this sect died out, largely due to the rise of more traditional orthodox schools of thought, such as the Ash’arites. Islamic theological thought can be understood as a spectrum, with the Mu’tazilites representing one extreme that strongly preferred reason, while the Ash’arites adopted a more orthodox view that is more in line with the median perspective of the Muslim community. The Ash’arite approach, which emphasized divine omnipotence and a more literal interpretation of scripture, eventually became the dominant tradition in Sunni Islam, leaving no direct analog within the tradition that champions the same level of rationalism as the Mu’tazilites once did.  
While this historical interpretation highlights the works and influence of key figures such as Al-Ghazali and Ibn Taymiyyah, it is important to clarify that these individuals alone cannot be held solely responsible for the broad geopolitical outcomes, such as the loss of Palestine, and must be contextualized within the broader struggle of the Islamic world.  
One notable example are the Mongol invasions of the 13th century, which inflicted unparalleled devastation on the Islamic world, leaving a lasting impact that reshaped its history. The sack of Baghdad in 1258 marked the end of the Abbasid Caliphate and the destruction of one of the most significant centers of learning and culture in the medieval world.   
**Among the most tragic losses was the destruction of the House of Wisdom, a renowned institution that had been a beacon of intellectual achievement, where scholars from various cultures gathered to study and preserve knowledge in fields such as science, mathematics, astronomy, medicine, and philosophy.** The obliteration of this library, along with its countless manuscripts, represented an incalculable loss to global knowledge and culture. The political fragmentation that followed the invasions disrupted trade routes, weakened regional powers, and led to the decline of intellectual and artistic pursuits across the Islamic world. The psychological and spiritual blow of the Mongol conquest reverberated for generations, contributing to a period of stagnation and decline from which the Islamic world struggled to recover. The invasions fundamentally altered the socio-political landscape, making it more difficult for the region to unify and rebuild, thereby compounding the challenges of adapting to subsequent external pressures and internal conflicts.  
**Nevertheless, we must understand the internal decline of the Islamic world, especially its abandonment of the Greco-Islamic tradition, as this underscores the critical role of intellectual openness in a civilization's survival and progress. This turn towards orthodoxy highlights how decisions about education, knowledge, and cultural exchange can deeply influence long-term success and resilience. These changes are part of broader, complex shifts in theological, philosophical, and scientific thought within the Islamic scholarly tradition, shaping its response to global challenges. Acknowledging these internal dynamics is key to identifying renewal pathways and underscores the need for intellectual freedom and embracing diverse ideas. This nuanced perspective helps us grasp how internal intellectual developments have steered the social and political courses of the Islamic world.**  
**In the Islamic world, there is a notable trend of prioritizing cohesiveness of thought over individual intellectual freedom.** This preference stems from a deeply ingrained value system that emphasizes communal harmony and unity, often rooted in religious and cultural traditions. This tendency can be seen in various spheres, including education, religious practices, and governance, where a unified approach to Islamic teachings and societal norms is heavily promoted. While this has historically helped in maintaining social order and a strong collective identity, it has also posed challenges to intellectual diversity and critical discourse. The consequences of such an approach are multifaceted, influencing the Islamic intellectual tradition and contributing to significant historical events, such as the loss of Palestine. This prioritization of consensus over critique may limit the community’s capacity to adapt and respond to complex geopolitical challenges, potentially hindering progress and reform within the Ummah.  
In contrast, during the same period in the Western world, thinkers like Thomas Aquinas successfully reconciled Aristotle’s philosophy within the Christian tradition, helping to shape medieval European thought. Aquinas utilized Aristotle's empirical approaches to reinforce Christian doctrines, demonstrating that reason and faith could coexist harmoniously. This integration was facilitated through systematic scholarly work and was institutionalized within European universities, ensuring a sustained influence of rational philosophical inquiry alongside theological studies.   
Aquinas' work was significantly influenced by the very Islamic philosophers who had kept Aristotelian thought alive and thriving. Figures like Averroes (Ibn Rushd), Avicenna (Ibn Sina), and Al-Farabi played a crucial role in interpreting and expanding upon Aristotle's ideas, which were then transmitted to the West through translations. Aquinas engaged deeply with their works, often building upon their ideas or critiquing them, thus creating a direct intellectual lineage from the Islamic Golden Age to the foundations of Western philosophy and theology.  
The profound impact of rationalism in shaping the Western world's trajectory is evident through its instrumental role in catalyzing the Enlightenment—a profound intellectual movement that began in the late 17th century. This period marked a seismic shift in thinking, where emphasis on reason, critical inquiry, and empirical evidence challenged the traditional authority of religion and monarchy. Enlightenment thinkers like John Locke, Voltaire, and Immanuel Kant championed ideals of liberty, progress, and tolerance, laying the intellectual groundwork for both the American and French Revolutions. These revolutions not only reshaped political landscapes but also affirmed the value of individual rights and rational governance, principles that are foundational to modern democracies.  
The ripple effects of rationalist thought continued through the Scientific Revolution, which transformed views on science by prioritizing observation and systematic experimentation. Figures such as Isaac Newton and Galileo Galilei dismantled old dogmas, introducing concepts that became cornerstones of physics and astronomy. This methodological shift not only advanced scientific knowledge but also fostered technological innovations that would fuel the Industrial Revolution. The transition to industrial economies, characterized by mechanization and mass production, originated in Western countries and significantly enhanced their productivity and economic power.  
**This surge in technological and economic capability underpinned the dominance of the Western world in global affairs. The advantages gained from industrialization allowed Western nations to exert substantial influence and control over trade routes, colonies, and international politics during the 19th and 20th centuries.** Ultimately, the adoption of rationalist principles and the consequent intellectual and industrial developments were pivotal in establishing the Western world's prominence on the global stage, demonstrating the transformative power of embracing reason and empirical research in shaping societal progress and geopolitical dynamics.  
**Compounding the intellectual retreat in the Islamic world was the crucial decision that had long-lasting repercussions: the banning of the printing press in much of the Islamic world.** While Europe embraced the printing press in the 15th century, revolutionizing the dissemination of knowledge and accelerating the spread of ideas, many Muslim rulers saw it as a threat to religious and social order. The Ottoman Empire, in particular, restricted Muslim use of the printing press for 270 years, fearing that it would lead to the spread of heretical ideas and weaken the authority of religious scholars. This ban significantly slowed the diffusion of knowledge within the Islamic world, further contributing to the intellectual stagnation that had already begun.  
The rise of nationalism, especially Arab nationalism, also played a crucial role in the decline of the Ottoman Empire. This ideological shift, emphasizing distinct national identities over a unified Islamic identity, exacerbated the fragmentation within the empire and hindered its ability to respond effectively to external pressures and internal dissent.  
The consequences of these developments were far-reaching. As the Islamic world turned inward, both intellectually and technologically, it began to lose its earlier dynamism and its ability to adapt to the rapidly changing global landscape. **The decline in scientific, philosophical, and technological advancement weakened the civilization, making it more vulnerable to external pressures and less capable of defending its territories effectively.** By the 19th and early 20th centuries, this intellectual and political decline was starkly evident in the Ottoman Empire, which controlled Palestine. The empire, once a formidable force, was now suffering from internal decay, corruption, and an inability to modernize its military and administrative structures. **This weakness made the empire increasingly susceptible to European intervention.**  
The imbalance of power between the declining Ottoman Empire and the rapidly industrializing European nations culminated in significant geopolitical shifts. European powers, capitalizing on the Ottoman decline, exerted greater influence in the Middle East. This culminated in events like the Balfour Declaration of 1917, where Britain expressed support for the establishment of a "national home for the Jewish people" in Palestine, and the subsequent British Mandate over the region. These developments, alongside growing Jewish immigration and the Zionist movement, ultimately led to the creation of the state of Israel in 1948\.  
The loss of Palestine can thus be seen as part of a broader history of decline within the Islamic world. The retreat from the intellectual openness and scientific inquiry of the Golden Age, the failure to adapt to the changing global dynamics, and the suppression of technological innovation such as the printing press left the Muslim world weakened and divided. These factors collectively contributed to the broader vulnerabilities that made the loss of Palestine possible.  
This historical trajectory underscores the critical importance of liberal education in the Islamic world—an education that embraces the balance between faith and reason, and one that fosters intellectual curiosity, scientific inquiry, and openness to technological advancements. The discussion serves as a reminder of how intellectual and technological stagnation can have devastating consequences for a civilization’s ability to sustain its influence and defend its territories.  
**In response to these lessons from history, the vision for the Modern House of Wisdom in the rebuilt Gaza Strip aims to revive the spirit of the Islamic Golden Age, and a full embrace of the Islamic intellectual and philosophical traditions.** This institution will be dedicated to providing a liberal education that integrates critical thinking, creativity, and pluralism, while focusing on non-religious studies. The goal is to foster a new generation of scholars and thinkers who can navigate the complexities of the modern world, ensuring that the mistakes of the past are not repeated. The Modern House of Wisdom will stand as a beacon of intellectual revival, symbolizing the importance of knowledge, innovation, and balanced education in securing a prosperous and resilient future for the Islamic world.

# Appendix E: Draft United Nations Security Council Resolution for the Regretful Displacement of Gazan Refugees[^8] {#appendix-e:-draft-united-nations-security-council-resolution-for-the-regretful-displacement-of-gazan-refugees}

**On the Temporary Displacement and Limited Prospects of Return for Gazan Refugees Under War Duress**

The Security Council,

Recalling Chapter VII of the Charter of the United Nations and the primary responsibility of the Security Council for the maintenance of international peace and security,

Reaffirming its previous resolutions on the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, including \[specific resolutions\], and recognizing the principles of international law and conventions pertaining to human rights and the treatment of refugees,

Noting with grave concern the severe impact of the prolonged conflict in Gaza, which consists of allegedly genocidal elements in the context of a broader, unresolved ethno-religious conflict, which has necessitated the involuntary displacement of a significant portion of the population,

Acknowledging the likelihood that many of these displaced individuals may not find it feasible or desirable to return due to the enduring nature of the conflict,

Emphasizing the need to uphold human rights and international humanitarian law in addressing the long-term implications of such displacement,

Deeply concerned by the humanitarian situation in Gaza and the need for a sustainable solution for refugees affected by the conflict,

Determined to contribute to the creation of conditions conducive to a sustainable peace between Israeli and Palestinian peoples,

Acting under Chapter VII of the Charter of the United Nations,

	1\.	Acknowledges that the temporary displacement from Gaza is a direct consequence of the war, and recognizes that a substantial portion of the displaced population may not return to Gaza due to its destruction.

	2\.	Calls for the establishment of a comprehensive support program for the resettled individuals, including integration assistance in host countries, recognizing that for many, resettlement may become a long-term or permanent situation.  
	3\.	Urges Member States and international organizations to collaborate in providing humanitarian aid, resettlement support, and development assistance to address the needs of the displaced population.  
4\.	Requests the Secretary-General to closely monitor the resettlement process, the conditions in Gaza affecting the possibility of return, and to regularly report to the Security Council on the long-term status of the displaced population.  
5\.	Mandates the Canaan Confederation to actively assist in the repatriation process of Gazan refugees who choose to return, once conditions allow, including providing logistical support, coordination with local authorities, and the necessary resources to ensure a safe and dignified return.   
	6\.	Mandates the State of Israel to open humanitarian evacuation corridors from the Gaza Strip to the West Bank in cooperation with Canaan Confederation peacekeeping forces.  
7\.	Recognizes the need for comprehensive support for those displaced individuals who choose not to return or find return infeasible, including long-term integration and resettlement assistance in host countries.  
	8\.	Continues to encourage voluntary return under safe and dignified conditions for those who wish to do so, when Gaza is eventually rebuilt, while acknowledging the likelihood of limited return.  
	9\.	Firmly states that no future Israeli settlement activity will occur in Gaza, emphasizing that such activities are contrary to international law and undermine the prospects for a peaceful resolution to the conflict.  
	10\.	Decides to remain actively seized of the matter and requests the Secretary-General to provide updates on the implementation of this resolution and the evolving situation in Gaza.

# Appendix F: Draft United Nations Security Council Resolution Calling for a Ceasefire[^9] {#appendix-f:-draft-united-nations-security-council-resolution-calling-for-a-ceasefire}

**On Ceasefire in the Israeli-Hamas Conflict and Convening an Emergency Session**

The Security Council,

Recalling its primary responsibility under the Charter of the United Nations for the maintenance of international peace and security,

Noting with grave concern the ongoing conflict between Israel and Hamas, and its detrimental impact on civilian populations,

Reaffirming the importance of achieving a peaceful resolution to the conflict, and the need for immediate steps to deescalate tensions,

Acting under Chapter VII of the Charter of the United Nations,

	1\.	Calls for an Immediate Ceasefire:  
	•	Demands an immediate cessation of hostilities by all parties involved in the Israeli-Hamas conflict, including the end of military actions, rocket firings, and other forms of aggression.  
	  
**2\.	Specific Disengagement Orders:**  
•	**Orders Hamas to disengage and withdraw its forces from North of the Netzarim Corridor, ceasing all military operations and activities in the area.**

•	**Orders Israel to disengage and withdraw its forces from South of the Netzarim Corridor, ceasing all military operations and activities in the area, excluding the Philadelphia Corridor.**

	3\.	Establishment of a Buffer Zone:  
	•	Declares Central Gaza, Khan Yunis, and Rafah as a demilitarized buffer zone. The establishment of this zone aims to reduce direct confrontations and facilitate humanitarian access. Monitoring and maintenance of the buffer zone will be conducted through remote surveillance and local reports, supported by the international community’s diplomatic efforts before the initial deployment of Confederation peacekeeping forces.

	4 	Mandate for Immediate Release:  
            •          Hamas and allied militias are mandated to immediately release all hostages currently under its custody.

5\. 	Mandatory Exile of Hamas and Palestinian Islamic Jihad’s Military Leadership[^10]

* Mandatory Exile as Precondition for Reconstruction: The immediate and irreversible exile of the Palestinian military leadership from the Gaza Strip is a precondition for any plan for Gaza's reconstruction.  
* International Monitoring and Oversight: This critical step will be under strict supervision by The Canaan Confederation, ensuring the full execution of the exile in accordance with the cease-fire terms.  
* Best Effort Protection by Host Country from Israeli Aggression: The international community recognizes the complexities surrounding the safety of exiled individuals. Protection will be offered based on the best efforts of the Confederation host country, acknowledging the inherent risks and the high-profile status of the exiled leaders. It is understood that safety from Israeli aggression cannot be fully guaranteed.  
* Permanent Nature of Exile: This exile is permanent, with no provisions for return included in the cease-fire agreement. The initiation of Gaza's reconstruction hinges on this action, aiming to foster a stable and peaceful environment necessary for recovery and a comprehensive peace agreement and ensuring long-term security and stability in the region.  
* Link to Reconstruction Initiatives: The successful implementation of this article directly unlocks international support and resources earmarked for Palestine's reconstruction. This includes initiatives aimed at rubble clearing, body retrieval, infrastructure rebuilding, humanitarian aid, and economic development, contingent upon establishing a peaceful and secure environment.  
* Commitment to Non-Violence and Reconstruction: All parties involved commit to an immediate cessation of hostilities and to cooperate on humanitarian efforts. The international community pledges substantial support for Gaza’s stabilization, contingent upon maintaining peace and fulfilling the terms of this cease-fire.

6\.	Convenes an Emergency Session:  
	•	Decides to convene an emergency session of the UN Security Council to be held within \[a specified timeframe\], summoning representatives of every relevant head of state, along with the representatives of Israel, the Palestinian Authority, Hamas, and other relevant stakeholders, to debate the terms of the proposed Canaan Confederation as a means to resolve the conflict.

7\.	Urges Participation and Dialogue:  
	•	Strongly urges all parties to participate constructively in the emergency session and engage in open and comprehensive dialogue aimed at establishing the terms of the confederation for lasting peace.

8\.	Support for Peace Initiatives:  
	•	Encourages the international community to support efforts for peace and reconciliation, including the proposed confederation, and to provide assistance for humanitarian relief and rebuilding efforts.  
	  
9\.	Monitoring and Compliance:  
	•	Requests the Secretary-General to monitor compliance with the ceasefire and report back to the Council on any violations and on the progress of preparations for the emergency session.  
	  
10\.	Decides to Remain Actively Seized of the Matter:  
	•	Decides to remain actively seized of the situation and to reconvene as necessary to assess progress and take further action as required.

# Appendix G: Draft Covenant Framework for the Al-Aqsa Mosque Compound/Temple Mount as a Pluralistic Religious Space {#appendix-g:-draft-covenant-framework-for-the-al-aqsa-mosque-compound/temple-mount-as-a-pluralistic-religious-space}

**Preamble**

Recognizing the profound religious significance of the site known to Muslims as the Al-Aqsa Mosque compound, revered as the place of the Prophet Muhammad’s Night Journey and Ascension, and to Jews as the Temple Mount, the site of the First and Second Temples. We embrace the vision of Al-Aqsa/Temple Mount evolving as a pluralistic religious space, symbolizing our common aspirations for peace, justice, and harmonious coexistence and specifically welcoming *People of the Book* in the spirit of shared Abrahamic traditions, in implementation of Isaiah 56:7[^11].

**Article 1: Fundamental Principles**  
Unity and Shared Aspirations: Highlighting Al-Aqsa’s role as a pluralistic religious space that represents a beacon of unity and shared spiritual heritage among Muslims, Jews, and Christians. This vision honors the site’s significance to all People of the Book, fostering a bridge towards shared aspirations and peace.

**Article 2: Governance**  
Inclusive Governance for All Abrahamic Faiths: Commitment to the establishment of an Judeo-Islamic governance structure directly inspired by the Constitution of Medina[^12], that not only respects the site’s significance to Muslims and Jews but also explicitly acknowledges and welcomes the involvement of all People of the Book, ensuring that the site’s management reflects a commitment to inclusivity and mutual respect. 

**Article 3: Access and Worship**  
Welcoming People of the Book: Promoting a model of coexistence that allows for Islamic worship at Al-Aqsa, while also championing the site as a pluralistic religious space that welcomes followers of all Abrahamic faiths. This approach symbolizes a commitment to prayer and reflection for all who uphold the ideals of peace and harmony.

**Article 4: Preservation and Education**  
Educational Outreach to People of the Book: Initiating programs that not only highlight the historical and religious significance of the site to Islam and Judaism but also explore its importance to the entire Abrahamic tradition. These educational efforts aim to foster a deeper understanding and respect among all People of the Book.

**Article 5: International Engagement**  
A Symbol of Abrahamic Unity: Showcasing the Al-Aqsa compound as a pluralistic religious space and a beacon of interfaith harmony, especially among People of the Book. This vision underscores the potential for shared sacred spaces to foster global peace and mutual understanding, emphasizing the site’s role in bridging Abrahamic faiths.

**Article 6: Aspirational Alignment with Universal Peace Ideal**s  
Shared Aspirations for Peace: This constitution acknowledges the profound significance of the Al-Aqsa Mosque compound/Temple Mount to both Muslims and Jews, embracing the site as a symbol of our shared hopes for peace, unity, and pluralistic harmony.

Commitment to a Pluralistic Vision: We commit to fostering an environment at the Al-Aqsa Mosque compound/Temple Mount that embodies principles of peace, understanding, and coexistence. This site is envisioned as a living testament to our shared human values, aiming to serve as a beacon of interfaith dialogue and mutual respect.

Engagement for Harmony: Urging continuous engagement and respectful dialogue, this article emphasizes our collective pursuit of a future marked by harmonious coexistence. It highlights the importance of working together to honor our shared aspirations, fostering a space that symbolizes unity and peace for all.

# Appendix H: Draft Covenant for the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif {#appendix-h:-draft-covenant-for-the-temple-mount/haram-al-sharif}

Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim (In the Name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful)  
In the spirit of Psalm 85:10-11: "Love and faithfulness meet together; righteousness and peace kiss each other."

**Preamble**

In recognition of the sacred trust and profound responsibility bestowed upon us by Allah, the Most High, to protect and honor the holy sites, and acknowledging the historical, religious, and cultural significance of the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif to both the Muslim and Jewish communities, we, the representatives of the Ummah of Islam and the People of the Book, hereby establish this covenant. Drawing inspiration from the Charter of Medina and the Prophet Muhammad's timeless wisdom that "The Jews have their religion, and the Muslims have theirs," alongside the teachings of Leviticus 19:18, "Do not seek revenge or bear a grudge against anyone among your people, but love your neighbor as yourself. I am the LORD," we seek to enshrine the principles of religious freedom, mutual respect, and cooperation, as commanded by Allah, to ensure the harmonious coexistence of all who revere this sacred place. Moreover, we commit to the long-term vision of fulfilling the noble words of the Prophet Isaiah (peace be upon him): "For my house shall be called a house of prayer for all peoples" (Isaiah 56:7). As Allah the Exalted has decreed, "There shall be no compulsion in religion" (Quran 2:256), and as echoed by the prophetic vision in Isaiah, we affirm our dedication to upholding the freedom of worship for all.

**Article I: “The Jews have their religion and the Muslims have theirs”**

**Freedom of Worship:** The Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif shall be a place where both Muslims and Jews are free to worship their Creator according to their respective traditions. Each community shall have the right to practice its faith without interference, in accordance with the teachings of the Prophet Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him), who said in his covenant with the Christians of Najran: "No bishop shall be removed from his bishopric, no monk from his monastery, and no priest from his parish." In this spirit, no one shall be removed from their place of worship or hindered in their religious duties on the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif. This commitment is further underscored by Micah 4:3-4, "He will judge between many peoples and will settle disputes for strong nations far and wide. They will beat their swords into plowshares and their spears into pruning hooks. Nation will not take up sword against nation, nor will they train for war anymore."

**Equal Access:** Both Muslims and Jews shall have regulated access to their respective sacred sites within the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif, with due respect for the sanctity and traditions of each faith, as ordained by Allah, the Just and the Merciful, and as envisioned by Isaiah, where "My house shall be called a house of prayer for all peoples."

**Article II: Enshrinement of the Current Status Quo**

Administration and Control:

* The Islamic Waqf, in accordance with the historical trust placed in it, shall continue to administer the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif, managing the Muslim holy sites within the compound, including Al-Aqsa Mosque and the Dome of the Rock, as guardians of these blessed sanctuaries.  
* The State of Israel, in collaboration with the Canaan Confederation, shall maintain overall security control, managing entry points and ensuring the enforcement of this covenant, with respect for the sanctity of the holy sites and the principles of justice as taught by the Prophets (peace be upon them).

Access and Worship:
