* Muslims shall have the exclusive right to perform their prayers at the Al-Aqsa Mosque and the Dome of the Rock, in accordance with the traditions of the Ummah.  
* Non-Muslims, including Jews, shall be permitted to visit the site during designated visiting hours but shall refrain from conducting their prayers there, respecting the Islamic nature of these sites as decreed by the historical status quo. Jewish prayer shall continue to be conducted at the Western Wall, in keeping with the practices established over generations.

Visiting Hours and Regulations:

* Non-Muslim visiting hours shall be specified and regulated by the Israeli authorities, typically outside of Muslim prayer times, in order to maintain the sanctity and order of the holy site. These visiting hours shall be enforced with care and respect, ensuring that "no one shall make them afraid" (Micah 4:4).

Security Arrangements:

* Israeli and Canaan Confederation security forces shall be stationed at the entrances to the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif to manage access and maintain order, in cooperation with the Islamic Waqf.  
* The Waqf shall have its own security personnel responsible for the internal security and management of the religious sites within the compound, acting as custodians of these sacred trusts.

Religious and Political Sensitivities:

* The status quo shall be maintained to avoid any escalation of tensions and conflict between religious communities, in accordance with the principles of wisdom and patience that Allah enjoins upon the believers, and the scriptural mandate that "Love and faithfulness meet together; righteousness and peace kiss each other" (Psalm 85:10-11).  
* Any changes or perceived changes to the status quo shall be subject to approval by the Joint Council and coordinated with relevant authorities, ensuring that peace and stability are preserved, as is the command of Allah, and as all communities are reminded, "Do not seek revenge or bear a grudge against anyone among your people, but love your neighbor as yourself" (Leviticus 19:18).

**Article III: Mutual Respect and Cooperation**

**Mutual Respect:** Both Muslims and Jews shall treat each other with the respect and dignity commanded by Allah, the Most High, who created mankind in diversity, and as reflected in the teachings of the Hebrew Scriptures, "Love your neighbor as yourself" (Leviticus 19:18). As the Prophet Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) declared in his covenant with the Monks of Mount Sinai, "No one is to destroy a house of their religion, to damage it, or to carry anything from it to the Muslims’ houses," we similarly commit to safeguarding the sacred spaces of both communities on the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif. Any form of incitement, provocation, or disrespect towards the other community's religious beliefs and practices is strictly prohibited, for Allah loves those who act justly, and as the Psalmist sang, "Righteousness and peace kiss each other" (Psalm 85:10).

**Joint Council:** A Joint Council, composed of representatives from both the Muslim and Jewish communities, shall be established to oversee the implementation of this covenant, address any disputes, and ensure ongoing dialogue and cooperation. This council shall operate in the spirit of the Prophet Muhammad’s (peace be upon him) inclusive governance in Medina, where all groups worked together for the common good, as Allah has commanded, and as the Psalmist envisioned, "Faithfulness springs forth from the earth, and righteousness looks down from heaven" (Psalm 85:11).

**Conflict Resolution:** Any disputes arising from the interpretation or implementation of this covenant shall be resolved through arbitration by the Joint Council, guided by principles of fairness, justice, and mutual respect, as enjoined by the Quran and the Sunnah, and as the Hebrew Scriptures counsel, "Love and faithfulness meet together; righteousness and peace kiss each other" (Psalm 85:10-11). As Allah the Most High instructs in the Quran: "And do not argue with the People of the Scripture except in a way that is best, unless it is with those who commit injustice among them, and say, 'We believe in that which has been revealed to us and revealed to you. And our God and your God is one; and we are Muslims \[in submission\] to Him'" (Quran 29:46).

**Article IV: Security and Protection**

**Collective Security:** Both communities shall work together to ensure the security and protection of the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif, recognizing that the safety of all worshippers and visitors is a sacred duty entrusted to them by Allah. As the Prophet Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) emphasized, the safety of all people is paramount, and any threat to the sanctity and safety of this holy site shall be addressed collectively, in the spirit of brotherhood and unity, as envisioned by the prophet Micah: "They will beat their swords into plowshares and their spears into pruning hooks. Nation will not take up sword against nation, nor will they train for war anymore" (Micah 4:3).

**Protection of Worshippers:** Measures shall be taken to ensure the safety and security of all worshippers and visitors, maintaining an environment of peace and tranquility, as Allah, the Lord of Peace, desires for His creation, and as echoed in the vision of Isaiah, "For my house shall be called a house of prayer for all peoples" (Isaiah 56:7).

**State-Sponsored Hudna Violations:** Any state-sponsored violation of this covenant shall be considered a violation of the Hudna and an act of war against the sanctity of the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif and the principles of peace and coexistence enshrined herein. Such violations shall be immediately referred to the dispute resolution systems of the Canaan Confederation as well as to the United Nations Security Council for urgent deliberation and action. The international community shall be called upon to uphold justice and ensure that the violators are held accountable, as Allah commands in the Quran: "Indeed, Allah orders justice and good conduct..." (Quran 16:90), and as the prophet Micah reminds us, "He will judge between many peoples and will settle disputes for strong nations far and wide" (Micah 4:3).

**Article V: Long-Term Vision**

**Isaiah 56:7 Goal:** As a long-term goal, this covenant aspires to fulfill the vision of Isaiah (peace be upon him), "For my house shall be called a house of prayer for all peoples." This vision shall guide future efforts to make the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif a place where people of all faiths can come together in peace and worship, as the Quran says, "And We have made some of you as a trial for others: will you have patience? And your Lord is Ever-Seer" (Quran 25:20), and as Isaiah prophesied, inviting all to a house of universal prayer.

**Article VI: Inspiration from the Covenants of Muhammad**

**Historical Precedent:** Drawing inspiration from the Covenants of the Prophet Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him), including the Constitution of Medina and the Covenant with the Christians of Najran, which established principles of coexistence and mutual respect among diverse religious communities, we commit to upholding similar values within the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif, as a testament to the enduring wisdom of the Islamic tradition. These principles are mirrored in the teachings of the Hebrew Scriptures, which call us to seek justice, love mercy, and walk humbly with our God (Micah 6:8).

**Principle of Religious Autonomy:** In line with the Constitution of Medina's principle that "the Jews have their religion and the Muslims have theirs," this covenant reaffirms the autonomy of each community to practice its religion freely and without interference, as is their right bestowed by Allah, the Most Just, and as Leviticus teaches us, "Love your neighbor as yourself" (Leviticus 19:18), a command that forms the ethical backbone of our mutual interactions on the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif.

**Article VII: Conditional Peace Treaty and Interfaith Respect**

**Conditional Détente Agreement:** This covenant represents a conditional détente between the Muslim and Jewish communities, dependent on the adherence of both parties to the terms outlined in this document. The détente established herein relies on the continuous respect and implementation of the covenant's provisions, fostering a sustained and cautious peace

**Promotion of Interfaith Respect:** Recognizing the profound importance of mutual respect and coexistence between the Muslim and Jewish communities, and in the spirit of fostering a peaceful future, the individual Muslim-majority nations that are signatories to this treaty commit to promoting interfaith respect through education, dialogue, and cultural exchange, as is the way of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), and as echoed in the Hebrew Scriptures, which teach us to seek peace and pursue it (Psalm 34:14).

**Judeo-Islamic Tradition:** Furthermore, the signatory nations express a collective desire to formalize the Judeo-Islamic tradition, acknowledging the rich history of cooperation, shared values, and intellectual exchange that has existed between Muslims and Jews throughout history. This initiative seeks to revive and celebrate the deep connections between the two faiths, creating a foundation for lasting peace and mutual understanding, as Allah has willed, and as the prophet Isaiah invites all nations to join in worship at a house of prayer for all peoples (Isaiah 56:7).

**Abrahamic Tradition:** In recognition of our shared heritage and the profound bonds that unite us, this covenant solemnly affirms the Abrahamic tradition as the cornerstone of our collective identity and mutual aspirations. We commit to honoring the teachings and values inherited from Abraham, who is revered across our diverse communities as a patriarch of faith, a model of hospitality, and a symbol of unwavering commitment to the divine. This covenant pledges to foster respect, understanding, and cooperation among all who draw inspiration from Abraham, ensuring that his legacy continues to guide us in pursuit of peace, justice, and reconciliation. We dedicate ourselves to embodying these principles, promoting dialogue, and supporting initiatives that reflect our common Abrahamic roots, thereby strengthening the bonds of brotherhood and sisterhood across our communities.

**Promotion of Understanding:** The signatory nations will encourage initiatives that foster understanding and reconciliation between the Muslim and Jewish communities, drawing on shared values and historical moments of cooperation. This effort is not an abrogation of faith but a reaffirmation of Islam's enduring principles of respect, coexistence, and the pursuit of justice, aligned with the biblical call to love your neighbor as yourself (Leviticus 19:18), fostering a community where "every man \[shall sit\] under his vine and under his fig tree, and none shall make them afraid" (Micah 4:4).

**Article VIII: Amendment Procedure**

1\. Amendment Authority:

* Amendments to this covenant may only be proposed and enacted by the Joint Council, composed of representatives from both the Jewish and Muslim communities. The Joint Council shall act in the best interest of maintaining peace, mutual respect, and the sanctity of the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif.

2\. Proposal of Amendments:

* Any member of the Joint Council may propose an amendment to this covenant. The proposal must be submitted in writing and include a detailed explanation of the proposed changes, the reasons for the amendment, and the potential impact on both communities.

3\. Deliberation and Consultation:

* Upon receiving a proposed amendment, the Joint Council shall engage in thorough deliberation and consultation. This process must include input from religious leaders, scholars, and community representatives from both the Jewish and Muslim communities, ensuring that all perspectives are considered.

4\. Voting Procedure:

* After deliberation, the Joint Council shall vote on the proposed amendment. For an amendment to pass within the Joint Council, it must receive at least a two-thirds majority vote from the members. If the amendment affects fundamental principles of the covenant, such as those related to religious freedom, mutual respect, or the administration of the holy site, a unanimous vote may be required.

5\. Issuance of a Plebiscite:

* Once an amendment has been approved by the Joint Council, it shall be subject to a plebiscite (a direct vote of the people). The plebiscite will allow the broader Jewish and Muslim communities to vote on the proposed amendment, ensuring that it reflects the will of the people.

6\. Monitoring by the Canaan Confederation:

* The plebiscite shall be organized and monitored by the Canaan Confederation to ensure fairness, transparency, and impartiality. The Canaan Confederation shall oversee the voting process, verify the results, and report on the conduct of the plebiscite to ensure that it meets international standards of democratic practice.

7\. Ratification and Implementation:

* If the proposed amendment receives a majority vote in the plebiscite, it shall be ratified and formally incorporated into the covenant. The Joint Council shall oversee the implementation of the amendment, ensuring that it aligns with the original spirit and intent of the covenant.

8\. Safeguards Against Erosion of Fundamental Principles:

* No amendment shall be made that undermines the core principles of religious freedom, mutual respect, and peaceful coexistence as enshrined in this covenant. Any attempt to introduce such amendments shall be deemed invalid and contrary to the purpose of this covenant.

9\. Periodic Review:

* The Joint Council shall conduct a periodic review of the covenant, at least every five years, to assess its effectiveness and consider whether any amendments are necessary to address changing circumstances or emerging challenges. Any amendments proposed as a result of this review shall follow the same procedure outlined above, including the issuance of a plebiscite.

**Conclusion**

In the spirit of reconciliation and peace, we embrace the teachings of Christ, who calls us to be peacemakers (Matthew 5:9) and to live in peace with everyone (Romans 12:18). Thus, we commit to this covenant not only as a political and social agreement but as a profound moral commitment to foster peace and respect across our communities.   
We, the undersigned representatives of the Jewish and Muslim communities, hereby agree to uphold and implement this covenant, ensuring the Temple Mount/Haram al-Sharif remains a place of peace, respect, and shared reverence for future generations.

Signed,  
\[Jewish Community Representatives\]  
\[Muslim Community Representatives\]

Witnessed By

\[Christian Community Representatives\]

Date: \[Current Date\]

# Appendix I: Draft Gentlemen’s Agreement Regarding the Diplomatic Recognition of the State of Israel and the State of Palestine {#appendix-i:-draft-gentlemen’s-agreement-regarding-the-diplomatic-recognition-of-the-state-of-israel-and-the-state-of-palestine}

**Preamble** Recognizing the importance of addressing critical issues such as territorial disputes and educational reforms in achieving lasting peace between the State of Israel and the State of Palestine, this agreement affirms the commitment of both states to the Canaan Confederation framework. This framework is instrumental in resolving these disputes and fostering an inclusive, democratic, and peaceful society.

**Article 1: Commitment to Peace, Cooperation, and Respect** The undersigned nations (hereinafter referred to as "Participating Countries") hereby express their unwavering support for a peaceful resolution to the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, emphasizing the role of dialogue, negotiation, mutual respect, and adherence to the Canaan Confederation’s initiatives.

**Article 2: Support for Critical Issues** Participating Countries support:

* The implementation of the land lease scheme to address territorial disputes, wherein the State of Israel and the State of Palestine agree to manage disputed lands via the Land Lease Management Authority of the Canaan Confederation.  
* Educational reforms as outlined by the Canaan Confederation Educational Framework to address historical grievances and promote a balanced understanding of shared histories between the Jews and the Muslims.

**Article 3: Conditionality of Diplomatic Recognition** Participating Countries condition their full and continued diplomatic recognition of both the State of Israel and the State of Palestine on their progress towards:

* The land lease scheme for resolving territorial disputes.  
* The educational reforms aimed at deradicalization and fostering an inclusive, democratic society within the framework of the Canaan Confederation.

**Article 4: Enforcement, Dispute Resolution, and Monitoring** The Canaan Confederation member states shall monitor compliance with the land lease agreement and educational reforms, employing sanctions for violations and providing incentives for achievements. Disputes shall be resolved through a predefined multistage dispute resolution process, aiming for equitable solutions that uphold the spirit of cooperation, peace, and reform.

**Article 5: Affirmation of Support** Participating Countries affirm their support for both Israel and Palestine in their pursuit of peace, security, prosperity, and meaningful reforms. This agreement is made in the spirit of encouraging compliance with international agreements, fostering lasting peace in the region, and supporting the development of inclusive and democratic institutions.

**Signatories** \[Signatory space for the representatives of Participating Countries\]

# Appendix J: Draft Formal Apology from the United States with an Invitation to the Islamic Republic of Iran to Join the Canaan Confederation {#appendix-j:-draft-formal-apology-from-the-united-states-with-an-invitation-to-the-islamic-republic-of-iran-to-join-the-canaan-confederation}

To the People and Government of the Islamic Republic of Iran,

As the Government of the United States of America, we extend our deepest apologies for our historical actions, notably our involvement in the 1953 coup in Iran and our subsequent actions and aggression that have contributed to division and strife in the Middle East. We are committed to rectifying these past actions with sincere efforts toward peace, understanding, and cooperation.

In recognizing the importance of moving forward together, we extend a heartfelt invitation to Iran to join the Canaan Confederation — a new initiative aimed at fostering regional unity, security, and prosperity.

**Iran's Critical Role in the Canaan Confederation:**

* **Funding the Confederation Waqf:** We propose using current Iranian frozen assets as the initial seed of the Confederation Waqf, dedicated to rebuilding efforts in Gaza and other regions in need within the Confederation. This investment symbolizes a new chapter of cooperation and shared responsibility for regional stability.  
* **Advocacy for Shia Rights:** Iran’s participation is invaluable in advocating for the rights of the Shia minority, ensuring that their voices and concerns are represented and respected within the framework of the Confederation.  
* **Healing the Sunni-Shia Divide:** By collaborating with Sunni members of the Confederation, Iran has a unique opportunity to bridge the historical Sunni-Shia divide, promoting intra-Islamic dialogue and understanding.  
* **Shared Goals for Peace and Prosperity:** Together, we can address common challenges such as security, economic development, and environmental sustainability, transcending sectarian and national divides.  
* **The Promotion of Zoroastrianism:** Recognizing the cultural heritage of Zoroastrianism, Iran’s native Persian religion, as a potential positive stabilizing force in the monotheistic world.

**The Promise of Collaboration:**

* We believe that through constructive dialogue and collaboration within the Canaan Confederation, we can create a powerful platform for healing and unity. The Confederation seeks to celebrate our diverse heritage while building a shared future characterized by peace and mutual respect.  
* The United States pledges to support this journey, respecting the equal standing of all member states and dedicating resources to ensure the success and sustainability of the Confederation.

This invitation is extended with hope and respect, aiming to mark the beginning of a new era in our relations—an era where, together, we can overcome past grievances and build a peaceful, prosperous region for all its inhabitants.

Signed,  
\[Name of the Secretary of State or President\]  
\[Date\]

# Appendix K: Draft Warning of Possible US-Led Police Action Against Iran {#appendix-k:-draft-warning-of-possible-us-led-police-action-against-iran}

To the Government of the Islamic Republic of Iran:

This communication addresses the critical situation developing due to the potential Iran-Israel conflict in the aftermath of the Hamas-Israel war, alongside grave concerns over Iran's nuclear program. Indications that Iran's nuclear endeavors may constitute an active weapons of mass destruction (WMD) program, combined with ongoing state sponsorship of terror and sectarian violence, risk an uncontained international response.

The historical context of international intervention, particularly the Iraq war, serves as a poignant reference point in this discourse. It is important to acknowledge that the United States, along with its allies, reflects on the Iraq war with a large degree of regret, especially regarding the intelligence assessments that led to the conflict and the subsequent long-term implications for regional stability and international relations. The justification for the Iraq war, largely predicated on the perceived threat of WMDs and terrorism, highlights the critical importance of accurate intelligence and the need for diplomatic engagement wherever possible.

Drawing from this experience, the international community, led by the United States, emphasizes the imperative of preventing the spread of WMDs and curbing state-sponsored terrorism. Iran is thus urged to engage transparently with international bodies regarding its nuclear program and to positively and constructively influence the actions of resistance groups it sponsors. The parallels between the current situation with Iran and the prelude to the Iraq war are concerning, underscoring the need for immediate action to avert potential conflict.

The potential for a non-containable Israel-Hezbollah or Israel-Iran Conflict, further complicated by Iran's controversial nuclear program, highlights the urgent need for Iran to demonstrate a genuine commitment to peace and stability. The international community expects Iran to take verifiable steps to assure the world of its peaceful intentions, including adhering to international nuclear agreements and disengaging from activities considered to support terrorism.

In issuing this warning, it is with a sense of responsibility and the hope to prevent conflict, reflecting on past actions such as the Iraq war with a critical eye. The aim is to promote a secure, stable, and peaceful international environment. The Iranian government is strongly advised to consider these factors and act accordingly to prevent escalation and ensure the well-being of all involved.

We urge the Islamic Republic of Iran to consider joining the Canaan Confederation, representing Shia and religious minority interests, as a testament to its commitment to regional peace. This move could significantly reduce the likelihood of future conflicts with the United States by showcasing Iran's preference for diplomacy over military action. Active participation in the confederation would allow Iran to voice its concerns constructively, fostering mutual understanding and respect within the region. Ultimately, Iran's involvement is seen by the international community, especially the United States, as a positive step toward diminishing tensions and enhancing long-term stability and cooperation in the Middle East.

Acknowledging the complex history between the United States and Iran, there lies a potential for reconciliation and a new era of mutual respect. The involvement of Iran in the Canaan Confederation could mark a significant step towards this goal, offering a platform for dialogue and cooperation. Overcoming past grievances through constructive engagement and transparency is essential for both nations. This endeavor promises a peaceful future and sets a precedent for resolving global conflicts.

Sincerely,

\[Your Name\] \[Your Position\] \[Your Organization/Country\]

# Appendix L: Draft International Declaration on Reconciliation and Remembrance for the Historical Tragedies of the Late Ottoman Period {#appendix-l:-draft-international-declaration-on-reconciliation-and-remembrance-for-the-historical-tragedies-of-the-late-ottoman-period}

**Preamble** 

In the spirit of reconciliation, truth, and a shared future, this document acknowledges the profound tragedies that occurred during the final years of the Ottoman Empire and the establishment of the Republic of Turkey. It aims to honor the memory of all those who suffered and to promote understanding and healing among all Turkish people and the descendants of those affected.

**Acknowledgment of the Past** 

The Ottoman Empire was a diverse mosaic of cultures, languages, and religions. As the Empire declined, exacerbated by rising nationalism and global conflicts, this diversity was managed less through the traditional millet system and more through increasingly repressive measures. This document specifically recognizes the events historically identified as the Armenian, Assyrian, and Greek Genocides as significant atrocities, representing immense suffering and loss. We introduce this acknowledgment into the International Court of Justice genocide case against Israel, offering a framework to evaluate the actions of the IDF against established historical patterns of state-led atrocity.

**Historical Evidence and Legal Framework**

**We propose that the State of Turkey submit detailed Ottoman archival evidence and expert historical analyses to the International Court of Justice. This submission will outline the operational tactics, administrative orders, and military engagements similar to those observed in modern conflicts, providing a comparative basis to assess claims of genocidal intent and execution in different contexts in the ongoing conflict in the Israel-Hamas War.**

**Understanding and Compassion**

This acknowledgment does not seek to blame contemporary Turkish society but to address historical actions within their complex contexts. It emphasizes the role of understanding and compassion in confronting painful histories, fostering a dialogue centered on truth and reconciliation.

**Moving Forward Together**

By recognizing these tragedies, we commit to a future where such suffering is actively prevented. This document lays the groundwork for a society that values dignity and rights universally, learning from the past to inform present actions and policies. It calls for an international dialogue, leveraging historical understanding to enhance global peacekeeping and human rights enforcement strategies.

**Conclusion**

Endorsing this document signals a bold step towards accepting our historical responsibilities, healing collective wounds, and building a resilient future. It serves as a testament to our commitment to truth, reconciliation, and the unbreakable human spirit to seek justice and unity in the face of past adversities. We urge other nations to reflect on these lessons, applying them to current and future international legal and diplomatic efforts.

# Appendix M: Draft Memorandum of Understanding on Human Rights and Legal Reforms in the Canaan Confederation {#appendix-m:-draft-memorandum-of-understanding-on-human-rights-and-legal-reforms-in-the-canaan-confederation}

This Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) is entered into on \[Date\], by and between the Member States of the Canaan Confederation (hereinafter referred to as "the Members") and \[International Human Rights Organization/Partner Country/International Body\] (hereinafter referred to as "the Partner"), collectively referred to as "the Parties."

**Preamble**

**WHEREAS**, the Parties are committed to the promotion and protection of human rights, the rule of law, and the advancement of justice within the Canaan Confederation;

**WHEREAS**, the Parties recognize the importance of continuous legal and social reforms to enhance human rights, gender equality, and judicial fairness across all Member States;

**WHEREAS**, the Parties acknowledge the efforts and initiatives already undertaken by Member States towards social and economic reforms and their alignment with the principles of the Canaan Confederation;

**WHEREAS**, recognizing the implementation of this Memorandum of Understanding as a foundational confidence-building measure, reflecting the shared commitment of all Member States to uphold the principles of justice, equality, and human dignity;

**WHEREAS**, the Parties recognize the enduring legacy of Prophet Muhammad as a progressive reformer, who introduced significant social, economic, and moral reforms to 7th-century Arabian society, emphasizing social justice, women's rights, economic fairness, and religious tolerance;

**WHEREAS**, inspired by the principles and reforms established by Prophet Muhammad, the Parties affirm their commitment to the ongoing struggle for human rights, advancing social justice, and ensuring dignity for all individuals, regardless of their gender, race, or religious beliefs;

**WHEREAS**, acknowledging the profound impact of these reforms on establishing a foundation for a more just society, the Parties commit to continuing this legacy by addressing contemporary challenges and promoting the advancement of human rights across the Canaan Confederation;

**The Parties hereby agree as follows:**

**Article 1: Commitment to Human Rights**

1.1 **Member States** commit to the ongoing struggle for human rights, seeking to align their legal and social practices with the highest possible standards of justice and dignity for all individuals.

1.2 **Member States** further commit to fostering a culture of respect, equality, and fairness, working collaboratively to address challenges and uphold the principles of human rights in all aspects of governance and society.

1.3 **Member States** recognize the importance of judicial fairness and transparency and commit to continuous improvement in their legal systems to reflect these values.

**Article 2: Implementation and Monitoring**

2.1 The Parties agree to establish a joint committee to monitor and review the progress of human rights advancements across Member States, providing recommendations and support as needed.

2.2 The joint committee shall include representatives from each Member State, the Partner, and independent human rights experts to ensure a balanced and transparent process.

**Article 3: Amendment and Termination**

This MOU may be amended or terminated by mutual consent of the Parties. Any amendments must be made in writing and signed by all Parties.

**Article 4: Legal Effect**

This MOU is a statement of intent and does not create legal obligations under international or domestic law.

**IN WITNESS WHEREOF**, the Parties hereto have executed this Memorandum of Understanding as of the date first above written.

**FOR THE MEMBER STATES OF THE CANAAN CONFEDERATION**

Signature:  
Name:  
Title:  
Date:

**FOR THE PARTNER**

Signature:  
Name:  
Title:  
Date:

# Appendix N: Towards Understanding and Reconciliation: France and the United Kingdom Reflect on the Sykes-Picot Agreement {#appendix-n:-towards-understanding-and-reconciliation:-france-and-the-united-kingdom-reflect-on-the-sykes-picot-agreement}

As we reflect upon the history of the Sykes-Picot Agreement, we, the Governments of France and the United Kingdom, take a moment to reflect on a chapter of our shared history that significantly shaped the course of the Middle East. In the midst of the uncertainties and tragedies of World War I, our predecessors, Sir Mark Sykes and François Georges-Picot, engaged in negotiations that led to the drawing of borders and the division of territories without the consent or consideration of the people who lived there. 

We recognize that the decisions made during those times have contributed to a century of conflict, division, and hardship for the peoples of the Middle East. The lines drawn on maps in European meeting rooms did not reflect the complex tapestries of culture, ethnicity, and faith that have existed in these lands for millennia. The legacy of those borders continues to influence the geopolitical and social landscape of the region today.

With humility and respect, we acknowledge the profound impact that the Sykes-Picot Agreement has had on the Middle East. We express our deep regret for the suffering and instability that have ensued from the actions taken by our governments a century ago. This acknowledgment is a step towards recognizing our past, understanding its effects on the present, and seeking a path forward that honors the dignity and aspirations of all peoples.

We are committed to engaging with the nations and peoples of the Middle East in a spirit of respect, partnership, and shared understanding. Our aim is to support initiatives that foster peace, stability, and prosperity in the region. This includes respecting the sovereignty and rights of Middle Eastern countries to shape their own future, free from external imposition or interference.

Looking to the future, France and the United Kingdom pledge to work collaboratively with international partners and the nations of the Middle East to address the challenges that remain. We believe that through dialogue, cooperation, and mutual respect, we can contribute to a more peaceful, just, and thriving Middle East.

In this spirit, we extend our sincerest hopes for reconciliation, and we reaffirm our commitment to a future defined by partnership and shared progress.

# Appendix O: Formal Apology for the Suez Crisis from the United Kingdom and France {#appendix-o:-formal-apology-for-the-suez-crisis-from-the-united-kingdom-and-france}

**Preamble:**  
Recognizing the profound impact of historical events on present-day relations and the importance of addressing past grievances to foster a future of peace and mutual understanding, the Governments of the United Kingdom and France hereby issue a formal apology for their roles in the Suez Crisis of 1956\.

**Acknowledgment of Actions:**  
We, the undersigned nations, acknowledge that the military intervention in Egypt during the Suez Crisis was a significant breach of international trust and norms. This intervention was not only a failure in terms of diplomatic relations but also a direct involvement that led to considerable suffering and instability in the region.

**Regret and Remorse:**  
The United Kingdom and France express deep regret for the hardships caused by our actions during the Suez Crisis. We are particularly mindful of the disruption to civilian lives and the undermining of national sovereignty in Egypt, which set back the course of regional peace and cooperation.

**Commitment to Peace and Cooperation:**  
As part of our ongoing commitment to fostering stability and peace in the Middle East, we pledge to support initiatives that promote dialogue, reconciliation, and cooperative development in the region. This includes active participation in the Canaan Confederation’s efforts to build and sustain an enduring peace framework.

**Future Assurance:**  
We affirm our dedication to upholding international laws and principles of sovereignty and non-interference. The lessons learned from the Suez Crisis inform our foreign policies today, ensuring that we support rather than undermine the aspirations of peoples and nations for self-determination and peaceful coexistence.

**Closing:**  
We offer this apology in the spirit of reconciliation and as a step toward healing the wounds of the past. Our nations are fully committed to working within the framework of the Canaan Confederation to build a future that honors our shared values of respect, justice, and mutual prosperity.

Signatories:

	•	\[Name\], \[Title\], on behalf of the United Kingdom  
	•	\[Name\], \[Title\], on behalf of the Republic of France

# Appendix P: Miscellaneous Initiatives for Lasting Peace in the Middle East[^13] {#appendix-p:-miscellaneous-initiatives-for-lasting-peace-in-the-middle-east}

In pursuit of lasting peace in the Middle East, we propose a series of specific initiatives designed to foster cooperation, build economic prosperity, and promote cultural understanding between Israel and Palestine. These initiatives are rooted in the belief that strategic partnerships and shared projects can significantly contribute to resolving longstanding conflicts and building a sustainable future.

1. **Iranian F-14 Deal: The United States proposes collaborating with Iran to restore F-14 Tomcat aircraft for airshows in exchange for targeted sanctions relief on spare parts for Iran’s commercial aviation sector, fostering mutual benefits and direct diplomatic engagement.**  
2. **Tripartite Water Resource Management Initiative**: We propose the creation of a collaborative effort between Israel, Palestine, and Jordan to develop shared water infrastructure, including desalination plants and wastewater treatment facilities. This initiative aims to address critical water shortages and promote cooperation over shared resources.  
3. **Tech for Peace Program**: This initiative will fund technology incubators that encourages Israeli and Palestinian tech entrepreneurs to collaborate on projects that address social challenges. Supported by global tech leaders and international funding, this program aims to reduce unemployment among the youth and foster a culture of innovation.  
4. **Abrahamic Cultural Heritage Festival**: An annual festival rotating among cities in Israel, Palestine, and neighboring countries would celebrate the region’s diverse cultural heritage, including art, music, food, and crafts. This festival would promote tourism, enhance mutual respect, and build economic ties through cultural exchange.  
5. **Health Bridges Initiative**: We propose a Canaan Confederation public health initiative to assist in the humantarian and disease risks following the destruction of healthcare infrastructure in the wake of the Israel-Hamas war.  
6. **Renewable Energy Partnerships**: To advance environmental sustainability, we advocate for the development of renewable energy projects along the borders of Israel and Palestine. These projects would not only provide green energy but also create jobs and serve as a model for environmental cooperation.  
7. **Educational Exchange and Scholarship Fund**: A scholarship fund supported by international partners would enable students from both nations to study abroad and bring their expertise back home. This initiative aims to build local capacity and foster global academic networks.  
8. **Women's Leadership Forum**: This forum would empower women leaders from both communities to spearhead initiatives focused on women’s empowerment and community development, supported by global organizations like UN Women.  
9. **Infrastructure for Peace Project**: Major infrastructure projects in Palestine, funded by The Canaan Confederation Waqf, would boost the local economy and improve living conditions. These projects would prioritize local labor and materials to maximize economic benefits.  
10. **Legal Reform Workshops**: Workshops with international legal experts would help strengthen the judicial systems in the region, focusing on reforms that enhance transparency, fairness, and accessibility.  
11. **Interfaith Dialogue Series**: Regular dialogues facilitated by Jewish, Muslim, and Christian leaders would address religious tensions and promote understanding. Supported by the Vatican and other religious institutions, these dialogues would aim to reconcile differences and build a foundation for peace.

These initiatives represent a comprehensive approach to addressing the complex dynamics of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict through collaborative and constructive efforts. Each is designed to address specific areas of need, from environmental sustainability to cultural exchange and from legal reform to educational opportunities, illustrating a roadmap towards a peaceful and prosperous future.

# Appendix Q: Draft 30-Year Hudna Agreement[^14] {#appendix-q:-draft-30-year-hudna-agreement}

Preamble:  
This agreement is made on \[Date\] between the following parties:

* The State of Israel  
* The Palestinian Authority  
* \[Other Palestinian Factions, e.g., Hamas, Islamic Jihad, etc.\]  
* Hezbollah  
* Republic of Lebanon  
* The Islamic Republic of Iran  
* The Canaan Confederation (as the overseeing body)

Recognizing the need for a durable peace and stability in the region, and with a commitment to the welfare of all peoples in the area, the parties agree to a 30-year Hudna (ceasefire) based on the following terms and conditions.

Article I: Objectives of the Hudna

1. To cease major hostilities between the signing parties.  
2. To create a stable and peaceful environment conducive to the rebuilding and development of the region.  
3. To facilitate the implementation of the broader Peace Plan, including the establishment of a viable Palestinian State and the security of the State of Israel.  
4. To provide an explicit mechanism to reestablishing peace when conflict i the Middle East inevitably breaks out.

Article II: Terms and Conditions

1. Cessation of Hostilities:  
   * All parties agree to an immediate and comprehensive cessation of all military actions, including but not limited to, rocket attacks, airstrikes, and ground operations.  
   * Any violations of the ceasefire will be subject to immediate investigation and appropriate mediation as determined by members of the Canaan Confederation.  
2. Demilitarization:  
   * Specific areas, particularly Gaza, will undergo a phased demilitarization process overseen by Confederation peacekeeping forces.  
   * Weapons caches and military infrastructure identified within these areas will be dismantled under international supervision.  
3. Humanitarian Access:  
   * Unimpeded humanitarian access will be granted to all affected areas to provide essential services, including medical aid, food, and water.  
   * Reconstruction efforts will be coordinated by the Canaan Confederation in collaboration with local authorities and international agencies.  
4. Prisoner Exchange:  
   * All parties agree to a negotiated prisoner exchange as a goodwill gesture to build trust and foster reconciliation.  
   * Detailed terms of the exchange will be determined by a joint committee established by the signatories.

Article III: Monitoring and Compliance

1. Establishment of Monitoring Mechanism:  
   * A dedicated monitoring body will be established under the auspices of the Canaan Confederation to oversee compliance with the Hudna.  
   * This body will include representatives from each signing party, international observers, and neutral experts.  
2. Reporting and Accountability:  
   * Regular reports will be submitted by the monitoring body to all signatories, detailing compliance and any violations of the ceasefire.  
   * Mechanisms for accountability and resolution of disputes will be in place, including mediation and arbitration processes facilitated by the Canaan Confederation.

Article IV: Duration and Renewal

1. Initial Term:  
   * This Hudna will be in effect for an initial period of 30 years from the date of signing.  
   * The signatories agree to maintain this overall security architecture for at least the duration of the Hudna.  
2. Renewal and Extension:  
   * A periodic 10-year review will be conducted to assess its effectiveness and discuss potential renewal or extension.  
   * Renewal terms will be negotiated based on the prevailing conditions and the progress made toward peace and stability.

Article V: Final Provisions

1. Amendments:  
   * Any amendments to this agreement must be made in writing and agreed upon by all signatories.  
2. Dispute Resolution:  
   * Any disputes arising from the interpretation or implementation of this agreement will be resolved through mediation and arbitration under the auspices of the Canaan Confederation.  
3. Signatories:  
   * This agreement is binding upon the undersigned parties and their respective successors and representatives.

Signatures:  
\[Representative from the State of Israel\]  
\[Representative from the Palestinian Authority\]  
\[Representative from Hamas\]  
\[Representative from Islamic Jihad\]  
\[Representative from the Canaan Confederation\]

\[International Observers\]

Witnesses:  
\[Witness 1\]  
\[Witness 2\]

\[Witness 3\]

**Resolution Number: \[Insert Resolution Number\]**

**Subject: Immediate Deployment of Canaan Confederation Peacekeepers to the Rafah Border Crossing**

The Security Council,  
Recalling all its previous resolutions on the Israeli-Palestinian conflict,  
Reaffirming the principles of the Charter of the United Nations,  
Expressing deep concern over the ongoing humanitarian crisis in Gaza,  
Noting the recent ruling of the International Court of Justice (ICJ) on provisional measures for Israel,  
Recognizing the urgent need for humanitarian assistance and the protection of civilians,

**Acting under Chapter VII of the Charter of the United Nations,**

**1\. Calls for the immediate deployment of Canaan Confederation Peacekeepers to the Rafah border crossing to ensure the safe and unhindered provision of humanitarian aid to Gaza, in line with the ICJ ruling;**

**2\. Requests** that all Member States, in cooperation with the United Nations, support the deployment and operation of these peacekeepers to facilitate the opening of land crossings and the delivery of essential services, including food, water, electricity, fuel, shelter, medical supplies, and care;\*\*

**3\. Urges** the Government of Israel to comply fully with the ICJ's provisional measures, including increasing the capacity and number of land crossing points and maintaining them open as long as necessary;\*\*

**4\. Calls upon** Hamas and all other relevant actors to ensure the safety and security of humanitarian personnel and to cooperate fully with the peacekeeping forces;\*\*

**5\. Requests** the Secretary-General to report on the implementation of this resolution within 30 days and to provide regular updates thereafter;\*\*

**6\. Decides** to remain seized of the matter.

# Appendix S: Draft Proposal for the Advisory Role of the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers in the Rebuilding of Gaza under the Auspices of the Canaan Confederation {#appendix-s:-draft-proposal-for-the-advisory-role-of-the-u.s.-army-corps-of-engineers-in-the-rebuilding-of-gaza-under-the-auspices-of-the-canaan-confederation}

**Executive Summary**

This proposal outlines the strategic involvement of the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers (USACE) in the comprehensive rebuilding of the Gaza Strip, framed within the governance of the newly proposed Canaan Confederation. This initiative, following a successful deployment of multinational peacekeeping forces and a significant reduction in regional hostilities as outlined by the Hudna, positions the USACE to lend its expertise in engineering, construction project management, and unexploded ordnance (UXO) clearance in an advisory capacity. Crucially, this proposal plans for the transition of operational responsibilities to Turkey and the Arab nations within the Confederation, ensuring local leadership and labor in the reconstruction efforts, with no American personnel on the ground.

**Objectives** The objectives of this initiative are to provide expert advisory engineering and construction services for rebuilding essential infrastructure in the Gaza Strip, neutralize UXO threats to ensure safety throughout the reconstruction process, align projects with the sustainable and long-term development goals of the Canaan Confederation, and foster local capacity building and economic development through collaborative projects.

**Preconditions** The implementation of this proposal depends on securing a significant decrease in hostilities, guaranteed by the effective deployment and operation of peacekeeping forces, obtaining approval and support from both local governing bodies and international stakeholders, and ensuring adequate funding from diverse sources including the Confederation Waqf.

**Scope of Work**  
The advisory scope includes planning and oversight in constructing roads, bridges, water systems, electrical grids, and medical and educational facilities. The USACE will also guide environmental projects and humanitarian constructions, involving community centers and housing.

**Integration of UXO Clearance**  
A comprehensive UXO clearance strategy will be developed, with the USACE providing technological assessments and training for local teams, ensuring safety and effectiveness.

**Phases of Deployment**

1. **Preparation and Initial Response:** Advisory on security and coordination with peacekeeping forces, guiding initial debris and UXO clearance.  
2. **Infrastructure and Environmental Stabilization:** Advisory on critical infrastructure projects and ongoing UXO operations.  
3. **Reconstruction and Development Handover:** Gradual transfer of responsibilities to Arab nations of the Confederation, including training and capacity building.  
4. **Evaluation and Long-Term Partnership:** Assess reconstruction efforts and establish sustained international support and collaboration.

**Budget and Funding** The budgeting process will be significantly supported by the Confederation Waqf, a financial institution designed to manage and allocate funds for projects that benefit the member states and their populations. This innovative funding mechanism will be central to sustaining the financial needs of the reconstruction effort. Additional funding will be sought through international aid, government grants, and strategic partnerships with global financial institutions, ensuring a diversified funding base to support the extensive scope of work.

**Conclusion** This proposal ensures that the USACE's involvement provides essential advisory services to address reconstruction needs effectively while integrating UXO clearance for safety. The strategic handover to local and regional authorities supports the goal of a resilient, self-sustaining Gaza Strip, benefiting from local expertise and international support in line with the goals of the Canaan Confederation.

# Appendix T: Draft Canaan Confederation Educational Framework of Jewish and Muslim Interactions in Early Arabia {#appendix-t:-draft-canaan-confederation-educational-framework-of-jewish-and-muslim-interactions-in-early-arabia}

The early interactions between Muslim and Jewish communities in Arabia during the time of Prophet Muhammad encapsulate a mix of cooperation and conflict. These interactions began with the Constitution of Medina, an early attempt at creating a pluralistic society where diverse groups, including Jewish tribes, could coexist under shared legal and social frameworks. This period highlights the potential for different communities to unite under mutual interests and common laws.

However, the relationships were strained, leading to several conflicts attributed to political and security concerns within the growing but nascent Muslim state. These conflicts, involving allegations of treaty violations and subsequent actions like the expulsion of Jewish tribes from Medina and later from Khaybar during Caliph Umar’s rule, reflect the complexities faced by a new religiously defined nation-state in maintaining internal security and religio-political authority.

**Drawing Analogies with the Israeli-Palestinian Conflict**

The historical narrative of early Jewish-Muslim relations in Arabia offers valuable analogies for the Israeli-Palestinian conflict. Both scenarios involve intertwined religious and political identities, territorial disputes, and issues of governance and security. Just as the early Muslim community faced initial challenges in integrating diverse groups, modern efforts in Israel and Palestine grapple with creating a peaceful coexistence amidst a backdrop of historical grievances and mutual distrust.

**Emphasizing Diplomatic Engagement and Shared Governance**

Recognizing these historical complexities is essential as we seek pathways to peace between Israelis and Palestinians. The Covenants of Muhammad serves as a poignant reminder of the possibilities for creating stable governance structures that respect and protect the rights of all communities. By drawing lessons from these early attempts at conflict resolution and community building, our current peace efforts can be informed by the understanding that sustainable peace requires accommodating diverse narratives and ensuring fair governance.

**Conclusion: Learning from History for Future Peace**

As we reflect on the historical interactions between Jews and Muslims in Arabia, and their parallels with the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, it becomes evident that both past and present conflicts, while deeply rooted in specific contexts, offer universal lessons on the need for diplomatic engagement and the challenges of building a shared society. Our peace plan, epitomized by the new Covenant for Al-Aqsa Mosque and Temple Mount, aims to establish a new framework for mutual respect, secure governance, and long-term stability, echoing the need to fundamentally reset the Status quo of Jewish-Muslim relations for the sake of peace and stability.

# Appendix U: Draft Framework for U.S.-Palestine Olive Oil Trade Agreement Under the Auspices of the Canaan Confederation {#appendix-u:-draft-framework-for-u.s.-palestine-olive-oil-trade-agreement-under-the-auspices-of-the-canaan-confederation}

**Preamble**

* Acknowledge the mutual benefits of trade in agricultural products, specifically olive oil, between the United States of America and the State of Palestine, under the auspices of the Canaan Confederation.  
* Recognize the importance of olive oil as a key agricultural export for Palestine and a valued import for the United States.  
* Affirm the role of the Canaan Confederation in facilitating, overseeing, and providing peacekeeping protection for this trade as a crucial part of the Palestinian economy.

**Article 1: Objectives**

* Strengthen bilateral trade relationships and promote economic development in Palestine through enhanced access to the U.S. market.  
* Ensure a stable supply of high-quality olive oil for the U.S. market.  
* Utilize the support, oversight, and peacekeeping protection of the Canaan Confederation to ensure the longevity and security of this trade agreement.

**Article 2: Tariff Reductions**

* The United States agrees to reduce tariffs on imported Palestinian olive oil incrementally over a period of five years, leading to complete elimination of tariffs at the end of this period.  
* Palestine agrees to adhere to the quality and health standards as required by U.S. regulations to maintain eligibility for tariff reductions.

**Article 3: Quality Control and Standards**

* Palestine must ensure that all olive oil exports meet U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) standards for import.  
* Both parties agree to cooperate on technical assistance to help Palestinian producers meet these standards, with coordination and additional support from the Canaan Confederation.

**Article 4: Trade Promotion and Support**

* The U.S. will provide technical and financial assistance to Palestinian olive oil producers to upgrade their production capabilities, focusing on sustainable agricultural practices and quality improvement.  
* Joint trade missions and business exchange programs will be organized annually to promote U.S.-Palestine business relationships in the agricultural sector, facilitated by the Canaan Confederation.

**Article 5: Geotechnical Investment and Water Management**

* Both parties commit to investing in geotechnical projects aimed at increasing the amount of fertile land available for olive cultivation and improving water usage efficiency.  
* Projects will include advanced irrigation techniques, soil fertility enhancement programs, and sustainable land management practices.  
* The Canaan Confederation will oversee and provide support for these initiatives, ensuring they align with broader environmental and economic goals.

**Article 6: Peacekeeping Support**

* The Canaan Confederation will provide peacekeeping forces to ensure the safety and stability of the olive oil production areas within Palestine.  
* These forces will assist in protecting the infrastructure and workers involved in the olive oil industry, mitigating any disruptions that could affect trade.

**Article 7: Dispute Resolution**

* Any disputes arising from this agreement shall be resolved through bilateral negotiations under the mediation of the Canaan Confederation.  
* If unresolved through negotiation, disputes will be referred to an agreed upon international arbitration entity.

**Article 8: Amendments**

* This agreement may be amended by mutual consent of the parties, with consultation and approval from the Canaan Confederation. Proposed amendments must be submitted in writing and approved by all parties.

**Article 9: Entry into Force and Termination**

* This agreement shall enter into force upon ratification by the appropriate governmental bodies of both nations and formal endorsement by the Canaan Confederation.  
* Either party may terminate this agreement upon six months’ written notice to the other party, with a copy to the Canaan Confederation.

**Signatories**

* \[Designated Official, United States of America\]  
* \[Designated Official, State of Palestine\]  
* \[Representative, Canaan Confederation\]

**Date**

* \[Date of Signing\]

# Appendix V: Compact of Free Association Between the United States and the State of Palestine \- A Stability Plan {#appendix-v:-compact-of-free-association-between-the-united-states-and-the-state-of-palestine---a-stability-plan}

This appendix outlines a strategic proposal for a Compact of Free Association (COFA) between the State of Palestine and the United States as part of the Canaan Confederation framework. This initiative is intended not only as a fallback should the primary objectives of the Confederation not be fully realized, but also as a significant effort to stabilize the region, provide justice and compensation for the Nakba, and amend America's historical role in Middle Eastern conflicts.

**Objective and Rationale:**  
The COFA is designed to foster a robust relationship between the United States and Palestine, emphasizing stability, security, and economic development, while affirming Palestine's political sovereignty. This agreement aims to repair America's moral standing in the Middle East by directly addressing the historical grievances of the Palestinian people and promoting a positive precedent for U.S. involvement in the region.

**Legal and Diplomatic Framework:**  
Under the COFA, Palestine would remain a sovereign entity with the United States providing economic aid, defense support, and assistance in international diplomacy. This support would respect Palestinian governance structures while ensuring security guarantees against external and internal threats.

**Economic and Infrastructure Support:**  
The United States would commit to substantial economic assistance to develop Palestine’s infrastructure, educational systems, healthcare services, and cultural projects, such as the House of Wisdom in the Virtuous City of Gaza. This initiative aims to compensate the Palestinian people for losses incurred during the Nakba and subsequent conflicts, facilitating a transformative recovery and sustainable development.

**Security Arrangements:**  
The U.S. would offer comprehensive defense support, including military training and equipment, to help Palestine secure its borders and maintain peace. These security arrangements would also include guarantees against aggression from neighboring states, particularly focusing on safeguarding the integrity and independence of Palestine.

**Cultural and Educational Integration:**  
Reforms in education would align Palestinian curricula with international standards, promoting values of tolerance, democracy, and human rights. Legal and policy advisors from the U.S. would assist in crafting laws that encourage economic growth, protect civil liberties, and promote effective governance.

**Sovereignty and Governance:**  
While retaining full sovereignty, Palestine would consult with the United States on issues impacting regional stability and international relations, ensuring a collaborative approach to foreign policy and security matters.

**Financial Arrangements:**  
A structured financial assistance package would be provided annually, adjusted for inflation, supporting the Palestinian government’s budget and special projects aimed at economic and infrastructure development.

**Duration and Review:**  
The COFA would be enacted initially for a 30-year period with reviews every five years to adapt the terms according to the evolving geopolitical landscape and the progress towards the set objectives of peace, stability, and development.

**Termination and Succession:**  
Provisions for renegotiation or termination would be included, allowing both parties to adapt to changes and ensure the agreement remains beneficial and relevant.

**Conclusion:**  
This Compact of Free Association is envisioned as a pragmatic and respectful partnership that addresses the historical injustices faced by the Palestinian people and sets a precedent for positive U.S. engagement in the Middle East. It underscores America’s commitment to fostering a stable, prosperous, and secure future for Palestine, reflecting a critical step towards healing and reconciliation in the region.

# Appendix W: Estimating Total Amount of Occupied Land Using OSINT {#appendix-w:-estimating-total-amount-of-occupied-land-using-osint}

**Purpose**

This appendix outlines the methodology and tools used to estimate the total land occupied by Israel, utilizing Open Source Intelligence (OSINT). This estimate supports the land lease scheme proposed in the peace plan.

Methodology  
	1\.	Data Collection  
	•	Sources:  
	•	Satellite imagery from Sentinel Hub, NASA, and Google Earth.  
	•	Maps from OpenStreetMap and historical GIS databases.  
	•	Reports and documents from the United Nations and other relevant international organizations.  
	•	Criteria for Selection:  
	•	Recency and relevance of data.  
	•	Public accessibility and credibility of the source.  
	•	Geographic coverage encompassing Israel, the West Bank, East Jerusalem, and the Golan Heights.  
	2\.	Data Analysis Using GIS Tools  
	•	GIS Software: Utilization of QGIS and ArcGIS for spatial analysis.  
	•	Processes:  
	•	Importation of maps and satellite images into GIS software.  
	•	Delineation of recognized international boundaries and occupied territories using layers and shapefiles.  
	•	Calculation of total area within delineated boundaries using polygon area calculation features in GIS.  
	3\.	Verification and Accuracy Enhancement  
	•	Cross-referencing: Comparing GIS results with historical data and other sources.  
	•	Consistency Checks: Using multiple data sets and imagery sources to validate findings.  
	4\.	Reporting  
	•	Mapping: Production of detailed maps highlighting the occupied areas.  
	•	Detailed Findings: A report documenting the methodology, sources, calculations, and conclusions.  
Tools and Resources  
	•	GIS Software:  
	•	QGIS: Open-source geographic information system.  
	•	ArcGIS: Comprehensive suite for map creation and spatial analysis.  
	•	Imagery and Maps:  
	•	Google Earth: For satellite imagery and global mapping.  
	•	Sentinel Hub: For access to multi-temporal satellite imagery.  
	•	OpenStreetMap: For detailed and community-updated maps.  
	•	Documentation:  
	•	United Nations documentation for legal and recognized boundaries.  
	•	Reports from international observatories and research institutions on land use and settlement expansion.  
Considerations  
	•	Disputed Territories: Analysis includes areas under dispute and zones affected by conflicts and settlements.  
	•	Dynamic Boundaries: Acknowledgment of the fluid nature of boundaries due to ongoing political changes and settlement expansions.  
	•	Ethical Use of Data: Ensuring that data usage complies with open-source licenses and respects privacy and security concerns.  
Conclusion  
The estimation of occupied land using OSINT provides a scientifically robust basis for addressing land lease issues in the peace plan. This appendix supports the transparent, accountable, and systematic approach to land allocation and management proposed in the broader framework of conflict resolution and regional stability.

# Appendix X: Deployment of Canaan Confederation Peacekeepers in the Jordanian Valley to Prevent Smuggling Activities by Foreign Actors {#appendix-x:-deployment-of-canaan-confederation-peacekeepers-in-the-jordanian-valley-to-prevent-smuggling-activities-by-foreign-actors}

**The Security Council,**

*Recalling* all previous resolutions concerning the region, including Resolutions on the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, and the mandates for UN peacekeeping operations,

*Noting* the ongoing challenges related to smuggling activities by foreign actors in the Jordanian Valley, which threaten regional stability and security,

*Acknowledging* the request by the Jordanian government for international support to combat these challenges,

*Recognizing* the Canaan Confederation as a capable and neutral force that can aid in maintaining security and stability in the region,

1. **Authorizes** the deployment of the Canaan Confederation Peacekeeping Forces to the Jordanian Valley, under the Chapter VII of the United Nations Charter, to prevent smuggling activities by foreign actors;  
2. **Decides** that the deployment will be for an initial period of twelve months, to be reviewed and extended as needed based on a report by the Secretary-General regarding the situation on the ground;  
3. **Urges** all parties to cooperate fully with the Canaan Confederation Peacekeeping Forces and to ensure their safety and freedom of movement;  
4. **Calls upon** member states to provide logistical, technical, and financial support to the Canaan Confederation Peacekeeping Forces to enable them to fulfill their mandate effectively;  
5. **Demands** that all forms of smuggling of weapons, drugs, and human trafficking across the Jordanian Valley cease immediately, and that all parties refrain from any action that may further destabilize the situation;  
6. **Encourages** the Canaan Confederation to engage in dialogues with local communities to ensure that the peacekeeping efforts are sensitive to the cultural and social dynamics of the region;  
7. **Requests** the Secretary-General to report to the Council every three months on the implementation of this resolution, including progress on the peacekeeping mission and the status of smuggling activities in the Jordanian Valley;  
8. **Decides** to remain actively seized of the matter.

# Appendix Z: Phased Deployment of Canaan Confederation Peacekeepers to the Gaza Strip for Hostile Population Disengagement {#appendix-z:-phased-deployment-of-canaan-confederation-peacekeepers-to-the-gaza-strip-for-hostile-population-disengagement}

# Appendix AA: A Spectulative Interpretation of the Death of the Prophet Muhammad {#appendix-aa:-a-spectulative-interpretation-of-the-death-of-the-prophet-muhammad}

## ⚠️⚠️Disclaimer⚠️⚠️ {#⚠️⚠️disclaimer⚠️⚠️-1}

**Disclaimer:** *The following interpretation is provided by an infidel author offering an independent perspective on the historical events described. It is important to note that this analysis is speculative, based on historical inference and interpretation of the available sources.*

The death of the Prophet Muhammad and the immediate fatality of his companion, Bishr ibn al-Bara’, following a poisoning incident at Khaybar, present complex scenarios analyzed through various potential poisons. After the Battle of Khaybar, the Prophet and his companions were served poisoned meat by a Jewish woman named Zaynab bint Al-Harith. While the Prophet Muhammad survived the initial poisoning and suffered long-term effects, he later remarked, "O Aisha\! I still feel the pain caused by the food I ate at Khaybar, and at this time, I feel as if my aorta is being cut from that poison" (Sahih Bukhari, Volume 5, Book 59, Hadith 713). Bishr ibn al-Bara’, however, died shortly after consuming the poisoned meat, indicating the use of a highly toxic substance.

**Analysis of Possible Poisons:**

1. **Aconite (Wolfsbane)** and **Hemlock** were considered due to their historical availability and the immediate and severe symptoms they can cause. Both are capable of causing rapid death but are less commonly associated with long-term effects. While they could explain the quick demise of Bishr ibn al-Bara’, they do not fit well with the prolonged suffering reported by the Prophet Muhammad.  
2. **Arsenic** emerges as the most likely candidate by process of elimination. Arsenic was well-known to the ancient Greeks, Romans, and Egyptians for its ability to cause both acute and chronic poisoning. Given the extensive trade routes and cultural exchanges between these civilizations and the Arabian Peninsula, it is highly likely that knowledge of arsenic and its uses as a poison was present in 7th-century Arabia. Arsenic's effects align with the severe gastrointestinal distress and potential death within hours or days, as well as long-term suffering if consumed in a smaller dose. Its capacity to cause prolonged health issues even after surviving the initial acute poisoning phase makes it a plausible explanation for the symptoms described by the Prophet. However, this interpretation remains speculative, as the historical sources do not provide direct evidence of arsenic being the specific poison used.  
3. **Native Arabian Poisons:** It is also possible that a locally sourced or native poison from the Arabian Peninsula was used in the incident. The Arabian Peninsula had a variety of toxic plants and potentially venomous animals whose toxins could be used as poisons. For instance:  
   1. **Toxic Plants:** Certain plants native to the region, possibly from the *Solanaceae* family (which includes nightshades), could contain lethal compounds. These could have been known to local healers or communities.  
   2. **Animal Toxins:** Venom from snakes or scorpions, while typically associated with bites or stings, could also have been harnessed deliberately as a poison.  
   3. **Herbal Concoctions:** Traditional Arabian medicine involved the use of various herbs, some of which might have been toxic if used improperly or intentionally for harm.

While arsenic is still the most likely candidate due to its well-documented effects and historical use, the possibility of a native poison being used cannot be discounted, especially considering the local knowledge and resources available at the time. However, this possibility also remains speculative, as there is no direct evidence pointing to a specific native poison being used in this context.

**Ethical Dimensions of this Analysis:**

1. **Respect for Religious Beliefs:** This analysis is conducted with respect for the religious significance of the events surrounding the Prophet Muhammad. The aim is to approach the subject with sensitivity, using neutral language to avoid offending religious beliefs.  
2. **Cultural and Historical Context:** The interpretation acknowledges the importance of understanding these events within their historical and cultural contexts, avoiding the imposition of modern values on historical figures and events.  
3. **Ethical Responsibility of the Interpreter:** The analysis is transparent about its speculative nature and the perspective of the interpreter. The goal is to maintain academic integrity while respecting the subject matter.  
4. **Relevance to Contemporary Discourse:** This interpretation is included as part of a broader peace plan, specifically due to the use of this story in the rhetoric of Amin al-Husseini, the first leader of the Palestinian national movement. The intent is to openly illuminate and address historical narratives that have fueled tensions.  
5. **Commitment to Truth and Integrity:** This peace plan is committed to truth and integrity. We believe that addressing historical narratives honestly, even when they are complex and sensitive, is crucial for understanding the conflict and fostering reconciliation.

**Conclusion:**

Given the widespread knowledge of arsenic among the Greeks, Romans, and Egyptians, and the likelihood that this knowledge reached 7th-century Arabia through trade and cultural exchanges, arsenic is identified as the most likely poison involved in this historical episode. Aconite and hemlock, while possible candidates, are less likely to account for both the immediate and prolonged symptoms described in the Islamic texts. The potential use of a native Arabian poison adds another layer of complexity, but arsenic's known properties and historical prevalence make it the strongest contender. However, it is crucial to acknowledge that this analysis is speculative, relying on historical inference and interpretation of sources that do not provide definitive proof of the specific poison used.
